### M110: the `findLiveRoutePenalty` route-level live-entry lookup — sole "return entry iff active penalty" helper at the route scope, consumed by `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth` and `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`, with four pre-existing pins (empty map, expired-at-boundary, live, composite-idempotent) asserting only on return-value shape via deepEqual/equal but three orthogonal drift surfaces (reference identity, read-only expired-hit, multi-segment non-prefixed wrap) left unpinned `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findLiveRoutePenalty` is the route-level twin of M104's `findLiveProviderPenalty`. It serves two readers — `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth` (`provider.models` hook that hides route-penalized models from opencode's map) and `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` (the `list_curated_models` tool reader that surfaces route-scope blocks). Four pre-existing pins cover the M70 boundary cases (empty map, expired-at-exact-boundary, live entry, composite-idempotent input) but they all assert exclusively on return-value shape via `deepEqual` / `equal`. They do NOT assert HOW the return value is produced or the map state after the call. Three orthogonal surfaces remain unpinned: (1) **Return-by-reference identity.** The live path returns the exact `ModelRouteHealth` object that the writer installed. `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` captures the reference at tool-call time so a later retry-count bump via `buildRouteHealthEntry` is visible through the same handle. A `{...routeHealth}` spread for "safety" would break reference equality while still passing every `deepEqual` pin. Parallel twin of the M104 provider-level surface. (2) **Read-only on expired hit.** The `!routeHealth || routeHealth.until <= now` short-circuit returns `null` and leaves the map untouched. Deletion is `expireHealthMaps`' job, not findLive's. A "helpful" cleanup-on-read regression would reset the retry-count escalation ladder mid-turn whenever an unrelated caller probed an expired entry. (3) **Multi-segment non-prefixed model is wrapped, not passed through.** The composite-idempotence pin #4 uses `{provider: "ollama-cloud", model: "ollama-cloud/glm-5"}` — prefix already matches. The inverse case — openrouter aggregator routes like `{provider: "openrouter", model: "anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet"}` where the model contains `/` but the leading segment is NOT the provider ID — is unpinned. A plausible `if (model.includes("/")) return model;` simplification of `composeRouteKey` would silently skip the wrap and miss the stored `"openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet"` key. `classifyPersistedHealthKey`'s docstring explicitly flags this class of refactor.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every `provider.models` hook invocation and every `list_curated_models` tool call — one probe per (provider, model) pair. Silent mis-classifications at this boundary directly shift which routes opencode is offered and which appear as "blocked" to the agent.
- **Fix**: appended ~65-line "Drift surfaces (M110 PDD)" section to the existing docstring, enumerating the three surfaces with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — the `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers` delegate, the combined expiry short-circuit, and the `return routeHealth` on live-hit are preserved exactly.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins after the fourth M70 boundary pin, inserted directly before `findLiveProviderPenalty_whenMapEmpty_returnsNull` so the route-level drift surfaces group together. Pin A (`_whenEntryLive_returnsTheInsertedObjectByReferenceIdentity`) constructs an `insertedEntry`, installs it, and asserts `result === insertedEntry` — `node:assert/strict`'s `assert.equal` is `===`, so a `{...spread}` regression fails. Pin B (`_whenEntryExpired_leavesMapUntouched`) asserts map size remains 1 and the expired entry is still retrievable under its composite key after the null return. Pin C (`_whenMultiSegmentModelWithoutMatchingPrefix_wrapsIntoCompositeKey`) uses the openrouter aggregator case — `provider="openrouter"`, `model="anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet"`, stored key `"openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet"` — and asserts the entry is found.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated NEW pin among the M110 additions. Sabotage 1 (`return { ...routeHealth };` defensive spread): `(fail) findLiveRoutePenalty_whenEntryLive_returnsTheInsertedObjectByReferenceIdentity` alone fired — pre-existing deepEqual pin #3 passed because the spread is structurally equal. Sabotage 2 (`if (routeHealth.until <= now) { modelRouteHealthMap.delete(...); return null; }` cleanup-on-read): `(fail) findLiveRoutePenalty_whenEntryExpired_leavesMapUntouched` alone fired — pre-existing pin #2 passed because the null return is unchanged. Among new M110 pins only pin C fired; the pre-existing collateral is additive coverage, which the asymmetric partition rule allows. Restored the fix, **334/334 pass** (331 pre-M110 + 3 new unit pins).
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (appended ~65-line drift-surface section to the existing `findLiveRoutePenalty` docstring — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (three new unit pins inserted directly before `findLiveProviderPenalty_whenMapEmpty_returnsNull`; `findLiveRoutePenalty` import already present).

### M109: the `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` zero-token quota classifier — central per-call zero-token detector consumed by the `assistant.message.completed` event narrower, with eight pre-existing pins covering top-level sibling counters and nested walker happy paths but three JavaScript-specific foot-guns (nested null, top-level NaN, nested non-numeric field) left silently unguarded `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` is the sole classifier that decides whether an `assistant.message.completed` event — with its tokens record extracted by `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` — constitutes a zero-token quota signal and therefore triggers a route-level penalty via `buildRouteHealthEntry`. Eight pre-existing pins cover the input/output zero check, the top-level sibling non-zero bail, and the nested walker detecting a single nested non-zero number, but three JavaScript-specific surfaces remain unpinned: (1) **Nested null is filtered out by the `value && typeof value === "object"` null guard.** `typeof null === "object"` in JavaScript; without the truthy guard the walker would attempt `Object.values(null)` and throw. A "simplification" that drops the `value &&` prefix (a common refactor when someone reads it as redundant) would crash the plugin on any tokens payload with a `cache: null` field. (2) **Top-level NaN counter is conservatively allowed — `NaN !== 0 === true` foot-gun.** The top-level non-zero bail is `if (value !== 0) return false;`. Because `NaN !== 0` is `true`, a `reasoning: NaN` counter immediately bails out of the zero-token classification — the safe conservative direction. A defensive refactor to `if (Number.isFinite(value) && value !== 0) return false;` would silently treat NaN as "not non-zero" and let the classifier flip to `true`, triggering spurious quota penalties on any upstream NaN counter. (3) **Nested non-numeric field is ignored, not rejected.** The nested walker's predicate `if (typeof nestedValue === "number" && nestedValue !== 0)` skips anything that is not a number (string, boolean, nested object, null). A refactor that inverts the predicate to `if (typeof nestedValue !== "number" || nestedValue !== 0) return false;` would reject any tokens payload whose nested object holds descriptive string fields like `cache: { backend: "redis", read: 0, write: 0 }`, returning `false` from the classifier and silently suppressing legitimate zero-token quota penalties on that payload shape.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every assistant message completion event — `handleAssistantMessageCompleted` invokes the classifier once per event and routes through `buildRouteHealthEntry` when it returns `true`. Silent mis-classifications at this boundary directly shift the health map.
- **Fix**: extended the existing docstring with a ~55-line "Drift surfaces (M109 PDD)" section enumerating the three foot-guns with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — the `value && typeof value === "object"` null guard, the `value !== 0` NaN-conservative bail, and the `typeof nestedValue === "number" && nestedValue !== 0` non-numeric tolerance are preserved exactly.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins after `_whenTopLevelSiblingCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse`, orthogonal to the eight pre-existing pins. Pin A (`_whenNestedFieldIsNull_returnsTrueWithoutThrowing`) passes `{input: 0, output: 0, cache: null}`, asserts `true` — a null-guard drop would throw on `Object.values(null)`. Pin B (`_whenTopLevelCounterIsNaN_returnsFalse`) passes `{input: 0, output: 0, reasoning: Number.NaN}`, asserts `false` — any `Number.isFinite` defensive refactor would flip it to `true`. Pin C (`_whenNestedFieldIsNonNumericString_returnsTrue`) passes `{input: 0, output: 0, cache: {backend: "redis", read: 0, write: 0}}`, asserts `true` — any inverted-predicate refactor would return `false`.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric NEW pin. Sabotage 1 (drop `value &&` from null guard): `(fail) isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenNestedFieldIsNull_returnsTrueWithoutThrowing` alone fired. Sabotage 2 (add `Number.isFinite(value) &&` to top-level bail): `(fail) isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenTopLevelCounterIsNaN_returnsFalse` alone fired. Sabotage 3 (invert nested walker predicate to `typeof !== "number" || !== 0`): `(fail) isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenNestedFieldIsNonNumericString_returnsTrue` alone fired. Exactly the asymmetric partition. Restored the fix, **331/331 pass** (328 pre-M109 + 3 new unit pins).
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (appended ~55-line drift-surface section to the existing `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` docstring — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (three new unit pins inserted after `_whenTopLevelSiblingCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse`).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` rebuild is purely for test/build hygiene since production behavior at HEAD is bitwise-identical.

### M108: the `parsePersistedHealthEntry` disk-schema validator — sole input-validation boundary between the persisted health JSON file and the in-memory `ProviderHealth` / `ModelRouteHealth` maps — had eight pre-existing pins covering happy path + corrupt-field cases but three input-validation boundaries (exact `until === now`, negative retryCount, non-finite retryCount) were silently unguarded `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `parsePersistedHealthEntry` at lines ~307–397 is the sole input-validation gate between the persisted `.plugin-state.json` health file and the in-memory `providerHealthMap` / `modelRouteHealthMap`. Eight pre-existing pins cover the happy path, the `"never"` literal normalization, null raw entry, unknown state string, corrupt-string until, NaN until, past until, and missing retryCount — solid breadth across the `state` and `until` branches plus one `retryCount` null-check — but three input-validation boundaries have zero direct coverage: (1) **`until === now` exact boundary.** The expiry check is `if (until <= now) return null;` and the semantics are "entries whose until lands on the current wall-clock ms are already expired, not still-live." On a fast-enough machine a penalty written in the same ms as the next plugin-boot read-back lands on the boundary. A silent drift to `if (until < now)` would keep such entries alive, re-applying a stale penalty across plugin restarts, and feed that ghost to `findLive*Penalty`'s own `<= now` convention (M103). The "past" pin #7 uses `now - 1000` — strictly less — so both `<` and `<=` behave identically for it and neither path is pinned. (2) **Negative retryCount rejected via `|| retryCount < 0`.** The retryCount guard is a three-clause disjunction: `typeof !== "number"`, `!Number.isFinite`, and `< 0`. Pin #8 exercises the `typeof` clause via `undefined`. Nothing exercises the sign clause. A hand-edited disk entry with `retryCount: -1` would be silently accepted if someone "simplified" the guard as defensive paranoia, and downstream `retryCount++` logic in `computeProviderHealthUpdate`/`buildRouteHealthEntry` would shift the entire retry escalation ladder by the negative seed, making `retryCount > 0` display checks in `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` lie about penalty freshness. (3) **Non-finite retryCount rejected via `!Number.isFinite`.** The second guard clause rejects `Infinity` / `-Infinity` / `NaN` for retryCount. Pin #8 fails on `typeof` and never reaches this clause; pin #6 (NaN until) is the UNTIL finite-check on a completely different branch. A hand-edited or corrupt entry with `retryCount: Infinity` would pass the typeof check, fail only `Number.isFinite`, and silently propagate if that clause were ever dropped — then `computeProviderHealthUpdate` computes `Infinity + 1 === Infinity` and the escalation ladder is broken forever on that entry.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every plugin boot — `loadPersistedProviderHealth` invokes this validator once per on-disk entry during plugin initialization to hydrate both health maps from `.plugin-state.json`. Silent failure modes at the disk-to-memory validation layer.
- **Fix**: extended the existing ~19-line docstring with a ~65-line "Drift surfaces (M108 PDD)" section explicitly enumerating the three uncovered invariants with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — the `<=` expiry check, the `retryCount < 0` sign clause, and the `!Number.isFinite` clause are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; `loadPersistedProviderHealth` invokes the validator identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins inserted before `_whenRetryCountIsMissing_returnsNull`, orthogonal to the eight pre-existing pins. Pin A (`_whenUntilEqualsNowExactly_returnsNullAtBoundary`) uses a fixed `1_700_000_000_000` timestamp for both `until` and `now`, asserts null — any `<` drift would return the entry instead. Pin B (`_whenRetryCountIsNegative_returnsNullRejectingSignedRecord`) passes `retryCount: -1` with an otherwise-valid entry, asserts null — any guard-simplification that drops the `< 0` clause would return the entry. Pin C (`_whenRetryCountIsInfinity_returnsNullRejectingNonFiniteCount`) passes `retryCount: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY`, asserts null — any guard-simplification that drops the `!Number.isFinite` clause would return the entry.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric NEW pin with zero collateral on the 325 pre-existing tests (322 pre-M107 + 3 M107 pins). Sabotage 1 (`if (until < now) return null;` — weaken boundary): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin A alone. Pin #7 (past until with `now - 1000`) passed because strictly-past is still rejected under `<`. All other `parsePersistedHealthEntry_*` pins passed because their scenarios either use `"never"` (infinity > now), don't reach the until check, or use a clearly-future until. Sabotage 2 (drop the `|| retryCount < 0` clause): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin B alone. Pin #8 (missing retryCount) passed because `typeof undefined !== "number"` still hits. Pin #6 (NaN until) passed because it's a different branch. All other pins unaffected. Sabotage 3 (drop the `|| !Number.isFinite(retryCount)` clause): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin C alone. Pin #8 (missing retryCount) passed via typeof. Pin B (negative) passed because the `< 0` clause still rejects it. All other pins unaffected. Exactly the asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three sabotage classes, three disjoint single-NEW-pin firings, zero collateral on 325 pre-existing tests. Restored the fix, **328/328 pass** (325 pre-M108 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (appended ~65-line drift-surface section to the existing `parsePersistedHealthEntry` docstring — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (three new unit pins inserted before `_whenRetryCountIsMissing_returnsNull`; `parsePersistedHealthEntry` import already present).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the docstring — but since production behavior is bitwise-identical at HEAD (only the docstring + test pins changed), the rebuild is purely for test/build hygiene and does not ship any production change. Value is structural: the disk-to-memory validator now has dedicated single-NEW-pin tripwires on all three input-validation boundaries (until-boundary, retryCount-sign, retryCount-finiteness) that would otherwise be silently corruptible via future "defensive paranoia" guard simplifications.

### M107: the `buildRouteHealthEntry` route-level reducer — route-scope analog of M106's provider-level `computeProviderHealthUpdate`, called by all four route-health writers — had seven pre-existing pins for routeKey composition and M43 preserve-longer field values but the same three orthogonal surfaces (preserve-branch object identity, strict `>` on the equal-until tie, new-path input-mutation) remained unguarded across the dual-map architecture `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildRouteHealthEntry` at lines ~2297–2423 is the sole route-level health record constructor, invoked by all four route-health writers (`session.error` model_not_found, `assistant.message.completed` zero-token quota, `chat.params` immediate timeout, `chat.params` hang-timer timeout) and by the `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` thin wrapper. It is the route-level analog of `computeProviderHealthUpdate` (M106). Seven pre-existing pins cover the four-way routeKey composition cartesian (`composite/unprefixed/openrouter/readback`) plus three M43-era preserve-longer field-equality checks (`existing-retryCount-carry`, `preserve-longer-existing`, `accept-longer-incoming`), but they assert exclusively on return-value field values — leaving three orthogonal invariants unguarded. The same three drift classes M106 pinned at the provider level apply symmetrically here because the two functions are parallel twins: (1) **The preserve branch must return a FRESH `health` object, not `existing` by reference.** A `health: existing` optimization would share a handle between the caller's pre-call reference and the map's post-call entry, retroactively mutating already-committed observations when a later writer bumps retryCount. The M43 field-equality pins coincidentally catch the bare form (because they expect `retryCount + 1`), but a careful `health: { ...existing, retryCount: existing.retryCount + 1 }` regression would pass every M43 pin while still leaking shared enumerable own-properties — especially load-bearing if `ModelRouteHealth` ever grows a nested object field. (2) **The condition is STRICT `existing.until > newUntil` (not `>=`) — equal-until takes the NEW path.** Two route-level writers computing the same `now + 1h` boundary in the same tick (e.g. a hang-timer and a session.error firing in the same event-loop cycle against the same route) must commit to the more structural classification so `healthStateLabel` and the fallback-route resolver see reality, not a stale label. None of the seven M43 pins uses tie-case untils — they all use clearly-unequal values — so the strict/non-strict boundary is an unpinned property of the source. (3) **The input `existing` record is never mutated.** Both branches allocate fresh object literals; neither writes through `existing`. If a future refactor chose `Object.assign(existing, { state, until, retryCount })` in the new-path branch to save an allocation, every M43 field-equality pin would still pass (Object.assign returns its first argument with the right fields), but any caller that held a pre-call reference to `existing` for logging, metric emission, or diff-against-previous would misattribute new observations to prior turns.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every route-level penalty install — four distinct writers across the error-taxonomy (session.error classification, zero-token quota from the assistant.message.completed narrower, immediate-timeout at chat.params, hang-timer at chat.params) all delegate through this reducer for every 429/402/model_not_found/timeout event against every route in the dual-map architecture. Silent failure modes at the sole route-health reducer, parallel to the M106 provider-level exposure.
- **Fix**: added a new ~95-line docstring to `buildRouteHealthEntry` (previously undocumented) covering args/returns AND a "Drift surfaces (M107 PDD)" section enumerating the three uncovered invariants with concrete failure modes cross-referencing the parallel M106 provider-level pins. Body left bitwise-identical — the preserve-branch object literal, the strict `>` guard, and the new-path fresh-allocation are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; all four route-level writers invoke the helper identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins inserted after `_whenNewUntilIsLongerThanExisting_adoptsNewStateAndUntil`, orthogonal to the seven pre-existing pins. Pin A (`_whenPreserveBranchTaken_returnsFreshHealthObjectNotExistingByReference`) installs existing with 2h until, calls with 1h incoming, asserts `health !== existing` (strict identity). Pin B (`_whenExistingUntilEqualsNewUntil_takesNewPathAcceptingNewState`) constructs existing and incoming with byte-identical untils via shared `sharedDuration`, asserts `health.state === "model_not_found"` (incoming, not existing "timeout"). Pin C (`_whenNewPathTaken_doesNotMutateInputExistingRecord`) creates existing with state=quota, calls with 2h > 1h and newState=no_credit, asserts `existing.state === "quota"` (unchanged post-call).

Sabotage 1 (`health: existing` in the preserve branch): `bun test` reported pin A failing among NEW pins, plus three pre-existing pins firing as additive coverage (`buildRouteHealthEntry_whenExistingUntilIsLongerThanNewUntil_preservesExistingStateAndUntil`, the `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` M43 integration, and the `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` wrapper) — expected because the sabotage also breaks the retryCount increment those pins assert. Pin B (equal-until scenario) and pin C (new-path mutation scenario) both passed because their scenarios exercise the other branch. Sabotage 2 (`>=` instead of `>`): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin B alone. No pre-existing pin fires because all seven use clearly-unequal untils. Pin A (different test with 2h > 1h) passed unchanged. Pin C (strictly-shorter existing) passed. Sabotage 3 (`Object.assign(existing ?? {}, {...})` in the new-path branch): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin C alone. The M43 field-equality pins passed because Object.assign returns its first argument with the new fields — every return-value field matches expectations. Pin A (preserve branch) and pin B (equal-until takes new-path but assigns into a fresh empty object because existing's until === newUntil puts the check in preserve-branch territory via `>=`... actually equal-until already takes preserve via strict `>` means `existing.until > newUntil` is false → new path, and the mutation is into the real `existing` object; pin B asserts state correctness which holds under Object.assign). Exactly the asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three sabotage classes, three disjoint single-NEW-pin firings. Restored the fix, **325/325 pass** (322 pre-M107 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.

### M106: the `computeProviderHealthUpdate` preserve-longer merge — sole reducer between incoming provider penalties and persisted `ProviderHealth` — had four M43-era field-equality pins covering both branches but three further orthogonal surfaces (preserve-branch object identity, strict `>` on the equal-until tie, new-path input-mutation) remained only coincidentally guarded `✅ COMPLETED`

### M105: the `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` narrower — sole type-narrowing gate between the `assistant.message.completed` opencode event bus and the zero-token quota classifier — had a per-step M85 drift-pin partition but three further orthogonal surfaces (load-bearing `type` tag check, empty-string sessionID rejection, tokens-by-strict-reference return) were only covered incidentally by the deepEqual return-value pin `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` at lines ~2156–2235 is the sole type-narrowing gate between opencode's `assistant.message.completed` event bus and the `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` classifier that records zero-token quota penalties. Three pre-existing M85 pins (valid shape → narrowed tuple, missing sessionID → undefined, missing tokens → undefined) use a per-narrowing-step partition so a sabotage that drops one check fires exactly one pin — clean but incomplete. Three further surfaces had zero direct coverage: (1) **The `type` field check is load-bearing, not redundant.** Although opencode's event bus dispatches by event name, the runtime also forwards consolidated lifecycle events (keepalive frames, partial flushes) through `assistant.message.completed` handlers whose `properties` may include a sessionID and tokens-shaped object. A future simplification that dropped the check "because dispatch already filters" would leak keepalives into `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal`, which would then fire false zero-token quota penalties on every keepalive — silently quarantining healthy providers. All three M85 pins use the correct `type` so none exercise this drift. (2) **Empty-string sessionID rejected via `|| .length === 0`.** The M85 missing-sessionID pin passes `undefined`, which fails at `typeof !== "string"` and never reaches the length clause. A refactor that "simplified" the check to just `typeof === "string"` would pass empty-string sessionIDs through to `readAndClearSessionHangState`'s `Map<string, ...>` lookups, where an empty string key silently collides across every session map — corrupting hang state across unrelated sessions. (3) **The returned `tokens` must be the exact input reference.** Downstream consumers pipe `tokens` directly into `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal`, which walks nested values via `Object.values(value as Record<string, unknown>)`. A future `{ ...tokens }` wrap for "safety" would preserve deepEqual structure while breaking reference-stability callers rely on for diffing/caching — and M85's deepEqual pin cannot distinguish identity from structural equality.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every assistant message completion — the `event` hook invokes this narrower before dispatching to `readAndClearSessionHangState` and `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` for quota-exhaustion detection. Silent failure modes at the zero-token quota classifier input layer.
- **Fix**: extended the existing ~36-line drift-shape docstring with a ~50-line "Drift surfaces (M105 PDD)" section explicitly enumerating the three uncovered invariants. Body left bitwise-identical — the type check, the empty-string length clause, and the direct reference return are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the event hook still calls the narrower identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins inserted before the first `extractSessionErrorApiErrorContext_*` test, orthogonal to the three M85 pins. Pin A (`_whenTypeTagIsWrong_returnsUndefined`) passes `type: "session.keepalive"` with otherwise-valid shape, asserts `result === undefined`. Pin B (`_whenSessionIDIsEmptyString_returnsUndefined`) passes `sessionID: ""` with valid tokens, asserts `result === undefined` — exercises the length clause that the M85 "missing sessionID" pin never reaches. Pin C (`_whenShapeIsValid_returnsTokensByStrictReferenceNotCopy`) captures the input tokens object, asserts `result.tokens === tokens` (strict identity, not deepEqual) — catches any spread/clone sabotage that M85's deepEqual pin would silently accept.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric NEW pin with zero collateral on the 316 pre-existing tests (313 pre-M104 + 3 M104 pins). M85's missing-sessionID pin passed because `undefined` still fails the `typeof` check. M85's valid-shape deepEqual pin passed because a spread object is still structurally equal. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint single-pin firings, zero collateral on 316 pre-existing tests. ### M104: the `findLiveProviderPenalty` helper — the sole provider-level "is this provider under active penalty" entry-returning reader used by `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`, `provider.models`, and `isProviderHealthy` — had a drift-surface docstring covering the `<= now` expiry boundary convention but three further surfaces (return-by-strict-reference, read-only-on-expired, exact provider-ID keying with no case folding) were undocumented and only covered by deepEqual-return pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findLiveProviderPenalty` at lines ~1020–1076 is the provider-level analog of `findLiveRoutePenalty` — the sole helper three readers delegate to when they need the `ProviderHealth` ENTRY (not just a boolean) to decide whether a provider is currently under penalty. Four pre-existing M71 pins (empty map, expired entry, live entry, key_missing infinity) all assert on the RETURN VALUE via `assert.equal` / `assert.deepEqual`. None of them assert on *how* the return value was produced or on the map state after the call — which leaves three orthogonal silent-drift classes uncovered: (1) **Return-by-strict-reference** — the live-entry path is `return health` where `health` is the exact object installed by `recordProviderHealthPenalty`; callers (notably `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`) capture this reference at tool-call time so a later retryCount bump by `computeProviderHealthUpdate` is visible through the same handle. A future regression that wrapped the return in `{ ...health }` "for safety" would break reference identity while still passing every deepEqual pin, silently severing the shared-handle contract. (2) **Read-only on expired hit** — the expired branch returns `null` and leaves the map untouched; cleanup is the sole responsibility of `expireHealthMaps` (invoked once per chat turn by `experimental.chat.system.transform`), NOT findLive*. A "helpful" regression that deleted the expired entry on read would reset the retryCount escalation ladder mid-turn whenever an unrelated caller happened to probe an expired entry before the next real penalty — exactly the silent-corruption class M103 hardened for `expireHealthMaps` itself. The pre-existing expired-entry pin only asserts the return is null; it never probes the map state post-call. (3) **Exact provider-ID keying** — the lookup is a bare `providerHealthMap.get(providerID)` with no case normalization or composite-key transformation. Provider IDs are canonical slugs passed verbatim by the `provider.models` hook from opencode's session state. A defensive regression that introduced `providerID.toLowerCase()` would pass every existing lowercase-ID pin but silently turn a mixed-case probe into a false hit, bypassing `isProviderHealthy` for any caller that happened to capitalize the provider ID — and the dual-map architecture (ProviderHealth vs ModelRouteHealth) depends on provider keys NOT going through `composeRouteKey` normalization.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn at three distinct call sites — `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` tool reader (surfaces provider-scope blocks to the agent), `provider.models` openrouter hook (short-circuits the model map to `{}` when openrouter is unhealthy), and `isProviderHealthy` boolean predicate (used by route filtering). Silent failure modes at the provider-penalty read layer.
- **Fix**: extended the existing ~37-line docstring with a ~50-line "Drift surfaces (M104 PDD)" section explicitly enumerating all three invariants with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — the `.get`, the `<= now` guard, and the `return health` are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; all three delegating readers call the helper identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins inserted before the first `findRegistryEntryByModel_*` test, orthogonal to the four pre-existing M71 pins. Pin A (`_whenEntryLive_returnsEntryByStrictReferenceNotCopy`) installs a `no_credit` entry, captures the installed object reference, and asserts `result === installedHealth` (strict identity, not deepEqual) — a spread/clone sabotage breaks identity while still passing the M71 deepEqual pin. Pin B (`_whenEntryExpired_doesNotMutateInputMap`) installs an expired `quota` entry, calls the helper, asserts return is null AND `providerHealthMap.has("openrouter")` is still true AND `providerHealthMap.get("openrouter") === expiredHealth` (same object reference, no silent replacement). Pin C (`_whenProviderIdHasMixedCase_doesNotCaseFoldTheLookup`) installs a lowercase `"openrouter"` entry and passes mixed-case `"OpenRouter"` as the probe; asserts return is null — any `.toLowerCase()` sabotage would return the entry and fire this pin.

### M103: the `expireHealthMaps` sweeper — called from `experimental.chat.system.transform` on every chat turn to drop expired entries from both provider and route health maps — had only a small top-level docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (provider-map `<= now` inclusive boundary, route-map `<= now` inclusive boundary independently of the provider-map side, and the preserved-entry `retryCount` byte-identity invariant that keeps the penalty escalation ladder intact) orthogonal to the two pre-existing mixed-expiry and infinity-preservation pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `expireHealthMaps` at lines ~1413–1478 is the sole sweeper called from `experimental.chat.system.transform` on every chat turn to drop expired entries from both `providerHealthMap` and `modelRouteHealthMap`. It had a small top-level docstring covering the "called from transform" contract and the infinity key_missing note, but did NOT enumerate the three silent drift surfaces encoded in its 10-line body. Two pre-existing pins (lines 605 + 645) covered the mixed expired+live sweep on both maps and the infinity-preservation case — but three further surfaces had zero coverage: (1) **Provider-map boundary `<= now` is inclusive** — an entry whose `until === now` must be dropped on the same tick; a refactor to `< now` (an easy "strictly expired" mis-read of the semantics) would leak boundary-exact entries, extending the penalty window one tick past its nominal end, and a fast-retry code path would still see the just-expired provider as dead via `isProviderHealthy`'s matching `<= now` convention — a stale-penalty phantom. Pre-existing pin 1 uses `now - 1` deadlines so a `< now` drift still expires those entries; the boundary invariant needs its own dedicated pin. (2) **Route-map boundary `<= now` is inclusive INDEPENDENTLY of the provider-map side** — the two loops have two separate `<=` comparisons, and a partial refactor could drift just one of them, producing a split-brain state where route-level penalties linger one tick past their deadline while provider-level penalties expire promptly. Pre-existing pin 1 uses `now - 1` on both maps, so neither boundary drift is caught structurally. (3) **Non-expired entries are preserved UNCHANGED — the helper has no `else` clause** — surviving entries must be walked over and left byte-identical, because `retryCount` in particular must survive for `computeProviderHealthUpdate` to compute the next-penalty escalation duration on the next penalty hit. A refactor that added an `else { set(...) }` clause "to normalise" preserved entries (e.g. resetting retryCount to zero on every sweep, capping it, or rebuilding the object with `{ ...health }`) would silently flatten the penalty escalation ladder on every chat turn because every previous retryCount would be zeroed before the next penalty hit. Pre-existing pins assert `.has(...)` on surviving entries but never read retryCount back, so this drift class is structurally uncovered.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn — `experimental.chat.system.transform` calls `expireHealthMaps` once per turn. Silent failure modes at the penalty-window boundary and the escalation-ladder preservation surfaces.
- **Fix**: replaced the ~17-line top-level docstring with a ~75-line drift-surface enumeration explicitly calling out all three invariants with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — every loop, comparison, and delete call is preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the transform hook still calls the sweeper identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file, orthogonal to the two pre-existing pins. Pin A (`_whenProviderUntilExactlyEqualsNow_dropsEntryAtInclusiveBoundary`) sets `providerHealthMap["iflowcn"].until = now` and a non-expired route entry (to prevent accidental early-return shortcuts from passing this pin via an empty-route heuristic), then asserts `providerHealthMap.has("iflowcn") === false`. Pin B (`_whenRouteUntilExactlyEqualsNow_dropsEntryAtInclusiveBoundary`) mirrors Pin A on the route side: `modelRouteHealthMap["iflowcn/qwen3-coder-plus"].until = now` plus a non-expired provider entry, asserts `modelRouteHealthMap.has("iflowcn/qwen3-coder-plus") === false`. Pin C (`_whenProviderEntryIsNotExpired_preservesRetryCountForEscalationLadder`) sets `providerHealthMap["iflowcn"] = { state: "quota", until: now + 1h, retryCount: 5 }`, runs the sweeper, reads the entry back, and asserts `retryCount === 5` AND `state === "quota"` — byte-identity on the escalation state.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric NEW pin with zero collateral on the 310 pre-existing tests (307 pre-M102 + 3 M102 pins). Sabotage 1 (provider-loop `<= now` → `< now`): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin A alone (312 pass / 1 fail). Pre-existing pin 1 still passed because its provider entry is `now - 1`, which is `< now` too. Sabotage 2 (route-loop `<= now` → `< now`): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin B alone (312 pass / 1 fail). Pre-existing pin 1 still passed for the same reason on the route side. Sabotage 3 (add `else { providerHealthMap.set(providerID, { ...health, retryCount: 0 }); }` to the provider-loop): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 failure** — pin C alone (312 pass / 1 fail). Pre-existing pin 1 still passed because it asserts `.has("ollama-cloud") === true` and never reads retryCount back; pre-existing pin 2 still passed because the infinity entry is still present in the map after the sabotage (set with retryCount=0, but still present). Value is structural: the transform-hook health-map sweeper is now documented at three orthogonal drift surfaces, each with a dedicated regression tripwire — the previously-silent failure modes (provider boundary leak, route boundary leak, flattened escalation ladder) now each have single-NEW-pin coverage.

### M102: the `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth` helper — the `provider.models` hook's per-provider visible-models gate — was exported with a partial docstring but had three undocumented drift surfaces (iteration source must be `providerModels` not `enabledRawModelIDs` to avoid fabricating ghost-model keys, original `modelValue` must be passed through by reference to preserve opencode's capability metadata, input `providerModels` map must never be mutated in-place) orthogonal to the two pre-existing enabled-gate + route-penalty pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth` at lines ~460–474 is the sole gate the `provider.models` hook uses to filter each provider's opencode-supplied raw models down to the enabled, route-healthy subset the agent sees. It had a partial docstring (explained why it exists and the enabled+penalty contract) but did NOT enumerate the three silent drift surfaces encoded in its 8-line body. Two pre-existing pins (lines 3648 + 3684) covered the route-level penalty exclusion and the expired-penalty symmetry — but three further surfaces had zero coverage: (1) **Iteration source is `Object.entries(providerModels)`, never `enabledRawModelIDs`** — a refactor that inverts the loop would fabricate `filtered["ghost-model"] = undefined` for enabled-but-absent models (registry rows whose primary route was retired / renamed / hidden upstream by the provider), which opencode's router then interprets as live advertised models and dispatches to, producing a phantom-model penalty cascade fully attributable to the drift. (2) **Original `modelValue` object is passed through by reference** — downstream opencode readers extract capability hints, context window, tool-support flags, and pricing band directly from these values; replacing the stored value with `true` / `{}` / `{ id: modelID }` silently strips all metadata while still advertising the model as available. (3) **`providerModels` is treated as read-only** — the opencode-owned map is handed to the hook by reference and may flow to other hooks in the same turn; a refactor that `delete`s excluded keys in-place would corrupt the caller's view across the entire turn, cascading into every downstream reader. The function signals non-mutation by building a fresh `filtered` object and leaving the input map byte-identical to entry state.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every `provider.models` hook invocation — opencode calls this per provider to produce the visible-models map the agent sees. Silent failure modes at the core routing-visibility layer.
- **Fix**: replaced the 30-line partial docstring with a ~75-line drift-surface enumeration explicitly calling out all three invariants with concrete failure modes. Body left bitwise-identical — every iteration step, filter call, and assignment is preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the `provider.models` hook still calls the helper identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file, orthogonal to the two pre-existing pins. Pin B (`_whenEntryPasses_preservesOriginalModelValueByIdentity`) builds a `stepfunValue` object with `{id, label, contextWindow}` metadata and asserts `filtered["stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"] === stepfunValue` (strict identity, not deep-equal) — catches any stub/boolean/synthesised replacement. Pre-existing pin 3648 still passed because it checks `Object.keys(filtered).sort()` against the fixed `["stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"]` set — the sabotage still respects the penalty check and the enabled set, so for that test the output is equivalent. ### M101: the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` assembler — the sole renderer of the agent-facing "Provider health status" system-prompt block injected into every chat turn via `experimental.chat.system.transform` — was exported but had zero top-level docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (the `"Curated fallbacks (longcat/claude/gpt/grok excluded):"` agent-legibility contract label, the `if (owningEntry)` crash-guard on route-penalty sections with no matching registry entry, the `"\n\n"` blank-line cross-section separator) orthogonal to the four pre-existing regression pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` at lines ~3838–3932 was the only renderer of the "Provider health status" system-prompt block that the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook injects into every chat turn. It was exported but had zero top-level docstring, and the ~90-line body encoded three independent agent-legibility invariants. Four pre-existing pins (lines 1328–1514) covered route-only section emission, the no-penalties null sentinel, the key_missing filter via `collectAgentVisibleLivePenalties`, and the mixed quota+key_missing case — but three further drift surfaces had zero direct coverage: (1) **the `"Curated fallbacks (longcat/claude/gpt/grok excluded):"` label literal** with its parenthetical exclusion note, which is an agent-legibility contract telling the LLM *why* proprietary models (the ones banned by `isFallbackBlocked`) are absent from the bullet list below it — without the note, an agent seeing e.g. a 2h openrouter `key_dead` with a curated-fallback list that doesn't include `openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet:free` has no signal that the absence is deliberate and may try to invoke the brand-blocked route anyway, trigger a hard fail, and burn a turn; (2) **the `if (owningEntry)` crash-guard on route-penalty sections** — when no current registry entry owns the penalized composite route key (legacy persisted key from a removed model, a race between a registry hot-reload and a still-firing penalty, or a route whose owning entry was disabled after the penalty was recorded), `owningEntry` is `undefined` and the section MUST emit header-only; dropping the guard produces a `TypeError: cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'provider_order')` inside `findCuratedFallbackRoute` that crashes the entire transform hook — and because hook failures are swallowed by `logPluginHookFailure`, the plugin silently stops injecting system prompts for the rest of the session; (3) **the `sections.join("\n\n")` blank-line cross-section separator** when both provider and route penalties exist — pre-existing pins only exercise single-section outputs, so the blank-line separator between adjacent sections is silently load-bearing; a refactor that collapses the join to `"\n"` merges adjacent sections into one opaque paragraph and the agent reads e.g. a provider quota block's fallback bullet as if it were part of the route block's header.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn — `experimental.chat.system.transform` calls this assembler once per turn to build the health-status block injected into `output.system`. The three surfaces have silent failure modes at the agent-facing rendering layer: a dropped exclusion-note label silently strips the brand-blocklist agent contract, a dropped owning-entry guard silently kills the entire transform hook for the rest of the session, and a collapsed section separator silently merges provider and route penalties into one opaque paragraph.
- **Fix**: prepended a ~75-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces, explicitly calling out the asymmetry of the provider-section `"Curated fallbacks (longcat/claude/gpt/grok excluded):"` label vs the route-section `"Curated fallback for ${id}:"` singular form, the load-bearing role of the `if (owningEntry)` guard as a crash-prevention boundary (not just a cosmetic skip), and the semantic distinction between the `"\n\n"` cross-section separator and the `"\n"` intra-section line joiner. Body left bitwise-identical — every filter, guard, join, and push is preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the transform hook still calls the helper identically.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file, orthogonal to the four pre-existing pins. Pin A (`_whenProviderPenaltyExists_emitsCuratedFallbacksLabelWithExclusionNote`) builds an entry with two visible routes, attaches a `quota` penalty to the first provider, and asserts the prompt literally contains `"Curated fallbacks (longcat/claude/gpt/grok excluded):"` — the exact string including the parenthetical exclusion note. Pin B (`_whenRoutePenaltyHasNoOwningEntry_emitsHeaderOnlyWithoutCrashing`) passes an empty `modelRegistryEntries` array alongside a `modelRouteHealthMap` containing a `"removed-provider/legacy-model"` key with a live `timeout` penalty, asserts the assembler does NOT throw, asserts the output contains `"Route removed-provider/legacy-model [TIMEOUT]"`, and asserts the output does NOT contain `"Curated fallback for"`. Pin C (`_whenBothProviderAndRoutePenaltiesExist_joinsSectionsWithBlankLine`) builds two entries, attaches a provider-level `quota` penalty to one and a route-level `model_not_found` penalty to the other, splits the resulting prompt on `"\n\n"`, and asserts the split produces ≥2 chunks each containing their respective markers (`"Provider opencode [QUOTA BACKOFF]"` in one, `"Route iflowcn/qwen3-coder-plus [MODEL NOT FOUND]"` in another).
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric NEW pin with zero collateral on any of the 304 pre-existing tests. ### M100: the `findPreferredHealthyRoute` helper — the sole resolver of the agent's declared `preferredModels` list into a dispatch route via `recommendTaskModelRoute` — was exported but had zero docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (exact-match precedence over same-entry first-healthy when preferred is NOT priority-1, `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` integration rejecting hidden paid routes, `entryContainsPreferred` gate preventing cross-entry fallback leak) orthogonal to the six pre-existing regression pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findPreferredHealthyRoute` at lines ~4720–4763 was the only resolver used by `recommendTaskModelRoute` to honor the agent metadata's `preferredModels` array — the hard constraint that lets an agent declare "I must run on this model or a same-entry sibling." It was exported but had zero top-level docstring, and the 40-line body encoded three independent semantic invariants. Six pre-existing regression pins (lines 5566–5692) covered empty-preferences early return, exact-match when preferred IS priority-1, same-entry sibling degradation, no-match null path, author-order honoring, and the tier-filtered caller contract — but three further drift surfaces had zero direct coverage: (1) **Exact-match precedence over first-healthy-visible** when the preferred model is a LATER sibling (not the priority-1 route). Pin 2 (`_whenExactPreferredRouteIsHealthy_returnsExactRoute`) uses `preferred=priority-1`, so a refactor that collapses the explicit `exactRoute` find into the fallback-find scan would STILL pass pin 2 (the first-healthy happens to equal the exact match). The failure surface is silently returning the priority-1 sibling when the agent explicitly declared the priority-2 sibling. (2) **`filterVisibleProviderRoutes` integration rejects hidden paid providers** — an agent that declared `xai/grok-4` must get `null`, not a hidden paid-route dispatch. None of the six pre-existing pins uses a hidden-provider preference; a refactor that replaced `filterVisibleProviderRoutes(entry.provider_order)` with raw `entry.provider_order` would silently resurrect the paid-dispatch path for every hidden provider (xai, deepseek, github-copilot, cloudflare-ai-gateway, togetherai, cerebras, minimax-cn*, openrouter paid). (3) **`entryContainsPreferred` gate prevents cross-entry fallback leak** — without the gate, the fallback-find branch would walk entries that do NOT contain the preferred model and return their first healthy visible route as a dispatch target, polluting the agent's preference across the registry boundary. Pins 4, 5, and 6 incidentally exercise shapes where dropping the gate produces wrong returns, but none explicitly constructs the most dangerous shape: entry A holds the preferred model on an unhealthy provider AND entry B holds a DIFFERENT model on a healthy provider.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn where `recommendTaskModelRoute` honors an agent's `preferredModels` array (the canonical "I must run on X" contract declared in agent metadata). The three surfaces have silent failure modes at the dispatch layer: a dropped exact-find silently returns the priority-1 sibling when the agent explicitly declared priority-2; a dropped filter silently dispatches to xai/grok-4 or another hidden paid provider; a dropped gate silently dispatches to an UNRELATED registry entry's healthy route.
- **Fix**: prepended a ~75-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces, explicitly calling out that each is orthogonal to the six pre-existing pins and documenting the load-bearing invariants — the exact-match find is a hard requirement (not a priority-order hint), the filter call is the only thing preventing hidden-paid dispatch, and the gate is the only thing preventing cross-entry fallback bleed. Body left bitwise-identical — all three filter/find blocks, the gate, and both reasoning strings are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; `recommendTaskModelRoute` still calls the helper identically.

Pin B (`_whenPreferredPointsAtHiddenPaidProvider_returnsNull`) builds an entry with a single `xai/grok-4` route (hidden by the visibility filter) and asserts `preferred=["xai/grok-4"]` returns null. Pin C (`_whenPreferredIsInUnhealthyEntryAndSiblingEntryHasHealthyOtherModel_returnsNull`) builds two entries — entry A with `ollama-cloud/pref-free` on a quota-blocked `ollama-cloud` provider, entry B with `opencode-go/other-free` on a healthy `opencode-go` provider — and asserts `preferred=["ollama-cloud/pref-free"]` returns null (the gate must skip entry B because it does not contain the preferred model).

### M99: the `findCuratedFallbackRoute` helper — the sole resolver of the agent-visible "Curated fallbacks" bullet list emitted into every provider-penalty and route-penalty section of the system prompt by `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` — was exported but had zero docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (blockedProviderID early-filter, `isFallbackBlocked` proprietary-brand blocklist, `NO_FALLBACK_MODEL_CONFIGURED_MESSAGE` sentinel return) orthogonal to the two pre-existing regression pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findCuratedFallbackRoute` at lines ~2855–2898 was the only resolver used by `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` to populate the "Curated fallbacks" bullet list that tells the agent what to route to when the primary route blows up. It was exported but had zero docstring, and the seven-line body encoded three independent filter clauses plus a sentinel return. Two pre-existing regression pins (`_whenNextRouteIsHiddenPaidProvider_skipsToVisibleRoute` at test:491 and `_whenRouteIsMarkedUnhealthyAtRouteLevel_skipsIt` at test:553) already covered the `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` integration and the route-level health predicate — but three further drift surfaces had zero direct coverage: (1) the `blockedProviderID` early-filter (`if (providerRoute.provider === blockedProviderID) return false;`), which force-skips routes from the provider that triggered the penalty section even when `isProviderHealthy` would return `true` for that provider (e.g. mid-flow between detection and persistence, or when the caller deliberately wants to force-skip without mutating the maps); (2) the `isFallbackBlocked` proprietary-brand blocklist, which excludes longcat/anthropic/openai/xai/github-copilot provider IDs plus `/longcat/i`, `/claude/i`, `/\bgpt-?\d/i`, `/\bchatgpt/i`, `/\bgrok-?\d/i` model patterns — crucially, a route like `openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet:free` is both VISIBLE (ends in `:free`, so `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` keeps it) AND brand-blocked, so the two filters are NOT redundant and dropping either one silently lets a proprietary claude route surface as a curated fallback through the openrouter `:free` backdoor; (3) the `NO_FALLBACK_MODEL_CONFIGURED_MESSAGE` sentinel (`"no fallback configured"`), which is a literal string contract with the agent's interpretation layer — the agent is trained to read this exact string as "do not retry, escalate or wait." A refactor that changes the sentinel to `""` or `null` produces agent-visible bullet lines like `- entry → ` with a trailing space and no target, which the agent may interpret as a truncated render and retry the blowing-up route anyway.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn where `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` renders a penalty section into `output.system` — the helper is called once per provider-level penalty (line ~3765) and once per route-level penalty (line ~3813). The three surfaces have silent failure modes at the agent-visible rendering layer: a dropped early-filter recommends the same blowing-up provider one line below its own penalty banner, a dropped brand-blocklist silently upgrades the agent to a proprietary model mid-session, and a changed sentinel produces a truncated-looking bullet the agent ignores.
- **Fix**: prepended a ~90-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces, explicitly calling out that the `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` layer alone does NOT close the brand-blocklist gap (because `openrouter/anthropic/claude-*:free` passes the visibility filter), and documenting the sentinel as a contract string with the agent interpretation layer. Body left bitwise-identical — all three filter clauses, the `find` callback, the sentinel return, and the composite-form read from `provider_order[].model` (per the M31 double-prefix regression note) are preserved exactly. No call-site changes; `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` still calls the helper exactly as before.

### M98: the `healthStateLabel` switch renderer — the sole source of the human-readable label emitted for every `ProviderHealthState` into agent-facing system-prompt penalty sections and route-health summaries — lived as an unexported private function with zero docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (quota `"QUOTA BACKOFF"` suffix convention, underscore→space substitution across all multi-word states, three-word expansion of `model_not_found` → `"MODEL NOT FOUND"`) with zero direct unit pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `healthStateLabel` at lines ~3526–3535 was the only translator between the internal `ProviderHealthState` union (`"quota" | "key_dead" | "no_credit" | "key_missing" | "model_not_found" | "timeout"`) and the human-readable labels stamped into penalty section headers and route-health summaries rendered into the agent's system prompt. It was unexported, had no docstring, and encoded three independent drift surfaces in an eight-arm switch: (1) the `"quota"` case alone returns a TWO-word label `"QUOTA BACKOFF"` — `"BACKOFF"` is a suffix convention signaling "transient recovery, wait the window out" that no other state carries (`"key_dead"` → `"KEY DEAD"` is semantically different: the key is gone, no waiting helps). A refactor that drops the suffix to match the other states collapses the only in-label signal that tells the agent *how* to recover from a quota penalty. (2) All four multi-word states (`key_dead`, `no_credit`, `key_missing`, `model_not_found`) substitute underscore for space, relying on every case arm to spell the literal label correctly rather than on a single `.replace(/_/g, " ").toUpperCase()` derivation — a refactor that replaces the switch with `state.replace("_", " ").toUpperCase()` (note the non-global regex) silently leaves `"MODEL_NOT FOUND"` because the non-global replace only touches the first underscore. (3) The `"model_not_found"` case is the only THREE-word form (`"MODEL NOT FOUND"`) — the drift class here is "all underscores must be replaced, not just the first", which is undetectable on two-word labels but catastrophic on three-word ones. All three surfaces lived as conventions of an inline switch rather than as properties-of-one-documented-helper with dedicated regression pins.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every plugin-init health-seeding pass and on every chat turn where `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` renders a penalty section — `healthStateLabel` is called from the penalty section prefix formatter and from the route-health summary renderer, both of which inject into `output.system`. The three surfaces have silent failure modes at the system-prompt layer: a dropped `"BACKOFF"` suffix removes the agent's only in-label recovery signal for quota penalties, an underscore-in-label exposes internal enum tokens to the agent, and a `"MODEL_NOT FOUND"` (first-only replace) drift is the exact failure mode a `.replace("_", " ")` refactor would produce.
- **Fix**: added `export` to `healthStateLabel` and prepended a ~55-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (QUOTA BACKOFF suffix convention, underscore→space substitution, three-word expansion for `model_not_found`) with concrete failure-mode descriptions for each. Body left bitwise-identical — all six case arms, return strings, and fallthrough structure preserved exactly. No call-site changes; penalty section prefix and route-health renderer still consume the helper exactly as before.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file. Pin A (`healthStateLabel_whenStateIsQuota_labelCarriesBackoffSuffix`) asserts `healthStateLabel("quota").endsWith("BACKOFF")` — inspects only the suffix convention so the underscore substitution and three-word expansion sabotages cannot flip this assertion. Pin B (`healthStateLabel_whenStateIsKeyDead_labelUsesSpaceNotUnderscore`) asserts `!healthStateLabel("key_dead").includes("_")` — inspects only the underscore substitution so the suffix drop on quota and the three-word expansion on model_not_found cannot flip this assertion. Pin C (`healthStateLabel_whenStateIsModelNotFound_labelIsThreeWordForm`) asserts exact `healthStateLabel("model_not_found") === "MODEL NOT FOUND"` — catches the `.replace("_", " ")` first-only drift class specifically because a correct two-word expansion would leave a lingering underscore.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated asymmetric pin. Sabotage 1 (`case "quota": return "QUOTA";` — drop the `"BACKOFF"` suffix): `bun test` reported 3 expected failures — pin A (new) plus 2 additive coverage pins from pre-existing `formatPenaltySectionPrefix_whenStateIsQuota_synopsisContainsQuotaBackoffLabel` and `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenQuotaAndKeyMissingMixed_omitsKeyMissingFromSections` that depend transitively on the quota label shape (295 pass / 3 fail). Pins B and C still passed because their target cases are untouched. Sabotage 2 (`case "key_dead": return "KEY_DEAD";` — underscore instead of space): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin B alone (297 pass / 1 fail). Pin A still passed because the quota arm is untouched. Pin C still passed because the model_not_found arm is untouched. Sabotage 3 (`case "model_not_found": return "MODEL NOT_FOUND";` — first-only replace drift class): `bun test` reported 2 expected failures — pin C (new) plus 1 additive coverage from pre-existing `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyRoutePenaltiesExist_emitsRouteSection` that depends transitively on the model_not_found label shape (296 pass / 2 fail). Pins A and B still passed because their target arms are untouched. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint NEW-pin firings, every new pin caught by exactly one sabotage, additive coverage from pre-existing integration tests acceptable because they do not co-fire across sabotages. Restored the fix, **298/298 pass** (295 pre-M98 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `export` keyword and ~55-line drift-surface docstring to `healthStateLabel` — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `healthStateLabel` import after `hasUsableCredential`, three new unit pins at end-of-file).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the exported helper — but since the production behavior is bitwise-identical at HEAD (only the `export` keyword and docstring changed), the rebuild is purely for test/build hygiene and does not ship any production change. ### M97: the `buildRoutingContextSystemPrompt` renderer — the sole source of the "Active model routing context" system prompt section injected on every chat turn — lived as an unexported private function with zero docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (header-first invariant, multi-value `.join(", ")` separator, cost-tier + billing-mode `" | "` fusion) with zero direct unit pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildRoutingContextSystemPrompt` at lines ~666–677 was the only renderer of the "Active model routing context" section pushed into `output.system` by the `chat.params` hook (line ~5439). It was unexported, had no docstring, and encoded three independent drift surfaces in eight lines of array-then-join construction: (1) the array opens with `ACTIVE_MODEL_ROUTING_CONTEXT_HEADER` as the FIRST element so the rendered string's first line is the canonical `"## Active model routing context"` header — opencode's `experimental.chat.system.transform` pipeline concatenates multiple prompt sections and downstream splitters locate this block by header match, so a refactor that drops the header (e.g. "the `Model:` line is enough context") silently merges the section into whichever prior section rendered before it, and any tooling that looks for the header to extract the active-model context gets nothing. (2) Three list-valued fields (`default_roles`, `best_for`, `not_for`) all join their array values with the canonical `", "` (comma + space) separator — the same separator every other agent-facing list renderer in this plugin uses — and a refactor that drops the space (the "commas are commas, why waste bytes" drift class) silently turns `"coding, architect"` into `"coding,architect"` at all three parallel sites at once, breaking any downstream parser that splits on `", "`. (3) The final line fuses `cost_tier` and `billing_mode` on ONE line with a `" | "` (space-pipe-space) separator — the two axes are deliberately kept on one line so the agent reads them together, but the pipe is the only signal that they are distinct axes. A refactor that changes the separator silently makes the line ambiguous to any naive `Cost tier: (\w+)` extractor. All three surfaces lived as conventions of one eight-line inline array rather than as properties-of-one-documented-helper with dedicated regression pins.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every chat turn where the active model is a curated registry entry — the `chat.params` hook calls this renderer unconditionally to inject the context section. The three surfaces have silent failure modes at the system-prompt layer: a header drop makes the block unlocatable, a separator drift breaks list parsers, a pipe change makes the cost-billing line ambiguous. None of the three would produce an immediate error; the agent would just silently get slightly-wrong context on every turn.
- **Fix**: added `export` to `buildRoutingContextSystemPrompt` and prepended a ~55-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (header-first invariant, multi-value `", "` separator, cost-tier + billing-mode `" | "` fusion) with concrete failure-mode descriptions for each. Body left bitwise-identical — header, field order, join separators, and pipe separator are all preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the `chat.params` hook at line ~5439 still calls the renderer exactly as before.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file. Pin A (`_whenRenderingEntry_emitsHeaderAsFirstLine`) builds an entry with single-role default_roles, asserts `rendered.split("\n")[0] === "## Active model routing context"` — inspects only the first line, so neither the separator sabotages nor the pipe sabotage can flip this assertion. Pin B (`_whenRolesIsMultiValue_joinsWithCommaSpaceSeparator`) builds an entry with TWO default_roles (`["coding", "architect"]`) and asserts the Roles line exact-matches `"Roles: coding, architect"` — header untouched so pin A's surface is unaffected, cost-tier line untouched so pin C's surface is unaffected. Pin C (`_whenRenderingEntry_fusesCostTierAndBillingWithPipeSeparator`) asserts the cost-tier line exact-matches `"Cost tier: cheap | Billing: paid_api"` — uses single-role input so pin B's separator surface is not co-located, and inspects only the cost-tier line so the header drop cannot flip this assertion.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated pin. Sabotage 1 (remove `ACTIVE_MODEL_ROUTING_CONTEXT_HEADER,` from the array so the rendered string starts with `"Model: ..."`): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin A alone (294 pass / 1 fail). Pins B and C still passed because their find-by-prefix assertions do not care about the header's presence. Sabotage 2 (change `default_roles.join(", ")` to `default_roles.join(",")` — drop the space): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin B alone (294 pass / 1 fail). Pin A still passed because the header line is untouched. Pin C still passed because the cost-tier line is untouched. Sabotage 3 (change `" | "` to `" / "` in the cost-tier line): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin C alone (294 pass / 1 fail). Pins A and B still passed because their target lines are untouched. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage, clean partition with no collateral. Restored the fix, **295/295 pass** (292 pre-M97 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
