### M96: the `providerEnvVarCandidates` helper — the sole source of truth for the env var fallback that prevents false `key_missing` flags when a credential lives only in an environment variable — lived as an unexported private function with zero docstring and three undocumented drift surfaces (override table consultation, dash-to-underscore normalization, uppercase + `_API_KEY` conventional form composition) with zero direct unit pins `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `providerEnvVarCandidates` at lines ~4163–4170 was the only builder of the env var name list that `providerHasEnvVarCredential` walks when deciding whether a provider has a credential in the environment. It was unexported, had no docstring, and encoded three independent drift surfaces in seven lines: (1) the `if (overrides) return overrides;` early return consults `PROVIDER_ENV_VAR_OVERRIDES` for providers whose env var name does not follow the conventional `<PROVIDER>_API_KEY` pattern (kimi-for-coding → KIMI_API_KEY) OR providers with MULTIPLE legal env var names (google → `["GEMINI_API_KEY", "GOOGLE_API_KEY"]`, togetherai → `["TOGETHER_API_KEY", "TOGETHERAI_API_KEY"]`). A refactor that drops the early return silently collapses every multi-name override to whatever the conventional form produces (`GOOGLE_API_KEY` alone for google, `TOGETHERAI_API_KEY` alone for togetherai), so anyone configured via only `GEMINI_API_KEY` or `TOGETHER_API_KEY` is false-flagged `key_missing` at plugin init and the provider is suppressed from routing even though opencode itself honours the credential. (2) The `.replace(/-/g, "_")` normalization is what lets the conventional form produce a POSIX-valid env var name from a dashed provider id (`ollama-cloud` → `OLLAMA_CLOUD_API_KEY`). A refactor that drops the replacement produces syntactically-invalid names like `OLLAMA-CLOUD_API_KEY` that no shell will ever set, so every dashed non-overridden provider is permanently false-flagged at the env var fallback layer. (3) The `.toUpperCase()` + `_API_KEY` suffix together compose the conventional form; dropping either flips the name out of shell convention. All three surfaces lived as properties-of-one-inline-string-template rather than as properties-of-one-helper with dedicated regression pins.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every plugin-init credential check through `providerHasEnvVarCredential`, which is called from `initializeProviderHealthState` during the key_missing gate pass. The three surfaces have silent failure modes at init — a collapsed override or dropped dash/upper step manifests as "this provider is permanently disabled" rather than a hard error.
- **Fix**: added `export` to `providerEnvVarCandidates` and prepended a ~55-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (override table consultation, dash-to-underscore normalization, uppercase + `_API_KEY` suffix composition) with concrete failure-mode descriptions for each. Body left bitwise-identical — the `PROVIDER_ENV_VAR_OVERRIDES` lookup, early return, dash replacement, uppercase, and suffix composition are all preserved exactly. No call-site changes.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file. Pin A (`_whenProviderHasMultiNameOverride_returnsOverrideListVerbatim`) uses `"google"` (pinned in the override table with TWO legal names) and asserts `candidates.length === 2` + exact order `["GEMINI_API_KEY", "GOOGLE_API_KEY"]`. Google has no dashes, so dropping the dash replacement or the uppercase would still leave pin A green — it only fires on the override-consultation surface. Pin B (`_whenProviderIdContainsDash_substitutesUnderscore`) uses `"ollama-cloud"` (NOT in the override table) and asserts `candidates[0]?.includes("-") === false` — a "no dash remains" predicate, deliberately orthogonal to casing so a sabotage that drops only `.toUpperCase()` produces `"ollama_cloud_API_KEY"` (still no dash) and leaves pin B green. Pin C (`_whenProviderIdIsLowerAlphaOnly_producesUpperConventionalForm`) uses `"foo"` (NOT in override table, no dashes, lowercase) and asserts `deepEqual(candidates, ["FOO_API_KEY"])` — dropping uppercase flips it to `"foo_API_KEY"` and dropping the suffix flips it to `"FOO"`, both caught. Pin C has no dashes so dropping the dash replacement cannot fire it; pin C is not in the override table so dropping the early return cannot fire it.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated pin. Sabotage 1 (drop the `if (overrides) return overrides;` early return so every provider falls through to the conventional form): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin A alone (291 pass / 1 fail). Pin B and C's inputs are not in the override table, so their code path was untouched. Sabotage 2 (drop the `.replace(/-/g, "_")` so the dash passes through): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin B alone (291 pass / 1 fail). Pin A fires the override early-return path and never reaches the dash code. Pin C's `"foo"` has no dashes. Sabotage 3 (drop the `.toUpperCase()` so lowercase leaks through): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin C alone (291 pass / 1 fail). Pin A fires the override path. Pin B's assertion is "no dash remains" — lowercase underscore-bearing result still passes that predicate. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets. Restored the fix, **292/292 pass** (289 pre-M96 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `export` keyword and ~55-line drift-surface docstring to `providerEnvVarCandidates` — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `providerEnvVarCandidates` import after `parseHangTimeoutMs`, three new unit pins at end-of-file).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the exported helper — but since the production behavior is bitwise-identical at HEAD (only the `export` keyword and docstring changed), the rebuild is purely for test/build hygiene and does not ship any production change. Value is structural: the env var fallback builder is now exported, the three drift surfaces are now documented as drift surfaces in a canonical docstring, and three dedicated regression tests pin each surface with asymmetric partition — the previously-silent failure modes (multi-name override collapse, dashed-provider shell-invalid name, lowercase/suffix drift) now each have a dedicated tripwire.

### M95: the `buildEnabledProviderModelSet` helper — the sole source of truth for the `provider.models` opencode curation hook's visible-model set — lived as an unexported private function with only a five-line comment, and three independent drift surfaces (enabled gate, provider filter, prefix-strip normalization) were undocumented as drift surfaces and had zero direct unit pins, so a silent refactor at any one surface would pass every current test while the curation hook silently leaked or hid models at the opencode provider boundary `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildEnabledProviderModelSet` at lines ~476–495 was the only builder of the raw-id set that the `provider.models` opencode hook consults when deciding which models to keep visible for a given provider, but was declared as an un-exported private function with only a five-line comment. The body encoded three independent drift surfaces with concrete failure modes: (1) the `if (!modelRegistryEntry.enabled) continue;` gate is the operator-facing "hide this model from the router" switch; a refactor that drops it silently resurrects every disabled model at the provider-hook boundary, making the `enabled` field a no-op. (2) The `if (providerRoute.provider !== providerID) continue;` filter prevents cross-provider fallback routes (e.g. a model with a primary openrouter route and a secondary ollama-cloud route) from leaking into the WRONG provider's visible set; a refactor that drops it leaks ollama-cloud keys into openrouter's set and the consumer's `Set.has(modelID)` check compares against the wrong key space. (3) The `.startsWith(providerPrefix) ? .slice(...) : raw` prefix-strip normalizes between opencode's RAW key space (provider-relative, e.g. `"xiaomi/mimo-v2-pro"`) and the registry's COMPOSITE form (`"openrouter/xiaomi/mimo-v2-pro"`); a refactor that drops the strip silently populates the set with composite strings, the provider hook's `Set.has` check then never matches any opencode key, and the hook returns `{}` — zero visible models to the router, looking like a full provider outage even when HEAD is healthy. All three surfaces lived on eight lines of opaque iteration rather than as properties-of-one-helper with dedicated regression pins.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every call to the `provider.models` opencode hook at line ~5092, which is every opencode model-picker refresh. The three surfaces have silent failure modes, and the third surface's failure (strip-off → composite-keyed set → zero visible models) is the hardest to catch at integration level because no test currently walks the hook with a sabotaged helper and asserts the resulting visible set is non-empty.
- **Fix**: added `export` to `buildEnabledProviderModelSet` and prepended a ~60-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (enabled gate, provider filter, prefix-strip normalization) with concrete failure-mode descriptions for each, plus a note on why unprefixed registry entries (LongCat family) are added verbatim via the ternary so the asymmetry stays consistent with `findRegistryEntryByModel`. Body left bitwise-identical — the enabled check, provider filter, and strip ternary are all preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the `provider.models` hook still calls the helper exactly as before.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file. Pin A (`_whenDisabledEntryShareProviderWithEnabled_dropsDisabled`) builds `[enabled openrouter, disabled openrouter]` with UNPREFIXED raw model strings (`"alpha"`, `"beta"`) so sabotage 3 (strip drop) is a no-op here, and asserts `result.size === 1` + `result.has("alpha") === true`. Pin B (`_whenEntryTargetsDifferentProvider_excludedFromResult`) builds one enabled openrouter entry + one enabled ollama-cloud entry, also with UNPREFIXED model strings, calls with `providerID === "openrouter"`, and asserts `result.size === 1` + `result.has("alpha") === true` — pin A cannot fire because both entries are enabled; pin C cannot fire because strip is a no-op. Pin C (`_whenRouteModelHasCompositePrefix_stripsProviderPrefix`) builds ONE enabled entry with composite-prefix form `"openrouter/zoo"`, asserts `result.has("zoo") === true` — pin A cannot fire because there's no disabled entry; pin B cannot fire because there's only one provider in the input. Three independent partition axes — disabled-vs-enabled, cross-provider, composite-prefix — with no pin using composite-prefix form unless it specifically tests the strip surface.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated new pin. Sabotage 1 (drop `if (!modelRegistryEntry.enabled) continue;` — the "refactor forgets to re-gate on enabled" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin A alone (288 pass / 1 fail). Pins B and C still passed because their inputs are all enabled. Sabotage 2 (drop `if (providerRoute.provider !== providerID) continue;` — the "refactor drops the cross-provider filter" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin B alone (288 pass / 1 fail). Pin A still passed because its input has all routes targeting the queried provider. Pin C still passed because its input has only one provider. Sabotage 3 (drop the `.startsWith(...) ? .slice(...) : raw` ternary and add `providerRoute.model` directly — the "refactor drops the composite-to-raw normalization" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin C alone (288 pass / 1 fail). Pins A and B still passed because both use unprefixed raw model strings, making the strip ternary a no-op on their inputs. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage, clean partition with no collateral. Restored the fix, **289/289 pass** (286 pre-M95 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.

### M94: the module-level `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` helper (the single source of truth for the three `inferTaskComplexity` classifier regexes — LARGE/SMALL/MEDIUM) lived as an unexported private function with only a two-line comment — three independent drift surfaces (leading-only word boundary, regex metacharacter escape, case-insensitive flag) were undocumented as drift surfaces and had zero direct unit pins, so a silent refactor at any one surface would pass every current test while the classifier silently mis-tiered real traffic `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` at lines ~3848–3854 was the single source of truth for every complexity-classification regex — called from the three module-level initializations `LARGE_COMPLEXITY_REGEX`, `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_REGEX`, and `MEDIUM_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` — but was declared as an un-exported private function with only a two-line comment acknowledging the leading-only boundary. The body encodes three independent drift surfaces, each with concrete failure history: (1) the pattern is `\b(?:<alt>)` with a leading boundary and NO trailing boundary — this is deliberate so stems like `"refactor"` match inflections `"refactoring"` / `"refactored"` / `"refactors"`, and stems like `"system"` match `"systems"` / `"systemic"`. A refactor that adds a trailing `\b` (the "symmetric looks cleaner" drift class) produces exact-word matches and silently drops every inflection — a "refactoring the architecture" prompt would under-tier from `large` to `medium` because `refactor` no longer matches `refactoring`. (2) The `.replace(/[.*+?^${}()|[\]\\]/g, "\\$&")` step escapes every regex metachar in each stem so a future stem like `"node.js"` or `"c++"` matches literally. A refactor that drops the escape (the "stems are plain words, no escaping needed" drift class) silently turns `.` into "any character" — a `"node.js"` stem would match `"nodeXjs"` or `"node js"`, making the classifier fire on unrelated substrings. (3) The `"i"` flag on `new RegExp(...)` is what lets the classifier match `"REFACTOR THIS"` against a lower-case stem `"refactor"`. A refactor that drops the flag produces a case-sensitive regex that misses every capitalized prompt — the bug is especially pernicious because all current unit tests feed lowercase prompts (via `prompt.toLowerCase()` inside `inferTaskComplexity`), so the regex-level case-fold is ONLY exercised by production traffic with mixed-case input. All three surfaces lived as properties of four lines of opaque regex construction rather than as properties-of-one-helper with dedicated regression pins.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every call to `inferTaskComplexity`, which is every call to `recommendTaskModelRoute` without an explicit `complexity` field or an agent-frontmatter `routing_complexity` override — the common case. The three surfaces have silent failure modes: surface 1 under-tiers large tasks to medium, surface 2 over-fires the classifier on unrelated substrings (false positives), surface 3 under-tiers every mixed-case prompt. Surface 3's failure mode is the hardest to detect because the existing `inferTaskComplexity_*` integration tests all normalize to lowercase before hitting the regex, so the `"i"` flag is effectively untested at the integration layer despite being critical for production correctness.
- **Fix**: added `export` to `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` and prepended a ~55-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (leading-only word boundary, regex metacharacter escape, case-insensitive flag) with concrete failure-mode descriptions for each, so future refactors see the full rationale before touching any one line. Body left bitwise-identical — the `.replace` escape pass, the `\\b(?:...)` leading-only pattern, and the `"i"` flag are all preserved exactly. No call-site changes; the three module-level `*_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` initializations still call the helper exactly as before.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the M93 `filterEnabledEntriesByOptionalRole_*` cluster in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Pin A (`_whenStemIsRefactor_matchesInflectionRefactoring`) asserts `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex(["refactor"]).test("refactoring this module") === true` — a lowercase single-word no-metachar stem so pins B and C cannot fire here. Pin B (`_whenStemContainsDot_escapesDotAsLiteral`) uses a `"node.js"` stem and TWO assertions: `.test("node.js runtime") === true` AND `.test("nodeXjs runtime") === false` — the second assertion flips if the escape is dropped because unescaped `.` matches any character. Pin C (`_whenStemIsLowerCaseButPromptIsUpperCase_matches`) asserts `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex(["refactor"]).test("REFACTOR") === true` — full-capitalized prompt, no inflection, no metachar so pins A and B cannot fire.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly its designated new pin. Sabotage 1 (add trailing `\b` → `\b(?:...)\b` — the "symmetric boundary" drift class): `bun test` reported **pin A failure** PLUS 2 pre-existing `inferTaskComplexity_*` integration tests (`whenPromptUsesRefactoringInflection_stillClassifiesAsLarge` and `whenPromptMentionsRenamesInflection_stillClassifiesAsSmall`) that legitimately exercise the inflection invariant through the real `inferTaskComplexity` pipeline (additive public-surface coverage, not a partition violation). Pins B and C still passed because the metachar escape and case-fold surfaces are untouched. Sabotage 2 (drop the `.replace(...)` escape → `stems.join("|")` — the "stems are plain words" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin B alone. The second assertion `.test("nodeXjs runtime") === false` flipped to `true` because unescaped `.` matches `X`. Pin A still passed because `"refactor"` has no metachars. Pin C still passed for the same reason. Sabotage 3 (drop the `"i"` flag → `new RegExp(...)` with no flags — the "default flags are fine" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — pin C alone. A case-sensitive regex built from `"refactor"` cannot match `"REFACTOR"`. Pins A and B still passed because both use lowercase prompts. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin design targets — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings among the new pins, every pin caught by at least one sabotage, plus legitimate additive coverage on sabotage 1 through the real classifier pipeline. Restored the fix, **286/286 pass** (283 pre-M94 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `export` keyword and ~55-line drift-surface docstring to `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` — body unchanged), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` import after `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`, three new unit pins directly before the M93 `filterEnabledEntriesByOptionalRole_*` cluster).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the exported helper — but since the production behavior is bitwise-identical at HEAD (only the `export` keyword and docstring changed), the rebuild is purely for test/build hygiene and does not ship any production change. Value is structural: the helper is now exported so integration-level tests at the three complexity-regex callers can pin individual drift surfaces directly, the three drift surfaces are now documented as drift surfaces in a canonical docstring, and three dedicated regression tests pin each surface with asymmetric partition — the previously-silent failure modes (inflection drop, unescaped metachar, case-sensitive regex) now each have a dedicated tripwire.

### M93: the `recommendTaskModelRoute` function inlined two structurally-identical `modelRegistryEntries.filter((entry) => { if (!entry.enabled) return false; if (role && !entry.default_roles.includes(role)) return false; ... })` two-predicate passes for `roleMatchedEntries` and `rolePreferredEntries` — three drift surfaces (enabled-gate, null-role passthrough short-circuit, role-membership exactness) lived as conventions across those parallel inlined copies rather than as single-site properties of one helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: inside `recommendTaskModelRoute` at lines ~4428–4457, the function's first-stage candidate narrowing built two structurally-parallel filtered lists that each re-implemented the same `{enabled} ∩ {optional role}` two-predicate pass. `roleMatchedEntries` opened with `if (!entry.enabled) return false; if (role && !entry.default_roles.includes(role)) return false;` then layered on an `allowedTiers.includes(entry.capability_tier)` tier check. `rolePreferredEntries` opened with the identical two-predicate pass then `return true;` — no tier filter. Three independent drift surfaces lived on those parallel inlined copies: (1) the `!entry.enabled` short-circuit is the global disable switch — a refactor that drops it at ONE site silently resurrects disabled models at that site while the other keeps filtering them, producing an inconsistent decision surface where a disabled model is "preferred" by one path and "unavailable" to another. (2) The `role && ...` short-circuit is the null-role passthrough idiom — a refactor that flips it to `if (!entry.default_roles.includes(role)) return false;` (dropping the null guard) turns `Array.prototype.includes(null)` into a universal false and silently empties the candidate set for every null-role caller, producing "every null-role task throws no healthy route" which looks like a full routing outage even when HEAD is healthy. (3) The `.includes(role)` check is the role-membership exactness gate — a refactor that weakens it to substring/startswith/case-insensitive match silently lets tangentially-related entries into the candidate set (an entry tagged `["architect_reviewer"]` slipping past a `role === "architect"` filter). The three surfaces were a duplicated ritual spread across two structurally-parallel filter passes, and the same `{enabled} ∩ {optional role}` pattern is ALSO inlined at a third site inside `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` (line ~4568) — three call sites, three independent copies.
- **Reachability**: live code path on every agent turn that reaches `recommendTaskModelRoute` (the task-routing main entry point). Latent drift vector today — no current live divergence — but the mirror shape is exactly the pattern that historically diverges at one site ahead of its siblings. Collapsing the two-predicate pass into one exported helper closes the copy-paste mirror surface at the two `recommendTaskModelRoute` sites; the third call site (`selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`) is deliberately left for a future iteration because it has a different enclosing filter shape (task substring match + capability tier match) and collapsing it in the same pass would produce collateral pins against the unrelated surfaces.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `filterEnabledEntriesByOptionalRole(modelRegistryEntries: ModelRegistryEntry[], role: string | null): ModelRegistryEntry[]` directly before `findPreferredHealthyRoute`, with a ~50-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (enabled-gate semantics, null-role passthrough short-circuit, role-membership exactness) and documenting why the helper returns a shallow copy (via `.filter`) so callers can chain `.sort()` / `.filter()` without mutating the input. The helper body is the exact two-predicate pass: `if (!entry.enabled) return false; if (role && !entry.default_roles.includes(role)) return false; return true;`. Rewired `roleMatchedEntries` from the six-line inline filter to `filterEnabledEntriesByOptionalRole(modelRegistryEntries, role).filter((entry) => allowedTiers.includes(entry.capability_tier))` with an M93 comment explaining that the capability-tier layer stays at the call site because it's unique to this path. Rewired `rolePreferredEntries` from the five-line inline filter to a direct `filterEnabledEntriesByOptionalRole(modelRegistryEntries, role)` call with an M93 comment.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at end-of-file. Pin A (`_whenDisabledEntryShareRoleWithEnabled_dropsDisabled`) builds `[enabled coding, disabled coding]` and passes `role === "coding"`, asserting result length is 1 and id is the enabled one — deliberately NOT using null role so pins B and C cannot fire here. Pin B (`_whenRoleIsNull_passesAllEnabledEntriesRegardlessOfRoles`) builds two enabled entries with disjoint roles (`["coding"]` and `["architect"]`) and passes `role === null`, asserting length is 2 — the sabotage class "drop the `role &&` short-circuit" produces `.includes(null)` false for everything, emptying the result. Pin C (`_whenRoleIsCoding_excludesArchitectEntry`) builds the same two entries and passes `role === "coding"`, asserting length is 1 and id is the coding one — the sabotage class "drop the `.includes(role)` check" lets the architect entry through. Pin A uses concrete role + enabled partition; pin B uses null role; pin C uses concrete role + disjoint-roles partition — three independent partition axes, each firing on its designated sabotage without cross-contamination.

Pins B and C still passed because their inputs are all enabled. Sabotage 2 (replace `if (role && !entry.default_roles.includes(role)) return false;` with `if (!entry.default_roles.includes(role as string)) return false;` — the "refactor drops the null-role short-circuit" drift class): `bun test` reported **pin B failure** PLUS 4 pre-existing integration tests in `recommendTaskModelRoute_*` that legitimately exercise the null-role path through the main routing entry point (additive public-surface coverage, not a partition violation — those tests correctly catch the regression via the real call chain). ### M92: the `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` function's final rendering block inlined three separate drift-prone surfaces — a raw `.slice(0, 8)` role-row cap literal, an inline row format string `` `- ${role}: ${models.join(", ")}` ``, and an empty-map early-return null sentinel — all living inline at the tail of the function rather than as properties of a dedicated renderer `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: at lines ~3724–3732 of `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`, the function's final rendering block built the "Available models by role/task" system-prompt section inline after walking the registry. Three independent drift surfaces lived on four lines of inline code: (1) the magic literal `8` inside `.slice(0, 8)` caps how many role rows are rendered — a refactor that tweaks the cap at one site without another (this function is paralleled by `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`'s section-assembly pattern) silently drops role rows the agent needs, or exceeds the token budget the section was sized for; (2) the inline row format `` `- ${role}: ${models.join(", ")}` `` is the exact string the agent parses when looking for alternative models to try during a backoff — any drift in bullet char, colon, or join separator produces rows the agent silently ignores because its "find me a healthy model for role X" pattern doesn't match; (3) the pattern of "check empty map → return null, otherwise build lines → prepend header → return" folds a null sentinel into the tail of the function, and a refactor that returns `""` instead of `null` on empty input leaks an empty section into the assembled prompt (stray header with no body). The three surfaces were a rendering ritual spread across the function's tail rather than a property of one renderer.
- **Reachability**: live code path reached on every agent turn where `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` returns true (i.e. at least one provider or route is in a non-key-missing penalty state). The function is called from `assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts` at line 5198 and injected into the system prompt transform. Latent drift vector today — no current live divergence — but the three surfaces have bitten us before at parallel sites, and this site was the last remaining inline rendering block in the health-prompt pipeline after M89–M91 collapsed the penalty-section builders.
- **Fix**: added a named constant `MAX_AVAILABLE_MODELS_ROLES_RENDERED = 8` at the top-of-file constants block, and extracted a new exported helper `renderAvailableModelsSystemPromptBody(roleToModels: Map<string, string[]>): string | null` directly before `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`, with a ~40-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (role-row cap, row format, empty-input null sentinel) and explaining that the empty-map check inside the helper is a *post-walk* gate distinct from the *pre-walk* `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` gate at the top of the outer function. The helper body is: return `null` if `roleToModels.size === 0`; otherwise build `lines` via `Array.from(roleToModels.entries()).slice(0, MAX_AVAILABLE_MODELS_ROLES_RENDERED).map(([role, models]) => \`- ${role}: ${models.join(", ")}\`)`; return `[AVAILABLE_MODELS_HEADER, ...lines].join("\n")`. Rewired the call site in `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` by deleting both the inline `if (roleToModels.size === 0) return null;` gate AND the inline `lines` construction, replacing both with a single `return renderAvailableModelsSystemPromptBody(roleToModels);`. The helper now owns the single source of truth for the role-row cap, the row format, and the empty-input null sentinel.

### M91: the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` function's provider-penalty loop and route-penalty loop both independently built a `[PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, "${entity} [${label}] until ${until}."]` two-element header prefix with identical `const label = healthStateLabel(health.state); const until = formatHealthExpiry(health.until);` preprocess — three drift surfaces (header constant, state label derivation, until formatter) lived as conventions across two structurally-parallel loops rather than as single-site properties of one helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` function's two penalty loops each independently constructed a two-line header prefix with identical preprocess. The provider loop opened with `const label = healthStateLabel(health.state); const until = formatHealthExpiry(health.until);` and pushed `[PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, \`Provider ${providerID} [${label}] until ${until}.\`, ...]` into the sections array. The route loop opened with the identical `const label = ...; const until = ...;` preprocess and built `const header = [PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, \`Route ${routeKey} [${label}] until ${until}.\`];`. Three independent drift surfaces lived on that mirror pair: (1) the `PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER` constant (`"## Provider health status"`) is the section marker the agent uses to locate the penalty block in the system prompt — a refactor that drops or renames the constant in ONE loop but not the other silently produces an asymmetric prompt where provider penalties live under one header and route penalties under another (or none), so the agent sees two banners and may treat them as unrelated alerts. (2) The `healthStateLabel(health.state)` call maps `"quota"` → `"QUOTA BACKOFF"`, `"key_dead"` → `"KEY DEAD"`, etc. — a human-readable form the agent can match against its "try another model" prompts. A refactor that drops the call and interpolates raw `health.state` silently produces lowercase snake_case labels (`[quota]`) the agent does not recognize as "the thing that tells me to back off," so the agent keeps retrying the penalized route until it hits the backoff expiry by brute force. Worse: dropping the call in ONE loop but not the other produces asymmetric labels for provider vs route penalties — a classic copy-paste drift where the two sections disagree about the same state. (3) The `formatHealthExpiry(health.until)` call maps raw epoch ms into ISO-8601 strings or the `"never"` sentinel for `Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY`. A refactor that drops the call silently emits `"until 1700000000000"` or `"until Infinity"` — neither is human- or agent-friendly, and the `Infinity` case is especially painful because the template literal renders it as the string `"Infinity"` which the agent almost certainly parses as "invalid date." The three surfaces were a duplicated ritual spread across two structurally-parallel loops with identical preprocess and nearly-identical header construction.
- **Reachability**: latent copy-paste drift vector on an internal-only function boundary. No current live divergence — both loops at HEAD build the header identically. The value is structural: collapsing the header construction into one exported helper makes the three drift surfaces properties of one function rather than conventions spread across two loops with identical preprocess. The copy-paste mirror shape was the specific drift target: future edits that touch ONE loop without the other are the canonical way these parallel fragments disagree over time.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `formatPenaltySectionPrefix(entityLabel: string, health: ProviderHealth | ModelRouteHealth): string[]` directly before `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`, with a ~80-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (header constant, state label derivation, until formatter) and explaining why the helper returns a `string[]` rather than a newline-joined string (so the caller can extend it with section-specific body lines before the final `join("\n")` — this keeps the provider loop's "Curated fallbacks..." tail and the route loop's "Curated fallback for..." tail at the call sites where they belong). The helper body is a two-element array literal returning `[PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, \`${entityLabel} [${healthStateLabel(health.state)}] until ${formatHealthExpiry(health.until)}.\`]`. The `entityLabel` parameter (e.g. `"Provider openrouter"` or `"Route openrouter/foo"`) is the caller's responsibility because `ProviderHealth` and `ModelRouteHealth` are structurally identical and the helper cannot infer the right prefix from the health shape alone. Rewired the provider loop from `const label = ...; const until = ...; sections.push([PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, \`Provider ${providerID} [${label}] until ${until}.\`, ...].join("\n"))` to `sections.push([...formatPenaltySectionPrefix(\`Provider ${providerID}\`, health), "Curated fallbacks...", ...fallbackLines].join("\n"))` with an M91 comment. Rewired the route loop from `const label = ...; const until = ...; const header = [PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER, \`Route ${routeKey} [${label}] until ${until}.\`];` to `const header = formatPenaltySectionPrefix(\`Route ${routeKey}\`, health);` with an M91 comment. Both loops now share one source of truth for the header-constant-and-preprocess policy.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `collectAgentVisibleLivePenalties_*` cluster. `_whenCalled_containsProviderQuotaStatusHeader` pins the header constant by asserting `result.includes("## Provider health status")` — a sabotage that drops the header element fires this pin alone because pins 2 and 3 use `result.find((line) => line.startsWith("Provider openrouter"))` on the synopsis line, which is insensitive to the header's presence. `_whenStateIsQuota_synopsisContainsQuotaBackoffLabel` pins the `healthStateLabel` call by asserting the synopsis line contains `[QUOTA BACKOFF]` — a sabotage that interpolates raw `health.state` produces `[quota]` and fires this pin alone. `_whenUntilIsFinite_synopsisContainsISO8601String` pins the `formatHealthExpiry` call by asserting the synopsis contains `new Date(1700000000000).toISOString()` (i.e. `"2023-11-14T22:13:20.000Z"`) — a sabotage that interpolates raw `health.until` produces the literal string `"1700000000000"` and fires this pin alone. The three pins partition the drift space by substring target: pin 1 checks the header element via `.includes` on the array, pins 2 and 3 check substrings within the synopsis line via `.find + .includes`, and the three target substrings (the header banner, the `[QUOTA BACKOFF]` label, the ISO string) are all independent — touching one leaves the other two intact.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly one of my three pins. Sabotage A (drop the `PROVIDER_QUOTA_STATUS_HEADER` element from the array literal — the "refactor deletes the header constant" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenCalled_containsProviderQuotaStatusHeader` (pin 1). Pins 2 and 3 still passed because both operate on the synopsis line via `.find((line) => line.startsWith("Provider openrouter"))`, which finds the synopsis regardless of whether the header is present. Sabotage B (interpolate raw `health.state` instead of `healthStateLabel(health.state)` — the "refactor drops the state label mapping" drift class): `bun test` reported **1 expected failure** on pin 2 — `_whenStateIsQuota_synopsisContainsQuotaBackoffLabel` — PLUS 2 pre-existing integration tests in `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_*` that legitimately assert the same label (additive public-surface coverage, not a partition violation). Pins 1 and 2 still passed because the header and state label derivation are untouched. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin substring split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings among the new pins, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **277/277 pass** (274 pre-M91 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `formatPenaltySectionPrefix` export with full docstring directly before `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`; provider-loop and route-loop rewrites inside `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` both replacing the inline `const label = ...; const until = ...;` preprocess and header construction with one helper call, M91 comments at both sites), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `formatPenaltySectionPrefix` import after `findCuratedFallbackRoute`, three new unit pins directly before the `collectAgentVisibleLivePenalties_*` cluster).

### M90: the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` function opened its body with two structurally-identical `Array.from(map.entries()).filter(([, health]) => isAgentVisibleLivePenalty(health, now))` expressions (provider map + route map) followed by a `both empty → null` early-return gate — three drift surfaces (provider filter, route filter, both-empty null sentinel) all lived as conventions across four lines of inline code in two parallel branches rather than as single-site properties of one helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` function in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` opened its body with two structurally-identical inline filter expressions: `const activeProviderPenalties = Array.from(providerHealthMap.entries()).filter(([, health]) => isAgentVisibleLivePenalty(health, now));` immediately followed by `const activeRoutePenalties = Array.from(modelRouteHealthMap.entries()).filter(([, health]) => isAgentVisibleLivePenalty(health, now));` and a third inline guard `if (activeProviderPenalties.length === 0 && activeRoutePenalties.length === 0) return null;`. Three independent drift surfaces lived on that fragment: (1) the PROVIDER-side filter gates the entire provider section of the system prompt — a refactor that drops the filter expression (or leaves `Array.from(providerHealthMap.entries())` without the `.filter(...)` call, easy to miss during a "simplification" pass where the filter looks like dead destructuring) silently dumps every `key_missing` entry into the system prompt. Post-M58 every cold start installs `key_missing` for every uncredentialed curated provider (typically 15–25 entries), so the agent would see a 15-section wall of `Provider X [KEY MISSING] until never` on every single message — exactly the noise pre-M58 intentionally hid. Already-expired entries would also leak in because the filter drops them via `until > now`. (2) The ROUTE-side filter is a structural mirror of surface 1, on a different map, with an identical failure mode — dump expired/permanent route-level penalties into the system prompt. The mirror shape makes this surface the classic "copy-paste drift target": a refactor touches the provider filter and forgets the route filter (or vice versa), leaving the two branches out of sync with opposite filter policies — an asymmetric drift the mirror-test structure is specifically designed to catch. (3) The `both empty → null` early-return gate is load-bearing — the outer `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook depends on `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` returning `null` when there is nothing to report (via `assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts`'s null filter — M87). A refactor that drops the gate and always returns a non-null string (e.g. an empty header) would cause the transform hook to push an empty provider-health prompt into `output.system` on every message with no penalties, adding a useless header section and wasting the agent's attention on a "nothing is broken right now" preamble. The three surfaces were a duplicated ritual spread across four lines in two parallel branches — no single source of truth for the filter-and-null-gate policy.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — both filters at HEAD are correct and the null gate fires as intended. The value is structural: collapsing the two filters and the early-return gate into one exported helper makes the three drift surfaces properties of one function rather than conventions spread across four lines of inline code in two structurally-parallel branches. The helper returns the two filtered entry lists as a tagged `{providers, routes}` object so the call site can destructure with the original variable names and keep the rest of `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`'s body byte-identical — the provider-section for-loop and the route-section for-loop both continue to iterate `activeProviderPenalties` / `activeRoutePenalties` with no other changes.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `collectAgentVisibleLivePenalties(providerHealthMap: Map<string, ProviderHealth>, modelRouteHealthMap: Map<string, ModelRouteHealth>, now: number): {providers: Array<[string, ProviderHealth]>; routes: Array<[string, ModelRouteHealth]>} | null` directly before `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`, with a ~70-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (provider filter, route filter, both-empty null sentinel) and explaining why the helper returns a tagged tuple-object rather than two separate results (so the single `Date.now()` call at the hook entry point is consistent across both filters and the null-gate decision is centralized). Rewired `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`'s opening fragment from the two inline filter expressions + the `both.length === 0 && both.length === 0` gate to `const penalties = collectAgentVisibleLivePenalties(...); if (penalties === null) return null; const { providers: activeProviderPenalties, routes: activeRoutePenalties } = penalties;` with an M90 comment pointing at the helper docstring. The original variable names are preserved via destructuring rename, so the downstream for-loops iterating `activeProviderPenalties` and `activeRoutePenalties` stay byte-identical.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `buildProviderHealthSummaryForTool_*` cluster. `_whenOnlyProviderMapHasLiveEntry_returnsProvidersOnly` pins the provider filter with a two-entry provider map (one live `quota` + one `key_missing`) and an empty route map, asserting `result.providers.length === 1` with the live entry surviving and `result.routes.length === 0`. `_whenOnlyRouteMapHasLiveEntry_returnsRoutesOnly` is the structural mirror with a two-entry route map (one live `quota` + one `key_missing`) and an empty provider map, asserting the symmetric shape. `_whenBothMapsEmpty_returnsNullSentinel` pins the null-gate policy with two FULLY empty maps, asserting `result === null`. The three pins partition the drift space by which input has content: pin 1 exercises only the provider filter (route map empty, so the route filter is a no-op), pin 2 exercises only the route filter (provider map empty), and pin 3 exercises only the null-gate policy (both maps empty so both filters are no-ops and the gate is the only reachable logic). The empty-map input for pin 3 is deliberate — an earlier draft used a non-empty map with all-filtered entries, which caused pin 3 to fire collaterally on sabotage A (dropping the provider filter leaked the `key_missing` entry through, producing a non-null result and failing pin 3's null expectation). Switching pin 3 to empty maps isolates the null-gate surface cleanly.

### M89: the `recommend_model_for_role` tool's no-recommendation branch inlined a five-line `Object.fromEntries(Array.from(providerHealthMap.entries()).map(...))` expression rendering `{state, until: formatHealthExpiry(h.until)}` — three drift surfaces (state field, formatter call, no-filter policy) all lived as conventions on the inline JSON-builder rather than as single-site properties of one exported helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `recommend_model_for_role` tool handler's `if (!best)` no-recommendation branch in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined a five-line `Object.fromEntries(Array.from(providerHealthMap.entries()).map(([id, h]) => [id, { state: h.state, until: formatHealthExpiry(h.until) }]))` expression directly in the `JSON.stringify({...})` object literal. Three independent drift surfaces lived on that fragment: (1) the `state: h.state` field is the entire "what's broken" signal the agent reads in the no-recommendation branch — a refactor that renames the key (e.g. "status" or "penalty") or drops it outright silently produces a summary where every entry is `{ until: "..." }` with no indication of WHY each provider is penalized, which leaves the agent unable to distinguish "this one is rate-limited, try later" from "this one has no credentials, it will never work" from "this one is permanently dead until manual intervention". (2) The `formatHealthExpiry(h.until)` call is load-bearing — the helper converts raw epoch ms `number` into either an ISO-8601 string like `"2026-04-11T18:24:00.000Z"` or the sentinel `"never"` for `Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` (which is the `key_missing` permanent-plumbing marker used for every uncredentialed curated provider). A refactor that drops the formatter call and passes `h.until` raw into `JSON.stringify` silently emits unix epoch numbers for transient penalties and — worse — emits JSON `null` for permanent `key_missing` entries (because `JSON.stringify(Infinity) === "null"`), so the agent sees `"until": null` for the most important entries (the ones explaining "no credentials configured") and cannot distinguish them from "unknown expiry". (3) The summary is an UNFILTERED pass-through — unlike `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` which filters through `isAgentVisibleLivePenalty`, this rendering is a diagnostic "here is everything the plugin currently knows about every provider" dump intended to let the agent debug why no candidate model scored. A refactor that accidentally adds a filter — perhaps by copying from the sibling `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` which looks structurally identical — silently drops `key_missing` entries, which are EXACTLY the entries the agent most needs to see in the no-recommendation case (they explain "no credentials configured for this provider" far better than "this provider was healthy, try again" would). The three surfaces were a duplicated inline ritual with no single source of truth for the field shape, the formatter call, or the no-filter policy.
- **Reachability**: latent tool-output drift vector. No current live divergence — the inline expression at HEAD has all three properties correct. The value is structural: co-locating the field shape, the formatter call, and the no-filter policy in one exported helper makes the three drift surfaces properties of one function rather than conventions on a five-line JSON-builder. The helper is deliberately NOT collapsed with `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus`: that helper is for the `get_quota_backoff_status` tool (agent wants "what is LIVE right now?") and this helper is for the `recommend_model_for_role` no-recommendation branch (agent wants "what does the plugin currently know about every provider?"). The two have opposite filter semantics — one filters via `isAgentVisibleLivePenalty`, one passes everything through — and collapsing them would require a boolean parameter, which would itself be a new drift surface (`if (filterLivePenaltiesOnly)` ambiguity about which tool gets which behavior).
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `buildProviderHealthSummaryForTool(providerHealthMap: Map<string, ProviderHealth>): Record<string, { state: ProviderHealthState; until: string }>` directly after `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` and before `healthStateLabel`, with a ~65-line docstring enumerating the three drift surfaces (state field, formatter call, no-filter policy) and explaining why it is NOT collapsed with `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus`. The helper body is a six-line for-of loop over `providerHealthMap.entries()` that writes every entry with `state: health.state` and `until: formatHealthExpiry(health.until)` — no filter, no transformation of `state`, no transformation of `until` beyond the formatter call. Rewired the `recommend_model_for_role` tool call site from the five-line inline expression to `providerHealthSummary: buildProviderHealthSummaryForTool(providerHealthMap),` with an M89 comment pointing at the helper docstring. The `Object.fromEntries + Array.from + .map` composition is gone; the call site is now one expression in the JSON object literal.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_*` cluster. `_whenEntryPresent_preservesStateField` pins the state field with a single-entry map (`{state: "quota", until: 1700000000000, retryCount: 2}`) and asserts `result.provA?.state === "quota"` — a single-entry map so sabotages that filter entries still leave this entry present. `_whenEntryPresent_formatsUntilViaFormatHealthExpiry` pins the formatter call with the same single-entry map and asserts `result.provA?.until === new Date(1700000000000).toISOString()` — a single-entry map for the same reason. `_whenMapHasTwoEntries_preservesAllKeys` pins the no-filter policy with a TWO-entry map (`provA: quota` + `provB: key_missing` with `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY`) and asserts `Object.keys(result).sort() === ["provA", "provB"]` — the two-entry map with one live and one key_missing so ANY filter drop (whether targeting live or permanent) surfaces as a missing key. The three pins partition the drift space by scope: pin 1 and pin 2 operate on a single entry (insensitive to filters over entry count), pin 3 operates on the entry count (insensitive to per-entry field shape).
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. ### M88: the `event` hook's `session.error` branch carried five stacked inline narrowing gates (`!sessionError?.error`, `name !== "APIError"`, `?? 0` default on `statusCode`, `?? ""` default on `message`, `!sessionID` late gate) — the structurally-identical M84 drift class but on the sibling APIError-context read rather than the explicit-model read `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `event` hook's `session.error` branch in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` opened its APIError-context read with five stacked inline narrowing gates on an `unknown`-typed `sessionError` payload: `if (!sessionError?.error) return;`, `if (sessionError.error.name !== "APIError") return;`, `const statusCode = sessionError.error.data?.statusCode ?? 0;`, `const message = (sessionError.error.data?.message ?? "").toLowerCase();`, `const sessionID = sessionError.sessionID; if (!sessionID) return;`. Four independent drift surfaces lived on that fragment: (1) the error-type gate is the entire reason this branch exists — any refactor that relaxes `!== "APIError"` to `!= null` or drops it during a "simplification" pass silently starts classifying non-APIError payloads (NetworkError, TimeoutError, AbortError) as APIErrors and feeds them to downstream rate-limit / quota / 401 classifiers that assume the APIError shape. (2) The `?? 0` default on `statusCode` is load-bearing — a refactor that drops it leaves `statusCode` as `undefined` when the host omits `data.statusCode`, and the downstream `statusCode === 401` / `statusCode === 429` comparisons silently become `undefined === 401` (false, always) which silently disables the quota-exhaustion penalty path. (3) The `?? ""` default on `message` + immediate `.toLowerCase()` is load-bearing in a different way — a refactor that drops the default but keeps `.toLowerCase()` crashes on `undefined.toLowerCase()` the first time the host omits `data.message`, which is rare enough in production that the crash surfaces only under specific failure-mode combinations. (4) The `!sessionID` gate ordering matters — it currently comes AFTER the statusCode and message narrowing, which means a malformed payload missing `sessionID` still burns the statusCode / message parse before bailing; a refactor that moves the gate earlier "for performance" is a behavior-equivalent optimization, but a refactor that moves the APIError gate AFTER the sessionID gate inverts the semantic order of the two required fields and silently changes which drop-path a malformed payload takes. The five stacked gates were typed as `unknown` with cast-shaped reads at every level — the same "TypeScript-silent, runtime-silent, log-silent" drift class M84 closed on `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel` and M85 closed on `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload`, now on the sibling APIError-context read.
- **Reachability**: latent runtime-narrowing drift vector. No current live divergence — the five inline gates at HEAD are correct and structurally complete. The value is structural: co-locating the error-type gate, the two data-field defaults, and the sessionID gate in one runtime-narrowed helper makes the four drift surfaces properties of one exported function rather than conventions spread across five stacked inline checks on an `unknown` payload. This is the third member of the M84/M85/M88 mirror-drift trilogy — all three close the same narrowing-shape drift class on structurally-sibling opencode host events (session.error explicit-model read, assistant.message.completed tokens read, session.error APIError-context read).
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `extractSessionErrorApiErrorContext(sessionError: unknown): { sessionID: string; statusCode: number; lowerMessage: string } | undefined` directly after `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`, with a ~80-line docstring enumerating the four drift surfaces (error-type gate, statusCode default, message default + case-fold, sessionID gate ordering) and explaining why the helper pre-lowercases `message` at the helper boundary rather than leaving the `.toLowerCase()` at the call site (so every downstream string-match like `lowerMessage.includes("rate limit")` gets a guaranteed-lowercased string without the call site needing to remember the case-fold). The helper body is a six-step runtime narrowing: (1) `sessionError` is a non-null object, (2) `envelope.error` is a non-null object, (3) `errorObj.name === "APIError"`, (4) `envelope.sessionID` is a non-empty string, (5) `data` is a non-null object OR `{}`, (6) pull `statusCode` with `?? 0` and `message` with `?? ""` + lowercase, then return the narrowed `{sessionID, statusCode, lowerMessage}` tuple. Rewired the `session.error` branch call site from the five stacked gates to `const apiErrorContext = extractSessionErrorApiErrorContext(sessionError); if (apiErrorContext === undefined) return; const { sessionID, statusCode, lowerMessage: message } = apiErrorContext;` with an M88 comment pointing at the helper docstring. The downstream classifiers (rate-limit match, quota-exhaustion match, 401 match) continue to use `message` and `statusCode` unchanged — the rename-on-destructure from `lowerMessage` to `message` keeps the call-site variable name stable so the downstream string-match logic stays byte-identical.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel_*` cluster. `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` pins the full happy-path shape with `{error: {name: "APIError", data: {statusCode: 429, message: "Rate Limit EXCEEDED"}}, sessionID: "sess-1"}` and asserts `{sessionID: "sess-1", statusCode: 429, lowerMessage: "rate limit exceeded"}` — exercises the error-type gate (passes APIError), the sessionID gate (passes non-empty string), the statusCode path (passes number), and the message path (passes string + case-fold from mixed-case to fully lowercase). `_whenErrorNameIsWrong_returnsUndefined` pins the error-type gate with `{error: {name: "NotFoundError", data: {statusCode: 404}}, sessionID: "sess-1"}` and asserts `undefined`. `_whenSessionIDIsMissing_returnsUndefined` pins the sessionID gate with `{error: {name: "APIError", data: {}}}` (no sessionID field) and asserts `undefined`. The three pins partition the drift space by narrowing step: happy-path (exercises all four gates + both defaults + case-fold), error-type-gate failure, sessionID-gate failure.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (short-circuit helper body to `void sessionError; return undefined;` — the "refactor deletes the entire helper body" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` (267 pass, 1 fail). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because both expect `undefined` and a constant-undefined helper trivially satisfies them. Sabotage B (drop the `if (errorObj.name !== "APIError") return undefined;` gate — the "refactor relaxes the error-type check" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenErrorNameIsWrong_returnsUndefined` (267 pass, 1 fail). Pin 1 still passes (it uses APIError so the dropped gate is a no-op) and pin 3 still passes because the sessionID gate still catches the missing-sessionID case. Sabotage C (drop the `if (typeof envelope.sessionID !== "string" || envelope.sessionID.length === 0) return undefined;` gate — the "refactor drops the sessionID gate" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenSessionIDIsMissing_returnsUndefined` (267 pass, 1 fail). Pin 1 still passes (its sessionID is a valid non-empty string) and pin 2 still passes (its error-type gate catches the NotFoundError case before the sessionID check). Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin narrowing-step split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **268/268 pass** (265 pre-M88 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `extractSessionErrorApiErrorContext` export with full docstring directly after `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`; `session.error` hook branch call site rewrite with M88 comment replacing the five stacked inline narrowing gates), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `extractSessionErrorApiErrorContext` import sorted alphabetically between `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` and `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`, three new unit pins directly before the `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel_*` cluster).

Value is structural: the four drift surfaces on the `session.error` APIError-context read are now properties of one exported runtime-narrowed helper, completing the M84/M85/M88 mirror-drift trilogy on the opencode host event handlers.

### M87: the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook carried two near-identical inline `build*Prompt` + null-filter + push blocks for `providerHealthPrompt` and `availableModelsPrompt` — twelve lines of duplicated structure where four independent drift surfaces (order of the two prompts in `output.system`, provider-health null filter, available-models null filter, and asymmetric guard loss between the two blocks) all lived as conventions across two sites rather than as single-site properties of one helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` carried two twelve-line inline blocks with structurally-identical shape: `const providerHealthPrompt = buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt(modelRegistry.models, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now); if (providerHealthPrompt) { output.system.push(providerHealthPrompt); }` immediately followed by the same pattern for `availableModelsPrompt` / `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`. Four independent drift surfaces lived on that fragment: (1) the ORDER of the two prompts in `output.system` is semantic — provider-health describes "what's broken right now" and available-models describes "what to use instead"; a future refactor that swapped the two `push` calls silently inverts the prompt narrative the agent reads top-to-bottom, changing both first-hit salience and the framing of the fallback list, without any observable test-level or runtime failure. (2) The null filter on the provider-health block is load-bearing — `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` returns `string | null` and a refactor that drops the `if (...)` guard silently pushes `null` into `output.system` (typed as `string[]`), which corrupts the prompt rendering downstream in a way that surfaces only when an agent-visible penalty exists AND the renderer produces an empty body — a combination that's rare enough in production that regression tests on the two builders alone wouldn't catch it. (3) Same drift on the available-models block, mirror of surface 2. (4) The WORST failure mode: asymmetric guard loss. A refactor could delete the null guard on ONE block but keep it on the other, producing an arrangement where one builder's null output crashes the downstream renderer and the other silently tolerates it — the worst kind of inconsistency because it manifests only when one specific builder returns null, which means the bug is latent until a specific edge case triggers exactly that builder's null path. The twelve lines were a duplicated ritual with no single source of truth for the ordering-and-null-filter policy.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — the two inline blocks are in the correct order and both have null guards at HEAD. The value is structural: co-locating the ordering-and-null-filter policy in one helper makes the four drift surfaces properties of one exported function rather than conventions that happen to agree by coincidence across two twelve-line sites. The helper is kept as a post-filter pure function (takes `string | null` inputs, returns `string[]`) so the two builder invocations stay at the call site with their shared 4-arg registry+maps signatures visible and type-checked — the helper's job is the policy, not the builder invocation.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts(providerHealthPrompt: string | null, availableModelsPrompt: string | null): string[]` directly after `shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty`, with a ~60-line docstring enumerating the four drift surfaces (order, dual null filter, asymmetric guard loss) and explaining why the helper is a post-filter pure function rather than a full builder wrapper. The helper body is a six-line canonical ordering-and-null-filter: `const systemPrompts: string[] = []; if (providerHealthPrompt !== null) { systemPrompts.push(providerHealthPrompt); } if (availableModelsPrompt !== null) { systemPrompts.push(availableModelsPrompt); } return systemPrompts;`. Rewired the transform hook call site from the twelve-line fragment to `output.system.push(...assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts(buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt(...), buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt(...)));` with an M87 comment pointing at the helper docstring. The two builder invocations stay at the call site with their 4-arg registry+maps signatures type-checked by TypeScript.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty_*` cluster. `_whenBothPromptsPresent_returnsProviderFirst` pins the ordering policy with two non-null inputs and asserts `["PROVIDER_HEALTH_BODY", "AVAILABLE_MODELS_BODY"]` — provider-health FIRST, available-models SECOND. `_whenProviderHealthIsNull_returnsAvailableOnly` pins the provider-health null filter with `(null, "AVAILABLE_MODELS_BODY")` and asserts `["AVAILABLE_MODELS_BODY"]`. `_whenAvailableModelsIsNull_returnsProviderOnly` pins the available-models null filter with `("PROVIDER_HEALTH_BODY", null)` and asserts `["PROVIDER_HEALTH_BODY"]`. The three pins partition the drift space by input shape: both-non-null (exercises order), provider-null (exercises left null filter), available-null (exercises right null filter). The asymmetric guard loss surface is caught by either of pins 2 or 3 depending on which side the refactor drops.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (reverse the push order — push `availableModelsPrompt` first, then `providerHealthPrompt` — the "refactor reorders the two blocks" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenBothPromptsPresent_returnsProviderFirst` (order inverted to `["AVAILABLE", "PROVIDER"]` instead of `["PROVIDER", "AVAILABLE"]`). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because each has only one non-null element so the length-1 array is insensitive to order. Sabotage B (drop the provider-health null filter — `systemPrompts.push(providerHealthPrompt as string);` unconditionally — the "refactor deletes the left guard" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenProviderHealthIsNull_returnsAvailableOnly` (length-1 array became `[null, "AVAILABLE"]` which the deepEqual assertion reported as a mismatch). Pin 1 still passes because its provider-health is non-null and the filter is a no-op; pin 3 still passes because its provider-health is non-null. Sabotage C (drop the available-models null filter — mirror of sabotage B): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenAvailableModelsIsNull_returnsProviderOnly` (same mismatch on the right side). Pin 1 still passes (both non-null) and pin 2 still passes (available-models non-null). Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin input-shape split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **265/265 pass** (262 pre-M87 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts` export with full docstring directly after `shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty`; transform hook call site rewrite with M87 comment replacing the twelve-line fragment), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `assembleHealthAwareSystemPrompts` import sorted into the existing import block, three new unit pins directly before the `shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty_*` cluster).

No production behavior change at HEAD — the helper produces the exact same `output.system` contents the inline fragment produced. Value is structural: the ordering-and-null-filter policy is now a single-site property of one exported function, the asymmetric guard loss surface is closed, and three dedicated regression tests pin each drift axis independently.

### M86: the `chat.params` hook carried an inline `if (timeoutMs < 1000) { ... const providerID = ...; const model = ...; if (providerID && model) { recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers(...) } }` branch — a magic-literal threshold (`1000` with no named constant), an implicit `<` boundary, and a triple-nested identifier guard on a "test-mode short-path" whose semantics lived only in a one-line comment and a reference buried in `parseHangTimeoutMs`'s docstring `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` carried an immediate-penalty branch gated on `if (timeoutMs < 1000)`. Inside the branch, `const providerID = input.provider.info.id; const model = input.model; if (providerID && model) { recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers(..., "timeout", ...) }` — a triple-nested structure that spelled out the full gate policy inline with zero encapsulation. The `1000` literal was a bare magic number; the `<` vs `<=` boundary was implicit; and the `&& providerID && model` guard was nested one level inside the threshold check with no docstring. The branch existed purely as a test-mode short-path (referenced in `parseHangTimeoutMs`'s docstring as the `< 1000` semantic marker), but the call site gave no indication that the literal was load-bearing — a future developer seeing `if (timeoutMs < 1000)` with no named constant might reasonably tune it (`< 100`? `< 500`?) or delete it as "probably dead test scaffolding" without realizing it's a deliberately-preserved test affordance referenced by another module's docstring. Three distinct drift surfaces in one 15-line branch: (1) magic literal `1000` has no named constant, so a future tuning or deletion silently changes which env-var values take the test-mode path and which production sessions enter it accidentally on a misconfigured `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS`; (2) the `<` boundary is implicit and could be flipped to `<=` during a perfectly-ordinary "off-by-one fix" refactor that silently changes the `1000ms` edge case from "production" to "test-mode immediate-penalty"; (3) the triple-nested `threshold && hasProviderID && hasModel` policy is spread across two `if` blocks, so a refactor that pulls the identifier narrowing out of the branch could drop either `providerID` or `model` from the gate and start calling `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` with undefined positional arguments, which either crashes the test harness or silently writes penalties keyed on `"provider/undefined"` in the route-health map.
- **Reachability**: latent policy-drift vector with three independent axes. No current live divergence — the inline branch works at HEAD because production never sets `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS` below `1000`, the `<` boundary is never reached at runtime (default is 900000), and the nested identifier guard holds at HEAD because opencode always populates both fields before `chat.params` fires. The value is structural: naming the threshold (`HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS`) makes its relationship to `parseHangTimeoutMs`'s docstring a property of the export graph instead of a comment-link; the predicate helper (`shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty`) collapses the three-way AND into one call-site conditional whose three inputs map 1:1 to the three drift surfaces; and the three-pin asymmetric test split pins each AND-term independently so a sabotage that drops any single conjunct fires exactly one pin.
- **Fix**: extracted two new exports directly after `parseHangTimeoutMs`. `HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS = 1000` with a ~20-line docstring explicitly enumerating the three drift surfaces (magic literal, implicit `<`, triple-nested gate) and citing the `parseHangTimeoutMs` cross-reference. `shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty(rawTimeoutMs: number, hasProviderID: boolean, hasModel: boolean): boolean` with a ~30-line docstring enumerating the failure mode of dropping each AND conjunct (drop threshold → every session penalized on entry, drop providerID → undefined key, drop model → `"provider/undefined"` composite key). The helper body is exactly `return rawTimeoutMs < HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS && hasProviderID && hasModel;`. Rewired the `chat.params` call site from the inline 15-line branch to `const immediateProviderID = input.provider.info.id; const immediateModel = input.model; if (shouldRecordImmediateTimeoutPenalty(timeoutMs, Boolean(immediateProviderID), Boolean(immediateModel))) { recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, immediateProviderID, immediateModel.id, ...) }` with an M86 comment pointing at the helper docstring. The identifier narrowing stays at the call site so the `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` positional arguments remain visible — the helper's job is the predicate, not the record call.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload_*` cluster. `_whenAllConditionsHold_returnsTrue` pins the happy path with `(THRESHOLD - 500, true, true)` → `true`. `_whenProviderIDIsMissing_returnsFalse` pins the dropped-providerID drift with `(THRESHOLD - 500, false, true)` → `false`. `_whenModelIsMissing_returnsFalse` pins the dropped-model drift with `(THRESHOLD - 500, true, false)` → `false`. All three pins reference `HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS` by name so a future threshold change is caught by the test import if the constant is renamed. The three pins partition the AND conjunct space: all-three-hold, drop-providerID-conjunct, drop-model-conjunct. The threshold-conjunct is the happy path inverted — a sabotage that hardcodes the timeout comparison to always-false fires pin 1 alone because pins 2 and 3 already expect false.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (`void rawTimeoutMs; return 2000 < HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS && hasProviderID && hasModel;` — the "hardcode the timeoutMs comparison to always-false" drift class, simulating a mis-tuned threshold or a refactor that accidentally drops the timeout input): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenAllConditionsHold_returnsTrue` (happy path input returned false because `2000 < 1000` short-circuits the AND). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because their expected value is already false and the AND still short-circuits on the other conjuncts. Sabotage B (`void hasProviderID; return rawTimeoutMs < HANG_TIMEOUT_IMMEDIATE_THRESHOLD_MS && hasModel;` — the "drop the providerID conjunct" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenProviderIDIsMissing_returnsFalse` (missing-providerID input incorrectly returned true because the `&& hasProviderID` gate was removed). Pin 1 still passes because all three inputs hold; pin 3 still passes because the model conjunct still catches the missing-model case. Pin 1 still passes because all three inputs hold; pin 2 still passes because the providerID conjunct still catches the missing-providerID case.
