### M85: the `assistant.message.completed` branch inside the plugin's `event` hook opened with stacked `(event as any).type === "..."` and `const props = (event as any).properties as any;` casts before trusting `props.sessionID` and `props.tokens` as raw reads — a runtime-unsound narrowing mirror-drift of the M84 `session.error` handler bug, where an opencode host release that renamed `sessionID`, wrapped `tokens` inside a nested envelope, or promoted it to a tagged union would silently deliver a malformed or `undefined` value into `readAndClearSessionHangState` and the `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` classifier with zero thrown error `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `event` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` opened the `assistant.message.completed` branch with `if ((event as any).type === "assistant.message.completed") { const props = (event as any).properties as any; const sessionID = props.sessionID; if (!sessionID) return; const tokens = props.tokens; if (!tokens) return; ... }`. Two stacked `as any` casts on one call site, followed by raw field reads with truthy-falsy gates that catch `undefined` but would silently accept any other malformed shape (empty-string sessionID, array-shaped tokens, number tokens). Exactly the same "TypeScript-silent, runtime-silent, log-silent" drift class M84 closed on the `session.error` handler — the opencode host does not export a stable TypeScript shape for `assistant.message.completed`, and the plugin simply trusts whatever the cast produces. Two concrete drift surfaces: (1) a future opencode release that renames `sessionID` → `session_id`, wraps the payload in `properties.message.tokens`, or promotes `tokens` to a tagged union silently delivers a malformed object into `readAndClearSessionHangState` (which does a `Map.get` on the session-id key and returns undefined bindings), collapsing the whole zero-token quota-exhaustion classification pass to a silent no-op; (2) a future refactor that spreads `{...props}` verbatim loses the implicit `!sessionID` / `!tokens` guards, pushing `undefined` through the classifier and either skipping legitimate quota penalties or applying them against undefined provider/model bindings. Both modes corrupt route-health telemetry with zero observable error. The bug is structurally identical to M84 on a sibling event branch — same fix pattern, same drift class, different event.
- **Reachability**: latent runtime-narrowing drift vector, mirror of M84. No current live divergence — opencode at HEAD ships `{type, properties: {sessionID, tokens}}` on the field and the stacked casts work by accident. The value is structural: replacing the casts with an explicit narrow pins the expected shape as a property of one helper with a documented drift-shape, and a future host change that breaks the shape is caught by the runtime guards returning `undefined` (causing the `if (completedPayload !== undefined)` block to skip entirely) instead of propagating a malformed object into the classification ladder. Co-locating this helper next to `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel` makes the `session.error` / `assistant.message.completed` pair a visible "both event handlers use runtime-narrowed payload helpers" convention rather than one-fixed-one-cast asymmetry.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload(event: unknown): { sessionID: string; tokens: Record<string, unknown> } | undefined` directly after `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`, with a ~50-line docstring explicitly calling out the mirror-drift relationship to M84 and enumerating the two drift surfaces (host field-shape change and spread-refactor guard loss). The helper body is a five-step defensive ladder: (1) event object shape check, (2) `type === "assistant.message.completed"` check (moves the branch tag inside the helper so the call site is a single conditional), (3) `properties` object check, (4) `sessionID` string-and-non-empty check (tighter than the old `!sessionID` truthy gate which would have accepted `0` or `false` from a future numeric id), (5) `tokens` object check. Any failure returns `undefined`. Rewired the call site from `if ((event as any).type === ...) { const props = ...; ... }` to `const completedPayload = extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload(event); if (completedPayload !== undefined) { const { sessionID, tokens } = completedPayload; ... }` with an M85 comment pointing at the helper docstring and the M84 mirror-drift relationship. Also dropped the now-redundant `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal(tokens as Record<string, unknown>)` cast — `tokens` is already narrowed by the helper return type.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel_*` cluster. `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` pins the happy path with a realistic `assistant.message.completed` envelope (`type`, `properties: {sessionID, tokens: {input, output, reasoning, cache: {read, write}}}`) and asserts the helper returns the narrowed `{sessionID, tokens}` literal. `_whenSessionIDIsMissing_returnsUndefined` pins the dropped-sessionID drift by passing `{type, properties: {tokens}}` and asserts `undefined`. `_whenTokensIsMissing_returnsUndefined` pins the dropped-tokens drift by passing `{type, properties: {sessionID}}` and asserts `undefined`. The three pins partition the narrowing ladder by step: valid-all-steps, drop-sessionID-check, drop-tokens-check.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (`void event; return undefined;` — the "helper never returns a value" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` (valid input returned undefined). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because their expected value is already undefined. Sabotage B (dropped the `sessionID` string check while keeping the `tokens` check — the "drop a single narrowing step" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenSessionIDIsMissing_returnsUndefined` (missing-sessionID input incorrectly returned `{sessionID: undefined, tokens: {...}}`). Pin 1 passes because the happy path still has both fields; pin 3 passes because the tokens check still catches the missing-tokens case. Sabotage C (dropped the `tokens` object check while keeping the `sessionID` string check — the mirror drift): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenTokensIsMissing_returnsUndefined` (missing-tokens input incorrectly returned `{sessionID: "sess-1", tokens: undefined}`). Pin 1 passes because the happy path still has both fields; pin 2 passes because the sessionID check still catches the missing-sessionID case. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin narrowing-step split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **259/259 pass** (256 pre-M85 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` export with full docstring directly after `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`; `assistant.message.completed` branch rewrite with M85 comment; redundant `as Record<string, unknown>` cast removed from `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` call), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `extractAssistantMessageCompletedPayload` import sorted alphabetically between `classifyPersistedHealthKey` and `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel`, three new unit pins directly before the `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel_*` cluster).

Value is structural: a future host field-shape change is caught by the guards returning `undefined` (skipping the classification block) instead of propagating a malformed object into `readAndClearSessionHangState` and `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal`. Pairs with M84 as the "both event branches use runtime-narrowed payload helpers" convention.

### M84: the `session.error` event handler inside the plugin's `event` hook trusted `sessionError.model` via an `(sessionError as any).model` cast — a runtime-unsound narrowing that assumed opencode always delivers a `{ id, providerID }` tuple on the field, where a host release that changed the payload shape (wrapped it in `model: { current: {...} }`, renamed to `modelID/providerID`, or dropped the field on non-API-error branches) would silently deliver a malformed or `undefined` value into the classification ladder and corrupt route-health penalties with no thrown error `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` handler in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` opened classification with `const model = (sessionError as any).model ?? mappedModel;`. The `as any` cast is the drift surface: the opencode host does not currently export a stable TypeScript shape for the `session.error` event's `model` field, and the plugin simply trusts that whatever shows up on the field is a `{ id, providerID }` object (or missing). Two concrete drift surfaces: (1) if a future opencode release wraps the payload (`sessionError.model.current`) or renames fields (`modelID`/`providerID`), the cast silently delivers a malformed object into `modelID = model?.id` and the whole route-health classification ladder collapses to id-undefined branches without any runtime error; (2) if a host release drops the field on non-API-error branches, the `?? mappedModel` fallback masks it at the call site but any future refactor that inlines the fallback differently loses the defense with no warning. Both modes corrupt route-health penalties (`recordModelNotFoundRouteHealthByIdentifiers`, `recordRateLimitRouteHealthByIdentifiers`, quota backoffs) with zero observable error — the `as any` cast produces `TypeScript-silent, runtime-silent, log-silent` drift.
- **Reachability**: latent runtime-narrowing drift vector. No current live divergence — opencode at HEAD ships `{ id, providerID }` on the field and the `as any` cast works by accident. The value is structural: replacing the cast with an explicit narrow pins the expected shape as a property of one helper with a documented drift-shape, and a future host change that breaks the shape is caught by the runtime guards returning `undefined` (forcing the `?? mappedModel` path) instead of propagating a malformed object into the classification ladder.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel(sessionError: unknown): { id: string; providerID: string } | undefined` directly after `parseHangTimeoutMs`, with a ~50-line docstring enumerating the two drift surfaces (host field-shape change and dropped-field masking) and explaining why the `?? mappedModel` fallback is kept visible at the call site (the policy decision — explicit vs mapped — is a site-local decision, not a helper concern). The helper body is a four-step defensive ladder: (1) object shape check, (2) `model` field object check, (3) `id` string check, (4) `providerID` string check. Any failure returns `undefined`. Rewired the `session.error` handler from `const model = (sessionError as any).model ?? mappedModel;` to `const model = extractSessionErrorExplicitModel(sessionError) ?? mappedModel;` with an M84 comment pointing at the helper docstring for the drift-shape rationale.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `classifyPersistedHealthKey_*` cluster. `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` pins the happy path with a realistic `session.error` envelope (`sessionID`, `error`, `model: { id, providerID }`) and asserts the helper returns the narrowed `{id, providerID}` literal. `_whenModelIsMissingId_returnsUndefined` pins the dropped-id drift by passing `{model: {providerID: "openrouter"}}` and asserts `undefined`. `_whenModelIsMissingProviderID_returnsUndefined` pins the dropped-providerID drift by passing `{model: {id: "claude-3.5-sonnet"}}` and asserts `undefined`. The three pins partition the narrowing ladder by step: valid-all-steps, drop-id-check, drop-providerID-check.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (`void sessionError; return undefined;` — the "helper never returns a value" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenShapeIsValid_returnsNarrowedTuple` (valid input returned undefined). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because their expected value is already undefined. Sabotage B (dropped the `id` check while keeping the `providerID` check — the "drop a single narrowing step" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenModelIsMissingId_returnsUndefined` (missing-id input incorrectly returned `{id: undefined, providerID: "openrouter"}`). Pin 1 passes because the happy path still has both fields; pin 3 passes because the providerID check still catches the missing-providerID case. Sabotage C (dropped the `providerID` check while keeping the `id` check — the mirror drift): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenModelIsMissingProviderID_returnsUndefined` (missing-providerID input incorrectly returned `{id: "claude-3.5-sonnet", providerID: undefined}`). Pin 1 passes because the happy path still has both fields; pin 2 passes because the id check still catches the missing-id case. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin narrowing-step split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **256/256 pass** (253 pre-M84 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel` export with full docstring directly after `parseHangTimeoutMs`; `session.error` handler rewrite with M84 comment), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `extractSessionErrorExplicitModel` import sorted alphabetically between `classifyPersistedHealthKey` and `findRegistryEntryByModel`, three new unit pins directly before the `classifyPersistedHealthKey_*` cluster).

Value is structural: a future host field-shape change is caught by the guards returning `undefined` (forcing the `?? mappedModel` path) instead of propagating a malformed object into the classification ladder.

### M83: `loadPersistedProviderHealth` classified each persisted JSON key as provider-level or route-level with an inline `const isRouteKey = key.includes("/")` predicate — the `/` delimiter convention was implicitly coupled to `composeRouteKey` with no shared code, so a future change to `composeRouteKey`'s delimiter (or a plausible "tighten to exactly-one-slash" refactor of the inline predicate) would silently corrupt on-disk health state on every plugin restart by routing half the entries into the wrong in-memory map with no validation error `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `loadPersistedProviderHealth` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` classified each key from the flat `providerHealth.json` document with an inline `const isRouteKey = key.includes("/")` check before deciding whether to route the parsed entry into `providerHealthMap` or `modelRouteHealthMap`. The predicate relies on the convention that `composeRouteKey` always inserts a `/` between provider and model while raw provider IDs never contain one — but that convention lives in two places at once (the `composeRouteKey` body, ~180 lines upstream, and the inline predicate in the loader) with no shared code connecting them. Two concrete drift surfaces: (1) if a future maintainer changes `composeRouteKey` to use a different delimiter (`::`, `|`, `#` — all plausible if a provider id ever legitimately contains a `/` character, e.g. a scoped npm-style namespace like `@foo/bar`), the inline `.includes("/")` check silently keeps returning `false` for every new-form route key, and every route-level penalty gets re-hydrated into the provider map on restart; (2) a future refactor that "tightens" the predicate to `key.split("/").length === 2` — a plausible narrowing that reads as "expect exactly provider + model" — would silently misclassify every multi-segment route key (e.g. `"openrouter/anthropic/claude-3.5-sonnet"`, which `composeRouteKey` produces when the opencode runtime model id already contains a slash for aggregator-routed models) as a provider ID. Either failure mode corrupts both halves of the health state on plugin restart with zero validation error: `JSON.parse` succeeds, `parsePersistedHealthEntry` succeeds, the misclassified entries land in the wrong map, and every subsequent read against `modelRouteHealthMap` / `providerHealthMap` silently misses. The persisted `retryCount` values are preserved but every live backoff window becomes invisible to the writer/reader pairs M68/M73 were built to protect.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector with a high-blast-radius failure mode. No current live divergence — `composeRouteKey` still uses `/` and the inline predicate still matches. The value is structural: co-locating the classification next to `composeRouteKey` makes the delimiter convention a property of one logical unit in the file rather than two independent sites that happen to agree by convention. A named helper also pins the multi-segment case explicitly: the three-pin test split includes a round-trip through `composeRouteKey` so a future edit to the composite-key builder is caught by a concrete assertion failure rather than a silent re-hydration bug that only surfaces on the next plugin restart after real traffic re-populates the route map.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `classifyPersistedHealthKey(persistedKey: string): "provider" | "route"` directly after `composeRouteKey` with a ~50-line docstring enumerating the two drift surfaces (delimiter-change silent breakage and split-length tightening silent misclassification), the co-location rationale, and the `composeRouteKey` round-trip convention. The helper body is exactly one line: `return persistedKey.includes("/") ? "route" : "provider";`. Rewired the inline `.includes("/")` check in `loadPersistedProviderHealth` to `if (classifyPersistedHealthKey(key) === "route") { ... }` with an M83 comment documenting the consolidation and pointing at the helper docstring for the drift-shape rationale. The helper is a discriminated-string return rather than a boolean so the caller reads as `classifyPersistedHealthKey(key) === "route"` instead of `isRouteKey(key)` — the string discriminant makes the call site self-documenting and mirrors the idiom TypeScript narrows on naturally.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel_*` cluster. `_whenKeyHasNoSlash_returnsProvider` pins the no-slash case with two provider IDs (`"iflowcn"`, `"ollama-cloud"`). `_whenKeyHasExactlyOneSlash_returnsRoute` pins the standard 2-segment composite case with two keys (`"iflowcn/qwen3-coder-plus"`, `"ollama-cloud/glm-5"`). `_whenKeyHasMultipleSlashes_returnsRoute` pins the multi-segment case with a literal 3-segment key AND a round-trip through `composeRouteKey({provider: "openrouter", model: "meta/llama-3-70b"})` — the round-trip asserts the classifier is consistent with the composite-key builder so any future edit to `composeRouteKey` that changes the delimiter surfaces as a concrete test failure here. The three pins partition the space by slash count: 0 slashes, exactly 1 slash, 2+ slashes. The partition is the critical design choice — it produces a clean asymmetric-sabotage cascade.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin. Sabotage A (`return "route"` — the "hardcode route bucket" drift class that a merge conflict or careless refactor could produce): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenKeyHasNoSlash_returnsProvider` (both provider IDs classified as "route"). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass because their expected value is already "route". Sabotage B (`return persistedKey.split("/").length > 2 ? "route" : "provider"` — the "require 2+ slashes" tightening drift class that would reject standard 2-segment composite keys): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenKeyHasExactlyOneSlash_returnsRoute` (both 2-segment keys misclassified as "provider"). Pin 1 passes because its 0-slash keys still return "provider"; pin 3 passes because its 3-segment keys pass the `> 2` check. Sabotage C (`return persistedKey.split("/").length === 2 ? "route" : "provider"` — the "require exactly 1 slash" tightening drift class that would reject multi-segment composite keys): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenKeyHasMultipleSlashes_returnsRoute` (both 3-segment keys misclassified as "provider"). Pin 1 passes because its 0-slash keys still return "provider"; pin 2 passes because its 2-segment keys match the `=== 2` check. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin slash-count split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings, every pin caught by at least one sabotage. Restored the fix, **253/253 pass** (250 pre-M83 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `classifyPersistedHealthKey` export with full docstring directly after `composeRouteKey`; `loadPersistedProviderHealth` inline `.includes("/")` rewrite with M83 comment), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `classifyPersistedHealthKey` import sorted alphabetically at the top of the import block, three new unit pins directly before the `loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel_*` cluster).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated classifier. No production behavior change — the helper produces the exact same `"route"`/`"provider"` discrimination as the inline predicate at HEAD. Value is structural: the "is this persisted JSON key a composite route key or a raw provider ID?" classification is now a single-site property documented alongside `composeRouteKey`, and a future delimiter change to the composite-key builder is caught by the round-trip pin before it can silently corrupt on-disk health state.

### M82: the `chat.params` and `experimental.chat.system.transform` hooks both inlined the same two-step `loadModelRegistry + findRegistryEntryByModel` ritual with an identical `{ id: input.model.id, providerID: input.model.providerID }` narrowing — a drift surface where a future refactor that spread `{...input.model}` verbatim in one hook while the other kept the explicit narrow would begin comparing different subsets of the runtime model against the registry, and a refactor that dropped `providerID` from one side would silently collapse lookup to id-only and false-positive match the first curated entry sharing that model id, injecting the wrong temperature override or the wrong routing-context system prompt with no observable error `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` opened with `const modelRegistry = await loadModelRegistry(CONTROL_PLANE_ROOT_DIRECTORY);` followed immediately by `const modelRegistryEntry = findRegistryEntryByModel(modelRegistry.models, { id: input.model.id, providerID: input.model.providerID });`. The `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook opened with the textually-identical pair (modulo an intervening `expireHealthMaps` call, which does not touch the registry). Two sites, same two-step ritual, same hand-written narrowing of `input.model` to a `{ id, providerID }` literal. Nothing at HEAD produces divergent behavior, but the pattern is a drift surface with an especially bad failure mode: opencode's runtime `input.model` currently carries exactly `{ id, providerID }`, but nothing stops a future opencode release from growing fields (pricing, context window, tokenizer handle) and nothing stops a future refactor from spreading `{...input.model}` verbatim in ONE hook while the OTHER keeps the explicit narrow. The two sites would then compare different subsets of the runtime model against the registry, and `findRegistryEntryByModel` — which normalizes both sides via `composeRouteKey` on `{provider, model}` — would only read the two fields it expects, so the spread would be silently tolerated at one site but the two sites would drift apart on future-field handling. Worse still: a refactor that dropped the `providerID` field from ONE site (because "input.model already has id and that's what we need for the lookup") would collapse lookup to id-only, which would match the first curated entry whose `provider_order[].model` id equals `input.model.id` regardless of provider, false-positive-matching any curated row that happened to share an id across providers (e.g. `gpt-oss:20b` exposed by multiple aggregators). The temperature override at the `chat.params` site and the routing-context system-prompt injection at the `experimental.chat.system.transform` site would both silently target the wrong registry entry with no thrown error and no observable telemetry.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — both inline blocks compile to the same runtime behavior today because opencode's `input.model` shape currently carries exactly `{ id, providerID }` and the two object literals are textually identical. The value is structural: the `{ id: input.model.id, providerID: input.model.providerID }` narrowing is the silent drift surface, not the `loadModelRegistry` call itself. A named helper moves the narrowing into one function body where a future opencode field growth is a single-site TypeScript-checked change, and where a test pin can directly assert the narrowing's semantics (provider mismatch must return undefined, not fall back to id-only matching). The helper also documents the contract that currently lives only as convention: "the two hooks share this load+narrow+lookup ritual and must keep lock-step narrowing forever." This is the same class of drift M75-M79 closed at the session-state and route-health layers, now applied to the registry-lookup layer.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported async helper `loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel(controlPlaneRootDirectory, inputModel, loadFn?): Promise<{ registry, entry }>` directly after `findRegistryEntryByModel` with a ~45-line docstring enumerating the drift shape, the false-positive match scenario, and the deliberate decision to return both `{ registry, entry }` (rather than just the entry) because the `experimental.chat.system.transform` site still needs `registry.models` three more times to build the provider-health and available-models prompts. The helper takes an injected `loadFn` defaulting to `loadModelRegistry` so tests can inject a fixture or throwing loader without disk I/O. The body is exactly three lines: `await loadFn(root)`, `findRegistryEntryByModel(registry.models, { id: inputModel.id, providerID: inputModel.providerID })`, and the tuple return. Rewired both call sites in the plugin body: `chat.params` collapses `const modelRegistry = await loadModelRegistry(...); const modelRegistryEntry = findRegistryEntryByModel(...)` into `const { entry: modelRegistryEntry } = await loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel(CONTROL_PLANE_ROOT_DIRECTORY, input.model);` (destructured entry only, since the site never uses the registry); `experimental.chat.system.transform` collapses into `const { registry: modelRegistry, entry: modelRegistryEntry } = await loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel(CONTROL_PLANE_ROOT_DIRECTORY, input.model);` (both destructured, since the transform body uses `modelRegistry.models` in `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` and `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` below). M82 comments document the consolidation at both call sites and point at the helper docstring for the drift-shape rationale.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the `logPluginHookFailure_*` cluster. All three pins inject a synthetic registry via the `loadFn` parameter so no disk I/O is required. `_whenEntryMatches_returnsRegistryAndEntry` pins the positive path: injected registry contains a matching curated entry, the helper must return `{ registry, entry }` where both are the same references as injected. `_whenProviderIdMismatches_returnsUndefinedEntry` pins the provider-narrowing contract: a curated entry whose `id` equals the input `id` but whose provider is `ollama-cloud` is looked up with `providerID: "openrouter"`; the helper must return `entry: undefined` because `composeRouteKey` normalization on both sides rejects the cross-provider match. `_whenLoaderCalled_forwardsControlPlaneRootVerbatim` pins the root-forwarding contract: a specific path `"/very/specific/root/path"` is passed in, captured by the injected loader, asserted `===` against the captured value — catches any sabotage that hardcodes the root. The three pins partition the contract by distinct sabotages: hardcoding `entry: undefined` fires pin 1 only (pins 2 and 3 already produce undefined/ignore-entry), dropping `providerID` from the narrowing fires pin 2 only (pin 1 still finds its match because pin 1's entry has the correct provider, pin 3 ignores the entry entirely), hardcoding the root argument fires pin 3 only (pins 1 and 2 ignore the captured root). No single sabotage fires more than one pin.
- **Verification**: three verify-on-HEAD sabotages, each fired exactly the expected single pin and nothing else. Sabotage A (`entry = undefined; void inputModel;` — the "hardcode undefined" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenEntryMatches_returnsRegistryAndEntry` (entry actual `undefined`, expected the injected matching entry). Pins 2 and 3 continued to pass. Sabotage B (`providerID: registry.models[0]?.provider_order[0]?.provider ?? ""` — the "drop providerID" drift class that would collapse lookup to id-only and false-positive match): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenProviderIdMismatches_returnsUndefinedEntry` (entry actual the false-positive `shared-id` entry, expected undefined). Pins 1 and 3 continued to pass because pin 1's entry has the correct provider and pin 3 does not inspect the entry. Sabotage C (`void controlPlaneRootDirectory; const registry = await loadFn("");` — the "hardcode the root" drift class): `bun test` reported **exactly 1 expected failure** — `_whenLoaderCalled_forwardsControlPlaneRootVerbatim` (captured root actual `""`, expected `"/very/specific/root/path"`). Pins 1 and 2 continued to pass because their injected loaders ignore the root argument. Exactly the per-sabotage asymmetric partition the three-pin split is designed to produce — three distinct sabotage classes, three disjoint pin firings. Restored the fix, **250/250 pass** (247 pre-M82 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel` export with full docstring directly after `findRegistryEntryByModel`; two call-site collapses in the `chat.params` and `experimental.chat.system.transform` hooks with M82 comments documenting the consolidation), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `loadRegistryAndLookupEntryForInputModel` import, three new unit pins directly before the `logPluginHookFailure_*` cluster). No type additions — the `inputModel` parameter uses an inline `{ id: string; providerID: string }` type because the helper deliberately narrows away any future runtime-model field growth.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated helper. No production behavior change — the helper produces the exact same runtime behavior as the two inlined blocks. Value is structural: the "load the registry and narrow an opencode input.model to its curated entry" operation is now a property of a single function body rather than two copy-pasted inline blocks, and a future opencode field growth on `input.model` is a single-site edit that TypeScript-checks both callers automatically.

### M81: `persistProviderHealth` inlined the same "spread + infinity-to-`never`" serialization transform in two places — once for the provider health map and once for the route health map — and a future edit that grew the persisted shape by a field would ship asymmetrically across provider vs route entries if the maintainer updated only one block, producing missing fields on half the health state after every plugin restart with no validation error `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `persistProviderHealth` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined the same shape twice. First, for `healthMap` entries: `Array.from(healthMap.entries()).map(([key, health]) => [key, { ...health, until: health.until === Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY ? "never" : health.until }])` piped into `Object.fromEntries`. Then, for `routeHealthMap` entries: `for (const [routeKey, health] of routeHealthMap.entries()) { obj[routeKey] = { ...health, until: health.until === Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY ? "never" : health.until }; }`. Identical transform, different collection idiom (`map + fromEntries` vs `for-of + assign`), SAME output shape. The duplication is a drift surface with an especially nasty failure mode: a future field added to `PersistedHealthEntry` (a `reason` telemetry string, a `lastPenaltyAt` timestamp, a `source` enum) has to propagate to BOTH blocks by hand, and forgetting one produces asymmetric JSON where provider entries carry the new field and route entries do not (or vice versa). The asymmetry would NOT throw at persist time because both output shapes are still valid `PersistedHealthEntry` values — `JSON.stringify` serialises whatever's there. It would surface only as missing fields on one half of the health state after a plugin restart, which is exactly the class of bug M68/M73 closed at the record layer: cross-process / cross-restart durability invariants that are impossible to reproduce from a unit test and surface only as intermittent telemetry drift.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector with a high-blast-radius failure mode. No current live divergence — both inline blocks produce byte-identical output today because the only transform beyond the spread is the infinity-to-`never` conversion, and `key_missing` entries can in principle live in either map (currently they only live in the provider map, but nothing enforces that invariant). The value is structural. The two-block split obscures a single logical operation — "flatten one in-memory health entry to its on-disk form" — into two collection-traversal idioms. A named serializer reveals the shared transform and makes the persist body a pure projection over `serializeHealthEntryForPersistence`. A future field addition becomes a single-site edit with compile-time propagation to both callers. The helper also pins the contract at the `ProviderHealth | ModelRouteHealth` union type: today those types are structurally identical, so routing through one serializer is the right fit; if they ever diverge, the helper's parameter shape surfaces the split in one place rather than two.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `serializeHealthEntryForPersistence(health: ProviderHealth | ModelRouteHealth): PersistedHealthEntry` directly after the `PersistedHealthMap` type alias (which was moved from `type PersistedHealthMap = Record<string, ...>` to a two-line `export type PersistedHealthEntry = ...; type PersistedHealthMap = Record<string, PersistedHealthEntry>;` so the element type is addressable from the helper and tests). Full ~50-line docstring enumerating the two-site drift surface, the `key_missing` infinity-to-`never` conversion rationale (`JSON.stringify(Infinity)` emits `null`, which `parsePersistedHealthEntry` rejects — the `"never"` string is the stable on-disk form hydrated back to `Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` on load), and the deliberate union-parameter decision. The helper body is exactly one return-spread with the infinity conversion. Rewired both call sites in `persistProviderHealth`: the `healthMap` block collapses from a 7-line inline map + fromEntries to a 4-line `Object.fromEntries` pipe that returns `[key, serializeHealthEntryForPersistence(health)]`; the `routeHealthMap` block collapses from a 5-line for-loop with an inline spread to a 3-line for-loop with a single `serializeHealthEntryForPersistence(health)` call. M81 comments document the consolidation at the point of collapse.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the existing `logPluginHookFailure_*` cluster: `_whenUntilIsInfinity_emitsNeverString` (infinity-conversion pin — `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` must serialize as the literal string `"never"`, catching a sabotage that drops the conditional), `_whenUntilIsFinite_passesNumberThrough` (finite pass-through pin — `until: 1_700_000_000_000` must serialize as `1_700_000_000_000` unchanged, catching a blanket-stringify sabotage that would break live quota backoffs by rewriting all finite timestamps to strings), `_whenCalled_preservesStateAndRetryCount` (spread-preservation pin — `state: "no_credit"` and `retryCount: 7` must survive the spread, catching a sabotage that switches from `{...health, until: ...}` to explicit field listing and forgets or typos a field). The three pins partition the contract by output-shape regions: pin 1 covers the infinity branch of the `until` field, pin 2 covers the pass-through branch of the `until` field, pin 3 covers all non-`until` fields via the spread. No single sabotage fires more than one pin — the asymmetric split is per-output-field rather than per-input-state.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the `until` conditional with a plain `until: health.until` pass-through — the exact class of drift M81 prevents, where a future maintainer simplifies the conditional and forgets the on-disk invariant. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 1 expected failure fired** — `_whenUntilIsInfinity_emitsNeverString` (actual `Infinity`, expected `"never"`). The other two pins continued to pass because the sabotage only touched the infinity branch of the `until` field: `_whenUntilIsFinite_passesNumberThrough` passed because `until: health.until` is identical to the correct finite-branch behavior, and `_whenCalled_preservesStateAndRetryCount` passed because the spread still carries `state` and `retryCount` verbatim. Exactly the per-output-field partition the three-pin split is designed to produce. Restored the fix, **247/247 pass** (244 pre-M81 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `PersistedHealthEntry` exported type alias, new `serializeHealthEntryForPersistence` export with full docstring directly after the `PersistedHealthMap` type, two call-site collapses inside `persistProviderHealth` with an M81 comment documenting the consolidation), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `serializeHealthEntryForPersistence` import, three new unit pins directly before the `logPluginHookFailure_*` cluster). The `PersistedHealthMap` type is unchanged at the value level (still `Record<string, PersistedHealthEntry>`) but the element type is now named and exported so the serializer has a principal return type.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated serializer. No production behavior change — the helper produces byte-identical JSON output to the inlined blocks. Value is structural: the "flatten one in-memory health entry to its on-disk form" operation is now a property of a single function body rather than two copy-pasted inline blocks, and a future field addition to `PersistedHealthEntry` is a single-site edit that TypeScript propagates to both callers automatically.

### M80: the `chat.params` and `experimental.chat.system.transform` hooks both wrapped their bodies in `try/catch { return; }` and swallowed every throw silently — a registry syntax error, a prompt-builder bug, or any hook-internal exception disappeared with zero operator signal while the plugin silently stopped setting temperatures / injecting system prompts / expiring health maps `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` and `experimental.chat.system.transform` hooks in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` both wrapped their bodies in `try { ... } catch { return; }` — the catch clause had no `error` binding and emitted nothing. The swallow policy itself is correct: a plugin that throws into the opencode host crashes the whole editor session, so the outer hooks MUST catch. But swallowing silently removes the ONLY operator signal that the hook has stopped working. Real manifestations this enables: (1) a syntax error in `config/models.jsonc` introduced by a hand edit makes `loadModelRegistry` throw — both hooks silently return, routing falls back to opencode defaults, the health maps stop being expired, and the persisted `providerHealth.json` file grows unbounded because the transform hook's `expireHealthMaps` call never runs, and nothing is written to stderr; (2) a prompt-builder bug (e.g. a null dereference in `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` on a malformed health entry) disappears silently on every single message, so the agent never sees the health-annotated system prompt and operators cannot see WHY from logs; (3) a `findRegistryEntryByModel` throw on an unexpected shape silently disables temperature overrides. All three failure modes are invisible in production. The third hook in the plugin (`provider.models`) already logs through `logRegistryLoadError(error)` on its catch clause, which sends a mixed signal: one hook surfaces errors, two silently swallow, and the two silent hooks run on EVERY chat.params / transform invocation while the logged hook runs only when opencode enumerates provider models.
- **Reachability**: reachable latent bug — the silent catches exist in the shipping plugin today and ANY throw inside either hook produces the invisible-failure behavior described above. Not a drift vector like M75-M79 (which closed composition-drift surfaces that were correct at HEAD), this one is a real observability gap that ships in production. The counterfactual: operators running aicoder-opencode against a broken `models.jsonc` would see degraded routing, no obvious root cause, and would have to attach a debugger to discover the plugin was throwing on every chat message. The fix surfaces the failure class to stderr without changing the swallow-and-continue policy — the hook still returns cleanly, the editor session still works, but operators now see a grep-friendly line per failing invocation.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `logPluginHookFailure(hookName, error, logFn?): void` directly after `logRegistryLoadError` (making the two log helpers visible as siblings, with the distinction documented: `logRegistryLoadError` uses a registry-load-specific message and is called from the `provider.models` hook where the error class is known, while `logPluginHookFailure` is the general hook-failure sink that names the hook in the message for grep-ability). The helper takes a third optional `logFn` argument defaulting to `defaultHookFailureLogSink` (a thin wrapper over `console.error`) — the injection is what makes the helper pinnable from tests without spying on the global `console.error`. The helper body is a single `logFn` call with a template literal: `` `[aicoder-opencode plugin] ${hookName} hook failed — ignoring and continuing:` ``. Rewired both silent catches to `catch (error) { logPluginHookFailure("<hookName>", error); return; }` with M80 comments documenting the swallow-and-surface policy and explaining why the swallow itself is still required (a plugin cannot crash the host). The `provider.models` hook is deliberately left on `logRegistryLoadError` — its return value is a behavior (fall back to `provider.models`) and its error class is consistently a registry-load failure, so the specialized logger remains the right fit there.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins at the top of the `bindSessionHangState_*` cluster (before M79's pins), mirroring the same asymmetric-split shape but with a per-sabotage partition instead of a per-call partition: `_whenCalled_forwardsMessageContainingHookName` (hook-name pin — captures the message into an array, asserts it regex-matches `/chat\.params/`, catches a sabotage that drops the `${hookName}` interpolation), `_whenCalled_forwardsErrorReferenceVerbatim` (error-pass-through pin — captures the error argument, asserts `strictEqual` to the passed reference, catches a sabotage that wraps the error in a new Error or stringifies it — reference equality fails BEFORE message matching gets a chance, so this pin specifically isolates the pass-through contract), `_whenCalled_invokesLogFnExactlyOnce` (call-count pin — increments a counter, asserts `=== 1`, catches a sabotage that double-logs the hook name and the error on separate calls). The three pins partition the contract by distinct sabotages: dropping `${hookName}` fires pin 1 only, wrapping the error fires pin 2 only, double-logging fires pin 3 only. No single sabotage fires more than one pin — the opposite of the symmetry-based split M79 used, and the right shape for a helper whose contract is composed of three independent output properties rather than three cooperating map mutations.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the template literal `` `${hookName} hook failed` `` with a hard-coded `"hook failed"` — the exact class of drift M80 prevents, where a future maintainer simplifies the template and forgets the interpolation. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 1 expected failure fired** — `_whenCalled_forwardsMessageContainingHookName` (the regex `/chat\.params/` failed to match `"[aicoder-opencode plugin] hook failed — ignoring and continuing:"`). The other two pins continued to pass because the sabotage only dropped the interpolation: the error still passed through by reference (pin 2 green) and `logFn` still fired exactly once (pin 3 green). Exactly the per-sabotage partition the three-pin split is designed to produce. Restored the fix, **244/244 pass** (241 pre-M80 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `logPluginHookFailure` export with full docstring directly after `logRegistryLoadError`, plus a private `defaultHookFailureLogSink` function for the default `logFn` argument; two catch-clause rewrites in the `chat.params` and `experimental.chat.system.transform` hooks with M80 comments), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `logPluginHookFailure` import, three new unit pins directly before the `bindSessionHangState_*` cluster). No type additions — the `logFn` parameter uses an inline function type.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the new stderr output path. Production behavior change: any hook-internal throw that used to be silent will now produce a grep-friendly stderr line per failing invocation. Operators running broken `models.jsonc` files will see the failure immediately instead of days-later routing degradation. Return behavior is unchanged — the hooks still swallow-and-continue, so the editor session is not affected.

### M79: the `chat.params` hook inlined three `Map.set` writes to bind session hang state by hand, leaving the write-side of the triplet with no SSoT counterpart to M78's `readAndClearSessionHangState` — a future edit that added a fourth map or dropped one of the three would silently desynchronise the hang detector with no runtime error and no test failure `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` hook at the top of its handler in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined the three write-side operations that are the symmetric counterpart to the three read-side operations M78 just consolidated: `sessionActiveProviderMap.set(input.sessionID, input.provider.info.id); sessionActiveModelMap.set(input.sessionID, { id: input.model.id, providerID: input.model.providerID }); sessionStartTimeMap.set(input.sessionID, Date.now());`. Three failure modes sat on this composition: (1) forgetting the `sessionStartTimeMap.set` would disarm the hang detector entirely — `finalizeHungSessionState` short-circuits on missing start-time, so the hang timer would fire, find no start-time, and silently return null without recording any timeout penalty; (2) forgetting the `sessionActiveProviderMap.set` or `sessionActiveModelMap.set` would leave the hang timer firing with `undefined` bindings, which `finalizeHungSessionState` tolerates but which produces a silently unrecorded timeout penalty (the `routeKey` would be `"undefined/undefined"`, the entry would still go into the map, but no route-level telemetry downstream would ever match it); (3) a future edit that grew the triplet to a quadruplet (per-session tool budget, per-session fallback depth, per-session retry counter) would have to be propagated to every current AND future caller of the write-side ritual, and the M78 read-and-clear helper would silently drop the new field. The most insidious failure mode is (1): disarming the hang detector means silent-death sessions never get cleaned up OR penalised, so a hung route never accrues its timeout backoff and continues being routed to.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — the single `chat.params` call site threads all three writes correctly today. The value is structural symmetry. M78 extracted `readAndClearSessionHangState` as the read-side SSoT for the three-map tuple, but left the write side inlined at the one current call site. That asymmetry sends a misleading signal to future maintainers: "the read side needs a helper because ordering is load-bearing, the write side does not need one because the order is arbitrary". The first half is true, the second half is not — the write-side order is also load-bearing (start-time must be set LAST so the hang timer is only armed after provider/model are live), and the write-side SYMMETRY is critical because the M78 read-side helper assumes all three maps are populated in lockstep. Any future writer that forgets a field silently breaks the M78 contract with no test failure because M78 pins the helper's output shape, not the input-map coverage. Extracting `bindSessionHangState` as the write-side sibling closes this gap: the three helpers (`bindSessionHangState` / `readAndClearSessionHangState` / `clearSessionHangState`) now form a complete triplet covering every lifecycle operation on the session hang state, and no call site needs to know which maps participate.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `bindSessionHangState(sessionID, providerID, model, now, sessionStartTimeMap, sessionActiveProviderMap, sessionActiveModelMap): void` directly after `clearSessionHangState` (before `readAndClearSessionHangState`) with a ~40-line docstring documenting the three failure modes, the sibling-triplet architecture, the start-time-last ordering rationale, and the `now` parameter injection for deterministic testing (reads `Date.now()` at the call site instead of inside the helper so tests can pass 5000 without freezing the clock). The helper body is exactly three `Map.set` calls in the load-bearing order: provider, model, then start-time. Replaced the inlined three-line ritual in the `chat.params` hook with a single seven-argument call, updating the comment to document the M79 consolidation and the sibling-pair relationship with M78.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the existing `readAndClearSessionHangState_*` cluster (visually placing the write-side pins adjacent to the read-side pins so the sibling architecture is obvious in the test file): `_whenCalled_populatesAllThreeMapsAtomically` (symmetry pin — empty maps, single bind call, asserts all three maps have the expected entry with the expected values, catches a dropped write in any of the three), `_whenReBoundForSameSession_overwritesEveryMap` (re-bind pin — pre-populates all three maps with old values, fires a bind with new values, asserts all three maps have the NEW values, catches a "check-before-write" drift where a helper might grow a `.has()` guard and silently skip fields that are already set), `_whenCalledForSecondSession_leavesFirstSessionIntact` (isolation pin — binds session s2 into maps that already hold s1, asserts s1's entries are untouched in all three maps AND s2's start-time and provider are set). The three-pin split is asymmetric by design: pins 1 and 2 test the full triplet (dropping any write fires both), while pin 3 only asserts s2's start-time and provider (not s2's model) — so dropping the model write fires pins 1 and 2 but leaves pin 3 passing, proving the pins catch specifically the "which fields are written" contract and not a generic "helper is broken" failure.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by dropping the `sessionActiveModelMap.set(sessionID, model)` line from the helper body — the exact class of drift M79 prevents, where a future maintainer reorders or deletes one of the three writes. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures fired** — `_whenCalled_populatesAllThreeMapsAtomically` (expected model entry present, got `undefined`) and `_whenReBoundForSameSession_overwritesEveryMap` (expected new-model entry, got the pre-seeded old-model entry because the missing write left the re-bind path relying on the map's existing value). The third pin `_whenCalledForSecondSession_leavesFirstSessionIntact` continued to pass because its s2 assertions intentionally exclude the model map — exactly the asymmetric failure signature the three-pin split is designed to produce. Restored the fix, **241/241 pass** (238 pre-M79 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `bindSessionHangState` export with full docstring directly after `clearSessionHangState`, one call-site collapse in the `chat.params` hook with M79 comment documenting the sibling-triplet relationship), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `bindSessionHangState` import, three new unit pins directly before the `readAndClearSessionHangState_*` cluster). No type additions — the helper reuses the existing session-map value shape `{ id: string; providerID: string }`.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated session-bind helper. No production behavior change — the helper produces byte-identical runtime behavior to the inlined three-line ritual. Value is structural: the three-map write triplet is now a property of a single function body instead of a property the `chat.params` hook must preserve by hand, and the M78 read-side / M79 write-side sibling pair forms a complete triplet with `clearSessionHangState` covering every lifecycle operation on the per-session hang-detection state.

### M78: the `session.error` and `assistant.message.completed` event handlers both inlined a "read `providerID` + read `model` + `clearSessionHangState(4 args)`" ritual by hand, and a future edit swapping the read and clear at either site would silently turn both lookups into `undefined` and short-circuit every route-health classification branch with no runtime error and no test failure `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: both terminal event handlers in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `session.error` (~line 3876) and `assistant.message.completed` (~line 3945) — inlined the same four-line ritual by hand: `const providerID = sessionActiveProviderMap.get(sessionID); const model = sessionActiveModelMap.get(sessionID); clearSessionHangState(sessionID, sessionStartTimeMap, sessionActiveProviderMap, sessionActiveModelMap);`. The ordering is load-bearing: `clearSessionHangState` deletes from all three maps, so any call site that clears BEFORE reading will see `undefined` for both bindings and short-circuit every downstream classification branch (`if (!providerID) return`, the zero-token quota classifier, the model-not-found classifier, the authoritative-priority `recordProviderHealth` call). The most dangerous part of the drift is that nothing complains: no exception, no warning, no test failure — the hook silently stops recording health penalties and a quota-exhausted provider keeps being handed live traffic. Compounding the drift, `session.error` overlays its own `(sessionError as any).model ?? mappedModel` fallback on the model lookup (opencode surfaces `sessionError.model` for some failure shapes) while `assistant.message.completed` uses only the map lookup — which means a naive "consolidate the two inline sites into a shared three-line helper" pass would either lose the session.error override or propagate it into the completion hook where it has no meaning.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — both sites thread the read-before-clear ordering correctly today. The value is structural. Both hooks are load-bearing for the provider-health contract: `session.error` is the only path that records quota/key_dead/no_credit/model_not_found penalties on API error responses, and `assistant.message.completed` is the only path that records zero-token-quota penalties from silent quota exhaustion (the completion fires but all token counters are zero). A future edit that swaps order at either site — say, a maintainer refactoring the hook to "clear early, then classify from a snapshot" — would silently drop penalty recording on that entire hook's worth of failure classes. Worse, because the session maps are still populated at the start of every turn by `chat.params`, the sabotage would NOT produce noisy "undefined provider" warnings; the hook would just observe `undefined` and early-return cleanly every time. The only way a maintainer would notice is in aggregate: routes that should be quarantined stop being quarantined, backoff stops firing, and the model-registry health telemetry silently degrades. Encoding "read before clear" as a property of a single helper function body instead of a property each call site must preserve by hand closes this drift surface at the compiler level — a caller literally cannot get the order wrong because the helper does both in one call and returns the snapshotted tuple.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported helper `readAndClearSessionHangState(sessionID, sessionStartTimeMap, sessionActiveProviderMap, sessionActiveModelMap): { providerID, model }` directly after `clearSessionHangState` (to make the read-and-clear / clear-only sibling pair obvious) with a ~30-line docstring documenting the ordering drift, the rationale for snapshotting the mapped tuple verbatim (the `session.error` overlay stays at the call site so the helper doesn't grow a `modelOverride` parameter that would obscure which branch needs it), and the two failure modes it prevents. The helper body is exactly four lines: two `Map.get` reads, one delegation to `clearSessionHangState`, one return. Replaced both call sites: `session.error` now destructures `{ providerID, model: mappedModel }` and applies its `(sessionError as any).model ?? mappedModel` overlay externally (keeping the asymmetry visible at the call site where it matters); `assistant.message.completed` destructures `{ providerID, model }` directly since it has no overlay. Both collapse from a four-line inline ritual to a single five-argument call.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins directly before the existing `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyRoutePenaltiesExist_*` test (adjacent to the `clearSessionHangState_*` cluster so the sibling pair is visible): `_whenFullyBound_returnsTupleAndClearsMaps` (happy path — both reads return the live values, all three maps are cleared afterward, proving the read-before-clear ordering), `_whenModelMapMissing_returnsProviderButUndefinedModel` (partial binding — session has an entry in the start-time + provider maps but not yet in the model map (a shape that can occur if `chat.params` short-circuited mid-write), asserts `providerID` is live but `model` is `undefined`, AND both populated maps still get cleared), `_whenUnknownSession_returnsUndefinedTupleWithoutThrowing` (unknown session id — totality pin: the helper must not throw on a session it has never seen, must return `{undefined, undefined}` as a clean signal to the caller to early-return, and must leave unrelated sessions' map entries untouched). The three-pin split is asymmetric by design: pins 1 and 2 both depend on the read-before-clear ordering (they test live populated maps and assert the returned values match what WAS in the maps), while pin 3 returns `undefined` regardless of ordering because both paths produce `undefined` for an unseen session. Sabotaging the ordering will fire exactly pins 1 and 2 and leave pin 3 passing — the asymmetric failure signature proves the pins specifically catch the ordering drift and not a generic "helper is broken" failure.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by swapping the read-and-clear order inside the helper — moved the `clearSessionHangState(...)` call to execute BEFORE the two `Map.get` reads, the exact class of drift M78 prevents. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures fired** — `_whenFullyBound_returnsTupleAndClearsMaps` (expected `providerID === "iflowcn"`, got `undefined`) and `_whenModelMapMissing_returnsProviderButUndefinedModel` (expected `providerID === "openrouter"`, got `undefined`). The third pin `_whenUnknownSession_returnsUndefinedTupleWithoutThrowing` continued to pass because its assertions are ordering-invariant for the unknown-session case. Exactly the asymmetric failure signature the three-pin split is designed to produce. Restored the original read-before-clear order, **238/238 pass** (235 pre-M78 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `readAndClearSessionHangState` export with full docstring directly after `clearSessionHangState`, two call-site collapses in the `session.error` and `assistant.message.completed` event handlers with M78 comments documenting the ordering invariant the helper enforces), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `readAndClearSessionHangState` import, three new unit pins directly before the `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyRoutePenaltiesExist_*` test). No type additions — the helper reuses the existing session-map value shape `{ id: string; providerID: string }`.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated read-and-clear helper. No production behavior change — the helper produces byte-identical runtime behavior to the inlined four-line ritual. Value is structural: the read-before-clear ordering is now a property of a single function body instead of a property each of the two terminal event hooks must preserve by hand, and a future maintainer cannot silently break provider-health classification by reordering the read and the clear.

### M77: the `chat.params` hang-timer `setTimeout` callback inlined a two-step `finalize → null-guard → record` ritual whose null-guard failure mode was an async-isolated crash inside a setTimeout closure — a refactor that dropped the guard would call `recordRouteHealthPenalty` with undefined fields and throw into an unhandled rejection, or worse, silently drop the M68 durability pair and leak backoff enforcement on the one cleanup path silent-death sessions have `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` hang-timer `setTimeout` callback in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined a two-step ritual by hand: `const result = finalizeHungSessionState(...); if (!result) return; recordRouteHealthPenalty(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, result.routeKey, result.health, persistProviderHealth);`. Three failure modes sat on this composition: (1) forgetting the `if (!result) return` guard would call `recordRouteHealthPenalty` with undefined route-key/health fields and throw inside the async-isolated `setTimeout` closure (which has no surrounding handler — the exception becomes an unhandledRejection, noisy in prod logs, and the penalty is lost even on the happy path where the computation succeeded); (2) forgetting the `recordRouteHealthPenalty` call entirely would silently drop the M68 durability pair — the hang was detected, per-session state was cleared by `finalizeHungSessionState`, but the penalty was never persisted, so the next identical hang accrues on the same route with no backoff (infinite retry on a dead long-reasoning endpoint); (3) mixing up the `finalizeHungSessionState` return shape with `recordRouteHealthPenalty` arguments (e.g. passing `result.health` as `routeKey`) — TypeScript catches it today, but the shape-pairing is another drift surface. The second failure mode is the worst because it silently degrades the backoff contract on the ONE cleanup path that silent-death sessions (network drops, client Ctrl-C, parent process kills that bypass `session.error` and `assistant.message.completed`) have.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector. No current live divergence — the single inline site threads all three steps correctly today. The value is structural. The hang-timer callback is armed for every `chat.params` hook that runs with `timeoutMs >= 1000` (i.e. the production configuration — only the testing short-circuit at `< 1000` goes through `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` directly), so this path is load-bearing for every turn that hits a silent-death scenario. The `setTimeout` closure boundary makes bugs on this path particularly vicious: an exception inside the callback becomes an unhandledRejection and disappears into the Node event loop, the penalty is lost, and there is no log trail pointing at the callback. Consolidating to a named wrapper with a `void` return (no nullable intermediate) eliminates the null-guard drift surface entirely — the wrapper handles the null short-circuit internally, callers cannot forget it.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported wrapper `finalizeHungSessionStateAndRecordPenalty(sessionID, sessionStartTimeMap, sessionActiveProviderMap, sessionActiveModelMap, modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, timeoutMs, now, persistFn): void` directly after `finalizeHungSessionState` (to make the pure-compute / impure-write sibling pair obvious) with a ~55-line docstring enumerating the three failure modes of the inline ritual, the rationale for a wrapper over a rewrite of `finalizeHungSessionState` (the pure function's existing unit tests pin the compute-and-cleanup contract without coupling to durability — rewriting would force every test to pass a stub persister and blur the pure/impure split), and the explicit M68 `recordRouteHealthPenalty` delegation so the durability pair is preserved. The wrapper calls `finalizeHungSessionState`, short-circuits internally on null, and otherwise delegates to `recordRouteHealthPenalty` — callers cannot forget the null-check because the wrapper's return type is `void`. Replaced the inline composition in the `chat.params` hang-timer `setTimeout` callback with a single ~9-argument call, updating the comment to document the M77 consolidation and the async-closure drift surface the wrapper eliminates. No changes to `finalizeHungSessionState` itself — it remains a pure function so its existing three unit tests (hung-session, already-completed, within-budget) still pin the compute-and-cleanup contract.

The three-pin split catches asymmetric failures: the null-path pins fire independently of the hung-path pin, so a refactor that drops the null-check (the most dangerous failure mode) fires exactly the two null-path pins.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the `if (result === null) return;` short-circuit with a no-op that falls through to `recordRouteHealthPenalty` with dummy `"dummy/dummy"` routeKey + synthetic ModelRouteHealth — the exact class of drift M77 prevents, where a maintainer converts the guard into something that still fires the write on the null path. The `_whenSessionHung_*` pin continued to pass because the sabotage only changed the null-path — the hung-session computation still returned non-null and the non-null branch wrote the correct timeout entry, fired persist, and cleared the maps. Exactly the asymmetric failure mode the three-pin split is designed to catch. Restored the fix, **235/235 pass** (232 pre-M77 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `finalizeHungSessionStateAndRecordPenalty` wrapper with full docstring, hang-timer `setTimeout` callback replaced with single call + updated M77 comment), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `finalizeHungSessionStateAndRecordPenalty` import, three new unit pins above the `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_closureDoesNotRetainFullInput_regressionPin`). ### M76: the `session.error` model-not-found branch was the last inline three-step `lookup + buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth + recordRouteHealthPenalty` composition — M75 explicitly deferred it to keep its sibling wrapper's state+duration contract clean, and a third writer copy-pasting the branch would still inherit the full M43/M68 drift surface `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` hook at lines 3745-3758 of `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined the same three-step write ritual M75 just collapsed — `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers` feeding `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth(providerID, modelID, existing, Date.now())` feeding `recordRouteHealthPenalty(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, routeKey, health, persistProviderHealth)` — but used the dedicated `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` pure builder (6h `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS`, hard-coded `"model_not_found"` state) instead of the generic `buildRouteHealthEntry` M75 handled. M75's docstring explicitly called out this site as deliberately out-of-scope: "the `session.error` model-not-found branch uses a different builder with a hard-coded 6h duration and no state parameter — that branch stays inline for now, adding it here would require either a union-typed parameter or an overload, both of which blur the state+duration contract the wrapper enforces". That left one of the three original inline sites uncovered, meaning a future writer copy-pasting the model-not-found branch (e.g. a `session.error` handler for a new 410 Gone status that also implies structural removal) would still inherit the full M43/M68 drift surface — same three failure modes M75 closes for the generic path.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector, same class as M75, but on the sister branch using the specialized `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` builder. No current live divergence — the single call site threads all three steps correctly today. The value is structural symmetry: M75 named the three-step ritual for the generic `(state, durationMs)` path but left the specialized `(model_not_found, 6h)` path inline, creating an obvious "half-done extraction" asymmetry. A maintainer reading the two branches of the `session.error` hook sees one branch using a named wrapper and one inlining the ritual, which signals (wrongly) that the inline branch is fundamentally different and cannot be folded through the same shape — when in fact the difference is purely which pure builder runs inside the wrapper. Closing M76 restores symmetry: both branches route through a named wrapper, and every route-level writer in the plugin has a compiler-enforced argument shape.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported wrapper `recordModelNotFoundRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, providerID, modelID, now, persistFn): void` directly after `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` (to make the M75/M76 sibling pair obvious) with a ~55-line docstring explaining the drift shape, the deliberate rejection of a union-typed or overloaded fold into M75 (an overload with a `"model_not_found"` discriminator would silently ignore the `durationMs` argument — caller passes 1h, gets 6h, no warning — which is worse than two dedicated wrappers), and the explicit M75 "stays inline for now" history. The wrapper body is structurally identical to M75's but calls `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` instead of `buildRouteHealthEntry`, keeping the M43 preserve-longer invariant through the builder's internal delegation to `buildRouteHealthEntry`. Replaced the single call site in the plugin closure — the ~14-line inline composition collapses to one 6-argument call.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins above the existing `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_*` cluster, mirroring the M75 three-pin split: `_whenCalled_writesSixHourModelNotFoundEntry` (builder-wiring pin — asserts the entry is written under the composite route key, state is `"model_not_found"`, `until` is exactly `now + ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS` (pinning that a maintainer cannot accidentally call `buildRouteHealthEntry` with the 1h quota duration), and `retryCount` is 1 for the first write), `_whenExistingQuotaEntryShorter_overridesWithLongerModelNotFound` (merge-chain pin — pre-seeds a 1h quota entry with `retryCount: 3`, fires an incoming 6h model_not_found penalty, asserts the longer penalty wins (state flips to `"model_not_found"`, `until` jumps to 6h), AND `retryCount` increments to 4 off the pre-existing entry — the `retryCount` increment proves the lookup step is wired, because a dropped lookup would reset `retryCount` to 1), `_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnThroughM68RecordWrapper` (durability-pair pin — spy asserts `persistFn` fires exactly once with reference equality to both live maps, identical to the M75 route-layer pin).
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the `existing` argument in the wrapper's `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` call with `undefined` — the exact class of drift M76 prevents, where a future maintainer inlines the build but forgets the lookup step. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 1 expected failure fired** — `_whenExistingQuotaEntryShorter_overridesWithLongerModelNotFound` (the merge-chain pin caught the dropped lookup: `retryCount` reset to 1 instead of incrementing to 4, failing the `assert.equal(entry.retryCount, 4)` with `actual: 1`). The other two pins continued to pass because the sabotage only dropped the lookup step — the state+until invariant still held with `undefined` as `existing` (the fresh entry built cleanly at `now + 6h` with `state: "model_not_found"`, which happens to match the builder-wiring pin's assertions since that pin uses an empty map and doesn't test the merge path), and `persistFn` still fired with both maps. Exactly the asymmetric failure mode the three-pin split is designed to catch. Restored the fix, **232/232 pass** (229 pre-M76 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.

No type additions.
