No production behavior change — the wrapper produces identical output to the inlined ritual. Value is structural: with M76 both branches of the `session.error` hook now route through named wrappers, the M75/M76 sibling pair is symmetric, and every route-level write path in the plugin has a compiler-enforced argument shape — there is no longer an inline composition for a future writer to copy-paste and silently break the M43/M68 invariants.

### M75: two route-level writer hooks (`session.error` zero-token-quota classifier and `chat.params` early-timeout branch) inlined the same three-step `lookup + buildRouteHealthEntry + recordRouteHealthPenalty` ritual by hand, so a third writer forgetting any of the three steps would silently break either the M43 preserve-longer merge, the M68 durability pair, or both `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: two hooks in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — the `session.error` zero-token-quota classifier and the `chat.params` early-timeout branch (for the sub-1000ms testing path) — inlined the same ~11-line three-step ritual: (1) `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerID, model.id)` to fetch the existing entry feeding the M43 preserve-longer merge, (2) `buildRouteHealthEntry(providerID, model.id, <state>, <durationMs>, existing, Date.now())` to compute the merged new entry, (3) `recordRouteHealthPenalty(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, routeKey, health, persistProviderHealth)` to fire the M68 durability pair. Every route-level writer needs all three steps in order: skipping the lookup passes `undefined` as `existing` and silently shrinks an active longer penalty (the exact M43 drift at the route layer); skipping the build writes a raw entry that bypasses the merge; skipping the record wrapper breaks the M68 persist pair and the penalty vanishes on plugin reload. The three helpers existed as exported pure functions after M43/M67/M68, but the call-site ritual was still a hand-wired composition with no named boundary — a third writer (new classifier, shim-level override, retry-escalation path) copy-pasting the pattern inherits all three bug classes unless the ritual is one named call.
- **Reachability**: latent composition-drift vector, same class as M67 (which consolidated the composite-key lookup for readers and writers) and M68 (which consolidated the set+persist pair). No current live divergence — the two existing call sites thread all three steps correctly today. The value is structural: the three-step ritual is a cross-cutting write contract, and M43 (preserve-longer merge) and M68 (durability pair) are both invariants enforced by the underlying helpers — but only if the ritual remains intact at every call site. A future fifth writer (say, a new `session.tool_failed` handler for routes that fail at the tool-calling layer, or a synthetic test-harness writer) that copy-pastes a neighboring hook and tweaks the state string could trivially skip one of the three steps without anything flagging it. M67 and M68 each closed one half of the composition drift; M75 closes the overall ritual by naming the whole three-step sequence as one operation.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported wrapper `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, providerID, modelID, state, durationMs, now, persistFn): void` directly after `recordProviderHealthPenalty` with a ~90-line docstring explaining the drift shape, the three-step contract, the three failure modes each step defends against (lookup missing → M43 merge breaks, build missing → raw write bypasses merge, record missing → M68 durability pair breaks), the rationale for a wrapper over a shared inline snippet (call-site arity collapses from ~11 lines to one 7-argument call, no independent semantic meaning for the three steps in isolation), and the explicit exclusion of `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` (which has a different builder signature with a hard-coded 6h duration and no state parameter — adding it would require either an overload or a union-typed parameter that blurs the state+duration contract). The wrapper takes the three-helper composition as a single named operation: `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers` → `buildRouteHealthEntry` → `recordRouteHealthPenalty`. Replaced both call sites in the plugin closure: the `session.error` zero-token-quota classifier dropped its ~11-line inline composition for a single `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers(...)` call with `"quota"` state, and the `chat.params` early-timeout branch did the same with `"timeout"` state.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins above the existing `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_*` cluster, each pinning one of the three steps of the ritual to a different invariant: `_whenCalled_writesEntryUnderCompositeRouteKey` (build+write wiring — the composite route key `"provider/model-id"` is correctly threaded through `buildRouteHealthEntry` and into the map write), `_whenExistingEntryHasLongerUntil_preservesM43MergeInvariant` (the lookup step is wired — pre-seeds a 6h `model_not_found` entry, fires an incoming 1h `quota` penalty, asserts the longer penalty dominates and `retryCount` increments), `_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnThroughM68RecordWrapper` (the record step is wired — spy asserts `persistFn` fires exactly once with reference equality to both live maps, identical to the M68 route-layer pin). The three-pin split catches asymmetric failures: any one of the three composition steps can be broken independently.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the `existing` argument in the wrapper's `buildRouteHealthEntry` call with `undefined` — the exact class of drift M75 prevents, where a future maintainer inlines the build but forgets the lookup step. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 1 expected failure fired** — `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenExistingEntryHasLongerUntil_preservesM43MergeInvariant` (the merge pin caught the dropped lookup: incoming `"quota"` state overrode the pre-existing `"model_not_found"` state because `existing` was `undefined` at merge time, and the assertion on `entry.state === "model_not_found"` failed with `actual: "quota"`). The other two pins continued to pass because the sabotage only dropped the lookup step — the write still landed under the correct composite key and `persistFn` still fired with both maps. Exactly the asymmetric failure mode the three-pin split is designed to catch. Restored the fix, **229/229 pass** (226 pre-M75 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` wrapper with full docstring, two call-site collapses in the `session.error` zero-token-quota classifier and `chat.params` early-timeout branch), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `recordRouteHealthByIdentifiers` import, three new unit pins above the `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_*` cluster). No type additions — `ProviderHealthState` and `PersistProviderHealthFn` reused from existing exports, `ModelRouteHealth`/`ProviderHealth` reused from their existing type promotions.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated route-level writer. No production behavior change — the wrapper produces identical output to the inlined ritual and runs the same side effects in the same order. Value is structural: the three-step route-level write contract is now named, tested, and a future writer gets the M43 merge + M68 durability pair for free just by calling the wrapper — no way to silently skip a step.

### M74: `session.error` hook hand-wired `ProviderApiErrorClass → duration` as three parallel if-else branches, coupling the class→duration mapping to its single call site with no exhaustiveness check — a new penalty state added to the union would silently fall through the chain and be dropped as if it were `"unclassified"` `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (lines 3615-3621 pre-fix) hand-wired the `ProviderApiErrorClass → duration` mapping as three parallel if-else branches: `if (errorClass === "quota") recordProviderHealth(providerID, "quota", QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS); else if (errorClass === "no_credit") recordProviderHealth(providerID, "no_credit", NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS); else if (errorClass === "key_dead") recordProviderHealth(providerID, "key_dead", KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS);`. The mapping had a single source of truth — the three closure-local alias constants `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS`/`KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS`/`NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS` — but the class→duration *assignment* was coupled to the if-chain shape, with nothing forcing all four states of `ProviderApiErrorClass` to be handled. If a fifth penalty state ever joined the union (say `"blocked"` for a Cloudflare 403 WAF hit or `"region_restricted"` for a geo-blocked endpoint), TypeScript would NOT fail — the new state would silently fall through the `else if` cascade and be treated identically to `"unclassified"`, quarantining nothing. The classifier would correctly identify the new state but the `session.error` hook would drop the penalty on the floor.
- **Reachability**: latent exhaustiveness-drift vector. No current live divergence — `ProviderApiErrorClass` has exactly the four states (`"quota" | "no_credit" | "key_dead" | "unclassified"`) the if-chain handles today, so the runtime behavior is correct. The value is structural: the drift shape is classic "open-ended discriminated union with hand-wired per-case handling elsewhere", and closed-union types exist precisely so the compiler can enforce exhaustiveness through `Record<>` or `switch`-never patterns. The current code encoded the mapping in a shape (if-else cascade) that the type system cannot cross-check against the union definition. A maintainer adding a new `ProviderApiErrorClass` state would have to remember to update the `session.error` hook by hand — and if they forgot, the bug would only surface in production telemetry as "why is this provider not being quarantined after repeated WAF blocks?". M43 already uses `Record<>` shapes for state-priority tables elsewhere in the plugin (`PENALTY_STATE_PRIORITY_MAP` drives the preserve-longer merge), and the `session.error` duration mapping deserves the same treatment.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported constant `PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS: Record<Exclude<ProviderApiErrorClass, "unclassified">, number>` at module scope (directly after `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS`) with a ~30-line docstring explaining the pre-fix drift shape, the `Record<Exclude<...>, number>` exhaustiveness contract (adding a new penalty state to the union fails compilation at the Record literal until a duration is assigned — no hand-wiring required), and the rationale for excluding `"unclassified"` by construction via `Exclude<>` rather than an if-guard (an if-guard can be forgotten; a type-level exclusion cannot). The Record maps `quota → ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS`, `no_credit → PROVIDER_NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS`, `key_dead → PROVIDER_KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS` — identical to the pre-fix mapping, pulled from module-scope constants so the single source of truth is unchanged. Collapsed the three-branch if-else cascade in the `session.error` hook to a single `if (errorClass !== "unclassified") { recordProviderHealth(providerID, errorClass, PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS[errorClass]); }`, with TS's discriminated-union narrowing proving `errorClass` is a valid Record key inside the guard. Removed the now-unused `KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS` and `NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS` closure-local aliases (the `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` alias stays — it's still referenced by the hang-timer path at lines 3708 and 3758).
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins above the existing `classifyProviderApiError_*` cluster: `PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS_quotaKey_mapsTo1HourConstant`, `_noCreditKey_mapsTo2HourNoCreditConstant`, `_keyDeadKey_mapsTo2HourKeyDeadConstant`. Each pin asserts reference equality between the Record entry and its source-of-truth module-scope constant (`ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS`, `PROVIDER_NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS`, `PROVIDER_KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS`), catching silent value drift if a future maintainer reassigns a Record entry to the wrong duration constant. The `"unclassified"` exclusion needs no runtime test — it's a compile-time guarantee enforced by `Exclude<ProviderApiErrorClass, "unclassified">` in the Record type, and a runtime test would just duplicate what the type system already proves.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by swapping `no_credit: PROVIDER_NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS` to `no_credit: ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` in the Record literal (the exact class of drift M74 prevents — a maintainer copy-pasting a neighboring line and not reassigning the duration). Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 1 expected failure fired** — `PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS_noCreditKey_mapsTo2HourNoCreditConstant` (reference-equality assertion failed because the swapped entry points at the 1h quota constant instead of the 2h no_credit constant). The other two Record pins continued to pass because the sabotage only touched one entry — exactly the granular failure mode the three-pin split is designed to catch. No integration failures fired because no existing tests drive the `session.error` hook from test code (the hook is event-system plumbing that fires at runtime), which is expected — the Record shape is the authoritative regression guard and the call-site collapse is a pure behavior-preserving refactor. Restored the fix, **226/226 pass** (223 pre-M74 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` Record constant with full docstring, `session.error` hook three-branch if-else collapsed to one call, two unused closure-local aliases `KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS`/`NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS` removed), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `PROVIDER_PENALTY_CLASS_TO_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS`/`PROVIDER_NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS`/`PROVIDER_KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS` imports, three new unit pins). No type additions — `ProviderApiErrorClass` is reused from its existing definition at line 1241.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the Record-backed `session.error` hook. No production behavior change — the Record lookup produces identical output to the three-branch if-else and runs the same `recordProviderHealth` side effect. Value is structural: the class→duration mapping has a compiler-enforced exhaustiveness contract, and a future fifth penalty state added to `ProviderApiErrorClass` forces TS failures at the Record literal until the author assigns a duration, making the mapping impossible to forget.

### M73: factory-local `recordProviderHealth` inlined the same set+persist durability pair that M68 extracted `recordRouteHealthPenalty` for at the route layer — the provider layer had no module-scope helper, no regression pin, and no symmetric boundary, so a future provider-layer writer that forgot `void persistProviderHealth(...)` would silently produce backoffs that work for a few minutes and vanish on the next plugin bounce `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the factory-local `recordProviderHealth` helper at lines 3291-3303 of `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` inlined the same two-line durability pair that M68 already extracted `recordRouteHealthPenalty` for at the route layer: `providerHealthMap.set(providerID, computeProviderHealthUpdate(existing, state, newUntil)); void persistProviderHealth(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap);`. The `set` alone keeps the penalty in memory for the current plugin instance but drops it on plugin reload, plugin crash, or cross-process handoff via the shared `providerHealth.json` file that dr-repo, letta-workspace, and aicoder-opencode shims all mount. M68 enumerated this drift shape at length for the four route-layer writers and extracted the module-scope helper with a `persistFn` spy so the pairing could be pinned. The provider layer was left for a follow-up — the factory-local helper carries both lines today because its author wrote them together, but there is no module-scope boundary enforcing the pair and no regression pin forcing the pair to stay together through a future refactor. A fifth caller (a new provider-level state classification in `session.error`, a test harness that wants to write synthetic penalties, a shim-level override) that copy-pastes only the `set` call produces exactly the "why does this provider keep getting re-tried after restart?" telemetry noise M68 closed at the route layer.
- **Reachability**: latent durability-drift vector, same class as M68 but at the provider layer. No current live divergence — the single factory-local helper carries both lines and its three callers (inside the `session.error` classification switch: `recordProviderHealth(providerID, "quota", QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS)`, `"no_credit"`, `"key_dead"`) all route through the helper so they share the pair. The value is structural: the durability invariant is a contract between the in-memory maps and the on-disk `providerHealth.json` snapshot file, and the current enforcement (a hand-written two-line helper inside the plugin closure) has no named boundary, no unit pin, no symmetric twin at the route layer, and no way for a future maintainer reading the `session.error` hook to grep for "record the penalty" and land at a single source of truth. M68's route-layer extraction explicitly called out the symmetric provider-layer gap ("the provider layer has the same shape and deserves the same treatment, left for a follow-up when a second writer materializes or when the durability invariant needs a regression pin"). That follow-up is M73.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `recordProviderHealthPenalty(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, providerID, newHealth, persistFn): void` directly after `recordRouteHealthPenalty` (to make the symmetric M68/M73 pair obvious) with a ~55-line docstring explaining the durability invariant, the M68 precedent and the explicit "route layer / provider layer split left as a TODO" history, the `computeProviderHealthUpdate` / `recordProviderHealthPenalty` boundary split (merge policy stays in the pure function, durability stays in the writer helper — same split M68 used between `buildRouteHealthEntry` and `recordRouteHealthPenalty`), and the atomic-snapshot shape where `modelRouteHealthMap` threads through unchanged so a provider-layer write also re-serializes any pending route-layer entries. The factory-local `recordProviderHealth` becomes a thin wrapper: read the existing entry, compute `newUntil` from `durationMs`, run `computeProviderHealthUpdate` for the M43 preserve-longer merge, and delegate to `recordProviderHealthPenalty` with `persistProviderHealth` as the injected `persistFn`. The helper reuses the `PersistProviderHealthFn` type M68 already exports, so no new type machinery.
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins above the existing `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_*` cluster (immediately after M68's `recordRouteHealthPenalty_*` trio): `recordProviderHealthPenalty_whenCalled_writesHealthToProviderMap` (map-set invariant — symmetric with the M68 route-layer pin, the helper must write the new `ProviderHealth` entry under the exact `providerID` passed in), `recordProviderHealthPenalty_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnWithBothMaps` (persistence-pairing invariant — spy asserts exactly one `persistFn` call with reference equality to both live maps so the persister sees the post-write state and the atomic-snapshot shape is preserved), and `recordProviderHealthPenalty_whenMapHasExistingEntry_overwritesItBeforePersistFires` (write-ordering invariant — spy reads `providerHealthMap.get(providerID)` at call time and asserts the overwrite is visible before the persist fires, preventing a future refactor from reordering the pair into a pre-write persist that would serialize the stale entry). Each pin explicitly calls out its symmetric M68 counterpart in the inline comment so future reviewers see the provider/route layer symmetry.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by dropping the `void persistFn(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap);` call from the helper body and leaving only the `providerHealthMap.set` — the exact durability-drift bug M73 prevents, where a future maintainer refactoring the writer accidentally separates the pair. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures fired** — `recordProviderHealthPenalty_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnWithBothMaps` (the persist-pairing spy asserted `persistCalls === 1` and got 0) and `recordProviderHealthPenalty_whenMapHasExistingEntry_overwritesItBeforePersistFires` (the write-ordering spy captured `undefined` at persist time because persist never fired). The third new pin (`_whenCalled_writesHealthToProviderMap`) continued to pass because the sabotage only dropped the persist half — the set still fires, so the map-set invariant holds — exactly the asymmetric failure mode the three-pin split is designed to catch. No existing integration tests fired because `recordProviderHealthPenalty` is new in M73 and no other code path depends on it yet (the factory-local `recordProviderHealth` delegating to it is exercised only indirectly via the end-to-end `recommendTaskModelRoute` path, which doesn't drive the `session.error` hook from tests). The three-pin unit coverage is the authoritative regression guard. Restored the fix, **223/223 pass** (220 pre-M73 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.

### M72: `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` inlined the same per-entry `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` + `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` scan that `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` already encapsulated — M65's dedupe sweep (which extracted `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` for the `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` caller) stopped one caller short and missed this structurally identical site `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` at lines 2898-2913 in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` duplicated the inner per-entry route scan that `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` (extracted in M61 and reused in M65) already owned. The two functions differ only in outer-loop arity — `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` scans ONE entry's `provider_order` for the first healthy visible route, and `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` scans MANY entries for the same thing — but `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` inlined its own four-line `const visibleRoutes = filterVisibleProviderRoutes(entry.provider_order); for (const route of visibleRoutes) { if (isRouteCurrentlyHealthy(...)) return ...; }` loop instead of delegating. M65's Completion Notes explicitly called out deduping the `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` inline copy as "the stray 7th inline copy missed in the M64 dedupe sweep" and routed that caller through `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry`, but the M65 pass stopped at that one site — `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` kept its inline form and became the 8th. Both sites encoded the same "provider healthy AND route expired/absent" conjunction via the same leaf predicate, so they don't currently diverge, but the per-entry scan shape (visible-route filtering + early-return on first hit) is exactly the answer `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` gives, and having two call sites for the same answer means any future refinement of the inner scan (a provider-preference tiebreak, a new capability-tier filter before health check, a composite-key normalization step) has to land at both places with nothing forcing the update.
- **Reachability**: latent drift vector in the same class as M64-M71. No current live divergence — the inline loop and the helper produce identical output today (both walk `filterVisibleProviderRoutes(entry.provider_order)` in order and return the first route passing `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy`). The value is structural: `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` is the downstream scanner powering `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s last-resort tier-widened pass (M60) — the "when every entry within the requested complexity tier has every route blocked, scan sibling tiers" path that a large-complexity request hits during a frontier+strong outage. Any future refinement of the per-entry "first healthy route" predicate (e.g. prefer routes whose composite key was updated most recently, or tiebreak by `retryCount` to favor routes that have cooled off longer) would need to land at both `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` (used by `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`, `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes`, `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`) AND `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`'s inline loop, with the second site silently keeping the stale behavior if the maintainer only updates the helper. The classic "helper already exists, second caller reinvents it" drift shape.
- **Fix**: rewrote `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`'s body to delegate the per-entry scan to `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` instead of inlining `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` + the `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` loop. The outer function still owns the multi-entry walk and the `{provider, model}` narrowing (strips the `priority` field that `ProviderRoute` carries but that this function's callers don't need), but the inner "first healthy visible route for ONE entry" question now has one definition site. Added a 12-line inline comment documenting the M72 dedupe explicitly referencing M65's partial sweep so a future reviewer doesn't re-inline the loop on the theory that "an extra function call per entry isn't worth the indirection" — the value is single-source-of-truth for the per-entry predicate, not runtime efficiency.
- **Tests**: no new unit pins added — M72 is a pure behavior-preserving delegation and `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` already has its own M61-era unit pins pinning its contract. The three existing `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_*` integration pins (`_whenFirstEntryHasHealthyRoute_returnsFirstMatch`, `_whenFirstEntryProviderUnhealthy_returnsNextHealthyEntry`, `_whenRouteLevelPenaltyBlocksPrimaryButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling`) cover all three axes the delegation must preserve: outer-loop arity (next entry after an all-dead one), provider-health filtering (depth axis 1 of the inner scan), and route-health filtering (depth axis 2 of the inner scan). Adding synthetic unit pins for the delegate wiring would just duplicate that coverage.

The cascade proves `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` is on the hot path of `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s last-resort scan exactly as M60's tier-widening comment claims — sabotaging it collapses the whole last-resort fallback through the `No healthy model route found` exit. ### M71: three sites (`computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` agent tool reader, `provider.models` openrouter hook short-circuit, internal `isProviderHealthy` boolean predicate) each encoded the same `providerHealthMap.get(...)` + `until > now` expiry boundary in a slightly different return shape — M70's route-level reader-sweep had no provider-level counterpart, so a future refinement of expiry semantics would have to land at three sites with nothing forcing the update `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: three sites in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` duplicated the same provider-level "live penalty" check — `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` at lines 1788-1795 (the `list_curated_models` tool reader that surfaces provider-scope blocks to the agent; inline `providerHealthMap.get(primaryRoute.provider)` + `providerHealth && providerHealth.until > now` + return `{state, until, scope: "provider"}`), the `provider.models` openrouter hook at lines 3384-3387 (inline `providerHealthMap.get(OPENROUTER_PROVIDER_ID)` + `health && health.until > now` + `return {}`), and the internal `isProviderHealthy` boolean predicate at lines 1812-1821 (inline `providerHealthMap.get(providerID)` + `health.until <= now` as the healthy-when-no-entry-or-expired negation). Each one encoded the SAME `until > now` expiry boundary in a different return shape: one returned the entry for scope reporting, one returned empty-object to short-circuit opencode's model map, one returned a bool for the leaf predicate used by `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` and `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry`. M70 had just extracted `findLiveRoutePenalty` as the route-level analog of exactly this shape (entry-or-null with `until <= now` expiry), but the provider-level sweep was left for a follow-up — three provider-level sites kept encoding the boundary inline.
- **Reachability**: latent drift vector, same class as M64-M70. No current live divergence — all three sites correctly use `until > now` today so their filter/report output agrees. The value is structural: any future refinement of the expiry boundary (a grace window, a boundary flip from `>` to `>=` for tick-aligned wall clocks, a new permanent state beyond `key_missing`, a `retryCount > 0` clause to suppress freshly-installed entries) would have to be replicated at all three sites, with the next writer-side refinement silently skipping any site that was overlooked. Additionally, `isProviderHealthy` is the canonical boolean leaf that `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy`, `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry`, `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`, `findPreferredHealthyRoute`, `countHealthyVisibleRoutes`, `recommendTaskModelRoute`, and `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` all eventually consult — a boundary drift here propagates through the entire route-selection graph, so keeping the predicate and the entry-returning readers in a single definition site is load-bearing for the whole system.

The `isProviderHealthy` refactor intentionally leaves the function non-exported — it's still an internal boolean convenience at the leaf of the route-selection graph — but now both the boolean predicate and the entry-returning readers share a single expiry-boundary definition site.

### M69: the `health.until > now && isAgentVisibleHealthState(health.state)` predicate was inlined across six sites (`hasAgentVisiblePenalty` provider+route loops, `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` provider+route loops, `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` provider+route filters) — structurally identical drift risk to M64's `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` extraction, plus a duplicate 8-line comment block in `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` from an earlier copy-paste that nobody noticed `✅ COMPLETED`

### M68: the four route-level health writers each inlined the write-through pair `modelRouteHealthMap.set(routeKey, health); void persistProviderHealth(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap);` — a durability invariant (set + persist must happen together, or the penalty dies on plugin reload) enforced only by convention, so a future fifth writer that omits the persist call would silently produce penalties that work for a few minutes and then vanish on the next bounce `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: four event-hook writers in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` each inlined the two-line write-through pair after calling `buildRouteHealthEntry` / `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` or `finalizeHungSessionState`: `session.error` model-not-found path (pre-M68 line 3354-3355), `assistant.message.completed` zero-token-quota path (3423-3424), `chat.params` early-fire test timeout path (3478-3479), and the `chat.params` setTimeout hang-detector callback (3509-3510). Each site did `modelRouteHealthMap.set(routeKey, health); void persistProviderHealth(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap);`. The pair is a durability invariant, not a convenience — the map-set alone keeps the penalty in memory for the current plugin instance, but drops it on plugin reload, plugin crash, or cross-process handoff (dr-repo and letta-workspace shims share the same on-disk state file via opencode's plugin mechanism). Any writer that forgets the persist call produces penalties that work locally for the remainder of the process lifetime and then silently vanish on the next bounce. Pre-M68 the pairing was enforced by convention: each of the four writers carried both lines because the author of the original `session.error` handler wrote them together, and subsequent writers copy-pasted the pattern. Nothing prevented a fifth writer (a new health state, a new event hook, a test harness, a shim-level override) from landing only half of the pair and producing the exact "why is this known-dead route being tried again after a restart?" telemetry class that's impossible to reproduce from a unit test.
- **Reachability**: latent drift vector with the worst failure-mode shape of any M55-M68 fix. The symptom is invisible to unit tests (which never touch the plugin-reload path), invisible to integration tests (which construct fresh state each run), and manifests only as intermittent "route I penalized two hours ago is being retried as if it were healthy" telemetry noise across plugin reloads. Three conditions make the fix preventative rather than reactive: (1) all four current writers correctly invoke the pair, so no live bug; (2) the plugin factory exports `persistProviderHealth` as an inner closure that captures both maps, making it trivial for a future writer to call `map.set` and forget the matching persist call; (3) there is no TypeScript-level guarantee that `set` and `persist` happen together — the invariant lives entirely in the author's attention. M68 names the boundary so the next writer has one place to route through and cannot silently half-implement the pair.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `recordRouteHealthPenalty(modelRouteHealthMap, providerHealthMap, routeKey, health, persistFn)` in the helper module. The helper takes `persistFn` as an injected dependency (typed `PersistProviderHealthFn`) so tests can pass a spy instead of touching the real atomic-write path in `persistProviderHealth` (which does mkdir, tmp-file write, atomic rename, unlink-on-failure cleanup — all orthogonal to the invariant the helper enforces). Added a 70-line docstring enumerating the four pre-M68 writers, the cross-process durability semantics behind the pairing, and the reason the side effect is injected rather than captured. Replaced all four inline write-through pairs with five-argument `recordRouteHealthPenalty(...)` calls. Added `PersistProviderHealthFn` type export so overlay shims and future writers can reference it without importing the inner closure. Net LoC: helper +86 (2-line body + 70-line docstring + 7-line type), writer sites +8 (four calls expanded from 2 lines each to 7-line call blocks with proper formatting — a slight size regression at each call site, offset by the boundary enforcement).
- **Tests**: added three new unit pins above the M67 `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_*` cluster in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenCalled_writesHealthToRouteMap` (map-set invariant — the new entry lands under the exact routeKey passed in), `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnWithBothMaps` (**the durability-pairing pin** — uses a spy to verify the persist function is invoked exactly once with both the live provider map AND the live route map as reference-equal arguments, so the persister serializes the post-write state), and `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenMapHasExistingEntry_overwritesItBeforePersistFires` (write-ordering pin — a spy reads the live map at persist-call time and confirms the overwrite is already visible, so the set-then-persist order is preserved even if someone reorders the helper body).
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by deleting the `void persistFn(...)` line from the helper body — the exact class of drift M68 prevents, where a future writer omits the persist call and produces a working-in-memory-but-dead-on-reload penalty. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures fired** — `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenCalled_invokesPersistFnWithBothMaps` (persistCalls was 0, expected 1) and `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenMapHasExistingEntry_overwritesItBeforePersistFires` (snapshotAtPersist was undefined because the spy was never invoked). The first pin guarantees the pair is enforced; the second pin guarantees the pair is also in the right order. `recordRouteHealthPenalty_whenCalled_writesHealthToRouteMap` continued to pass under the broken helper because the map-set is still happening — it's the persist half that was deleted. This is the expected pattern: the three pins cover the three axes of the invariant (write happens, persist happens, write happens BEFORE persist), so one deletion hits two pins and leaves the third as a sanity check. Restored the fix, **208/208 pass** (205 pre-M68 + 3 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `PersistProviderHealthFn` type export, new `recordRouteHealthPenalty` helper with full docstring, four call sites in `session.error` model-not-found handler, `assistant.message.completed` zero-token-quota handler, `chat.params` early-fire test timeout path, and `chat.params` setTimeout hang-detector callback rewritten to delegate), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `recordRouteHealthPenalty` import, three new unit pins). No existing test changes — the four writer sites' integration coverage stays in the factory-level tests.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated write-through path. No production behavior change — all four writers already carry both lines of the pair, so map contents and persistence timing are identical. Value is structural: the durability invariant now lives behind a named boundary (`recordRouteHealthPenalty`) with its own regression tests, so the next writer added to the plugin has one place to route through and the spy-based pins guarantee any future refactor that accidentally drops the persist half fails loudly in unit tests rather than silently dropping penalties in production.

### M67: four route-level health writers each inlined the same three-step composite-key lookup — `composeRouteKey({provider: providerID, model: modelID})` → `modelRouteHealthMap.get(...)` → pass as `existing` to `buildRouteHealthEntry`/`buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` — duplicating the exact M30 drift shape the `composeRouteKey` helper was introduced to fix, and silently risking the M43 preserve-longer invariant if any writer ever diverged from the canonical key construction `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: four independent route-level health writers in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` each inlined the same composite-key lookup before invoking `buildRouteHealthEntry` / `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth`: `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` (line 1337-1346 pre-M67, the pure hang-timer helper), the `session.error` model-not-found path (3212-3219), the `assistant.message.completed` zero-token-quota path (3281-3290), and the `chat.params` early-fire test timeout path (3328-3337). All four built `modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey({provider: providerID, model: modelID}))` as the `existing` argument to the builder. This is structurally identical to the M30 bug that introduced `composeRouteKey` in the first place: pre-M30, writers inlined `${providerID}/${model.id}` directly and longcat's unprefixed registry entries produced mismatched keys where writes landed at `"longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat"` (composite) but reads looked for `"LongCat-Flash-Chat"` (raw), silently invisible route-level penalties. M30 fixed it by routing both sides through `composeRouteKey`, but only at the existing inline sites — nothing prevented a future writer from inventing its own key shape, and the four current writers each independently agreed on the correct shape with no named boundary enforcing the agreement. Any future writer forgetting to wrap `{provider, model}` in `composeRouteKey` would silently get `undefined`, the builder would start fresh at `retryCount = 1`, and the M43 preserve-longer merge invariant ("a longer `model_not_found` penalty must dominate a shorter `quota` writer arriving a moment later") would silently evaporate for that writer's events.
- **Reachability**: latent drift vector; no observable divergence in today's tree because all four writers currently agree on the composite-key shape. The risk is the shape of the bug, not its current instance: the M30 regression (longcat penalties silently invisible) happened exactly because multiple sites independently built their own key and one site forgot to canonicalize. Today's four writers agree by convention, not by boundary — the next writer added (a fifth retry handler, a schema-drift handler, a test harness) has nothing forcing it through the canonical lookup. Verify-on-HEAD (below) proves that a naive `${providerID}/${modelID}` shape silently regresses the `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` integration path for the exact M43 preserve-longer invariant — the retry counter resets to 1 instead of incrementing the existing entry's counter, so repeated hangs become invisible to the health telemetry and the longer-lived penalty is silently overwritten.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerID, modelID)` next to `composeRouteKey` in the helper module. The helper is a two-line wrapper that composes the key and performs the map read, but the point is the boundary: future writers are forced through the one place that documents the key convention. Replaced all four inline composite-key-lookup triplets with `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers(modelRouteHealthMap, providerID, modelID)` as the `existing` argument to the builder. Added a 60-line docstring on the new helper enumerating the four pre-M67 writers, the M30 drift history that motivates centralization, and the M43 preserve-longer invariant that depends on correct lookups. Net LoC in the factory body: -12 (four inline 3-line triplets collapsed to one-line calls), +66 in the helper section (2-line function body + 60-line docstring explaining why the boundary matters).
- **Tests**: added four new unit pins to `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` directly above the `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeIdIsRawAndRegistryIsComposite_returnsEntry` block, colocated with the existing `composeRouteKey_whenRegistryEntryIsUnprefixed_producesCompositeKey` regression pin so the boundary test cluster stays close: `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenEntryStoredUnderCompositeKey_returnsEntry` (happy path — writer stored at composite key, reader finds it), `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenModelIsAlreadyCompositePrefixed_doesNotDoubleNest` (idempotence — registry entries whose `model` already contains the provider prefix, like `ollama-cloud/glm-5`, must not produce `ollama-cloud/ollama-cloud/glm-5`), `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenNoEntryExists_returnsUndefined` (miss shape — `undefined` so the builder starts retry counter at 1), and `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenLongcatEntryIsUnprefixed_findsCompositeKey` (the exact M30 drift shape — reader passes raw `LongCat-Flash-Chat`, writer stored at `longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat`, the helper must normalize so the write-side and read-side see the same key).
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing `composeRouteKey(...)` inside the helper with a naive `${providerID}/${modelID}` inline build — the exact pre-M30 drift shape that produces double-nested `"ollama-cloud/ollama-cloud/glm-5"` keys and raw `"LongCat-Flash-Chat"` lookups when the registry stores composite-prefixed models. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures fired** — `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers_whenModelIsAlreadyCompositePrefixed_doesNotDoubleNest` (unit pin for idempotence) and, critically, `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_whenSessionHung_returnsTimeoutEntry` at line 3608 (**an existing integration pin** that checks the retry counter increments: expected `retryCount: 5`, got `1` because the broken helper returned `undefined`, the builder started fresh, and the M43 preserve-longer invariant silently lost the existing `retryCount: 4` state). The second failure is the exact class of bug M67 is designed to prevent — a pre-existing integration test, written for M43 preserve-longer, catches the regression immediately. This is a clean verify-on-HEAD: one new unit pin proves the helper's idempotence contract, and one existing integration pin proves the downstream invariant depends on the canonical lookup. Restored the fix, **205/205 pass** (201 pre-M67 + 4 new unit pins). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers` helper with full docstring, four call sites in `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty`, the `session.error` model-not-found handler, the `assistant.message.completed` zero-token-quota handler, and the `chat.params` early-fire test timeout path rewritten to delegate), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (new `lookupRouteHealthByIdentifiers` import, four new unit pins). No test rewrites — existing `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_*` integration suite is the downstream regression guard.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated writer path. No production behavior change — all four writers currently agree on the key shape, so route-level penalty writes produce identical map entries. Value is structural: the M30 `composeRouteKey` boundary is now enforced at the caller-facing helper, not just at the inline writers' discretion, so the next writer added to the plugin has one named place to route through and cannot silently invent a new key shape.

### M66: `findCuratedFallbackRoute` was the seventh inline copy of the `(provider healthy) AND (route expired/absent)` predicate — deliberately kept inline by the M64 docstring because its upfront `blockedProviderID` + `isFallbackBlocked` guards are strictly stronger, but the tail of the check is byte-for-byte `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy`, so the "strictly stronger" argument only justified keeping the prefix guards, not keeping the suffix inlined, and the same drift risk the M64/M65 sweeps closed applies here too `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findCuratedFallbackRoute` at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:1362-1372` (pre-M66) ran four checks in sequence inside its `visibleRoutes.find(...)` lambda: (1) `providerRoute.provider === blockedProviderID` exclude, (2) `isFallbackBlocked(...)` exclude, (3) `isProviderHealthy(...)` negate, (4) `modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey(...))` expired-or-absent. Checks (3) and (4) together are exactly the `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` helper extracted in M64. The M64 dedupe helper docstring explicitly called out `findCuratedFallbackRoute` as "deliberately does NOT delegate (it adds `isFallbackBlocked` for strictly-stronger 'valid fallback' semantics)" — but that justification only applies to the prefix guards (1) and (2); it does NOT justify keeping (3)+(4) inline, because those two lines are the canonical predicate M64 tried to consolidate. So the file shipped M64+M65 with seven call sites of the pattern, six delegating and one inlined under a misleading rationale. Structurally identical latent-drift risk to M65: a future health-state refinement lands in `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` and every consumer inherits it, but `findCuratedFallbackRoute` silently skips the change and returns the wrong answer for exactly the inputs that exercise the new behavior. Today's tree has no observable divergence — the inline suffix and the helper agree on current inputs — but the single-source-of-truth boundary M64 tried to establish is still half-porous.
- **Reachability**: latent drift vector, not a live symptom in today's tree. The fallback loop is traversed every time `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` emits a "Curated fallback for X:" line (each penalized route generates one), and every time `handleFallbackSelection` walks registry entries looking for a non-blocked visible route when a primary goes down. Both callers currently produce correct output because the inline suffix and `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` agree. The fix is preventative: it makes M64's "one place to land the next drift" invariant actually true across all seven sites.
- **Fix**: replaced the two-line inline tail (`isProviderHealthy(...)` + `modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey(...))` + `routeHealth.until > now` check) with a single `return isRouteCurrentlyHealthy(providerRoute, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` call. The prefix guards (`blockedProviderID` short-circuit, `isFallbackBlocked` short-circuit) stay inline as-is because they genuinely do not belong in the canonical predicate — they answer "is this a valid fallback destination" which is strictly stronger than "is this route currently routable". Added an M66 block comment at the call site documenting why the split is correct (prefix = fallback-specific policy, suffix = canonical health predicate) and pointing forward consumers at the M64 Completion Notes for the drift history. Net LoC: -3 (removed the two-line inline tail, added one delegated call).
- **Tests**: no new tests added — two existing integration pins already guard this site. `findCuratedFallbackRoute_whenRouteIsMarkedUnhealthyAtRouteLevel_skipsIt` at line 518 constructs an entry where the top route has a live `modelRouteHealthMap` penalty and asserts the fallback walks past it to the next route — this pins the route-level half of `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy`. `findCuratedFallbackRoute_whenNextRouteIsHiddenPaidProvider_skipsToVisibleRoute` at line 456 pins the visible-route filtering that sits above the predicate. Both pins fire under the refactor because the delegation is observationally identical, and both pins fire under a broken inline copy (confirmed below).
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the new `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy(...)` call with `isProviderHealthy(providerHealthMap, providerRoute.provider, now)` — i.e. reverting the suffix to the pre-M29 provider-only check that ignores `modelRouteHealthMap`. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **exactly 2 expected failures** fired — `findCuratedFallbackRoute_whenRouteIsMarkedUnhealthyAtRouteLevel_skipsIt` (broken inline returned the unhealthy route as a valid fallback) and `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyRoutePenaltiesExist_emitsRouteSection` (which uses `findCuratedFallbackRoute` internally to pick the "Curated fallback for X:" recommendation string and got the wrong route). This confirms (a) both pins are genuinely live against this call site, and (b) the M66 refactor is correctly wired through the helper. Restored the fix, **201/201 pass**.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (one call site in `findCuratedFallbackRoute` rewritten to delegate the suffix to `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy`, with an M66 block comment explaining the prefix/suffix split). No test file changes — existing pins at lines 456 and 518 cover the regression.
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated call site. No production behavior change — the inline suffix and the helper agree on current input shapes. Value is structural: M64's single-source-of-truth invariant now actually holds across all seven call sites of the route-health predicate, so the next drift event has exactly one named place to land.

### M65: `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` inlined the `(provider healthy) AND (route health expired or absent)` predicate at line 1987-1992, missed by the M64 dedupe sweep — a stray 7th call site of the same pattern M64 consolidated across six others, so the single-source-of-truth boundary M64 tried to establish was still porous and the next drift event would land one-of-seven instead of hitting the canonical helper `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:1986-1993` (pre-M65) walked `filterVisibleProviderRoutes(entry.provider_order).find(...)` with an inline `isProviderHealthy + modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey(...)).until > now` two-step check. This is structurally identical to the six call sites M64 (commit `d1b4b91`) deduped through the new `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` helper — the exact same predicate, the exact same drift history (M29 route-level health, M31 composite route keys, M61 per-entry walk), the exact same potential for one-site-drift to silently leak past a future audit. The M64 sweep walked the file looking for inline copies of the pattern but missed this one because it was nested inside a longer function body that also did role-bucketing and billing-mode decoration — the inline predicate was ~5 lines buried in a 30-line function, easy to overlook when scanning for 3-line lambda patterns. The consequence isn't a live user-facing symptom in today's tree (the inline copy happens to agree with `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` — M27 already centralized the correct shape here), but the refactoring value M64 tried to deliver ("single source of truth for the predicate so future drift lands in one named place") was silently undermined: six call sites went through the helper and one did not, so a future maintainer adding a new health state or a new expiration policy would see six sites to update and miss the seventh, reintroducing the exact drift pattern M64 closed.

The post-M27 inline predicate in `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` matches the `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` behavior byte-for-byte, so the current tree's `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` output is unchanged. The value is structural: the next time someone touches the predicate (e.g. adds an `isStructuralPlumbingState` gate to hide operator-required states, adds a new health enum member, or refactors `composeRouteKey` semantics), the helper gains the new behavior and every consumer of it gains it atomically, but a stray inline copy would silently skip the change. The test constructs an entry with a single `iflowcn/dead-model` visible route, writes a `model_not_found` penalty into `modelRouteHealthMap` with `until: now + 60_000`, and asserts `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` returns `null`. Under the refactor, `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` walks the visible routes, `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` checks `providerHealthMap` (empty, returns healthy) then `modelRouteHealthMap.get("iflowcn/dead-model")` (returns a live penalty), the predicate returns false, no healthy route is found, the entry is skipped, the `roleToModels` map stays empty, and the function returns `null`. The existing test is therefore the integration pin for the M65 delegation — it proves the refactor is wired through the helper and honors the `modelRouteHealthMap` the helper reads.

### M64: six readers of the `(provider healthy) AND (route health expired or absent)` predicate inlined the two-step check instead of going through a shared helper, so every past centralization milestone (M29 adding route-level health, M31 canonicalizing composite route keys, M61 extracting the per-entry walk) had to land a duplicate edit at every call site or the predicate drifted — the current tree already had one live divergence (`findCuratedFallbackRoute` adds `isFallbackBlocked`, nobody else does) and six equivalent inlines waiting for the next drift opportunity `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: six independent call sites in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` duplicated the same "is this route currently routable" predicate — `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` (line 1422-1424 pre-M64), `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth` inner loop (1176-1187), `findPreferredHealthyRoute`'s `isRouteHealthy` lambda (2533-2537), `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` (2610-2612), `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s `bestRouteIsHealthy` lambda (2725-2729), and `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes`'s `isRouteHealthy` lambda from M62 (1491-1495). Every one of them reimplemented the exact same two-step check: `isProviderHealthy(providerHealthMap, route.provider, now)` AND `modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey(route))` is expired-or-absent. The historical audit trail shows the drift risk is real, not hypothetical: M29 introduced the route-level health map and had to touch every call site to add the second half of the check; M31 canonicalized composite route keys via `composeRouteKey` and had to walk every site that built route keys; M61 extracted `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` as the first named helper for this predicate but only for single-entry lookups — the other five sites were left inlined. The current tree already has one live semantic divergence downstream of this pattern: `findCuratedFallbackRoute` at line 1303-1337 deliberately adds an `isFallbackBlocked(route.provider, route.model)` clause (so proprietary providers like `anthropic`, `openai`, `xai`, `longcat` never appear as silent fallbacks even when their routes are healthy), but no other reader has this clause because "is a valid fallback" is a strictly stronger question than "is routable right now". That divergence is intentional — but the fact that it lives as an inline difference instead of a documented abstraction boundary means future readers can't tell which predicate shape to copy. The next drift event (a new health state, a new sentinel value, a new expiration policy) has six places to land and one explicitly-different cousin to ignore, and whatever site the author forgets silently starts returning the wrong answer for exactly the inputs that exercise the drift.
- **Reachability**: reachable today only as a *latent* bug — no user-facing symptom in the current tree, because the six inline copies happen to agree. But every past audit of this file that touched the predicate found at least one inline copy that had drifted: M29 found `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`'s predecessor checking only provider health (route-level penalties were invisible to the last-resort scan), M31 found multiple sites building route keys as `${provider}/${model}` instead of using `composeRouteKey` (so already-prefixed longcat model ids produced zombie keys nobody could ever look up), and M61 found `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` reporting an entry as blocked whenever its PRIMARY was dead even when sibling visible routes were healthy. Each of those bugs is the same pattern: the predicate is duplicated at N sites, one site drifts, and the drift is invisible until a user hits the exact input shape the drifted site handles wrong. M64 closes the reachability window before the next drift lands — the call sites now *can't* disagree by construction, because they all share the same function body.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy(providerRoute, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now): boolean` placed immediately above `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth` at line 1100, with a full docstring that (a) enumerates the six previously-inline call sites, (b) explains the drift history (M29/M31/M61) as the motivation, and (c) explicitly documents why `findCuratedFallbackRoute` does NOT delegate to the helper — its `isFallbackBlocked` clause makes "valid fallback" a strictly stronger question than "routable right now", and keeping that divergence explicit via a named function boundary (instead of an inline difference) lets the two predicates evolve independently. The helper composes `isProviderHealthy` (which is already the canonical "does this provider have an active penalty" check, including the `key_missing`-is-unhealthy M58 semantics) with a single `modelRouteHealthMap.get(composeRouteKey(route))` expiration check. Route-key composition goes through `composeRouteKey` so the M31 write/read symmetry invariant is preserved even when callers pass an unprefixed `route.model` (longcat's `LongCat-Flash-Chat` shape). Updated the six call sites to delegate: `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` collapses to a single `if (isRouteCurrentlyHealthy(route, ...)) return route;` loop body; `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth`'s accumulator loop becomes a 3-line if/else; `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`'s inner loop mirrors `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry`; `findPreferredHealthyRoute` drops its `isRouteHealthy` lambda and inlines the helper call in both the exact-match and fallback `.find` predicates; `recommendTaskModelRoute` drops its `bestRouteIsHealthy` lambda and inlines the helper in the `visibleRoutes.find` call; `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes` drops its `isRouteHealthy` lambda (the M62 addition) and inlines the helper in the `.map` that builds `alternativeRoutes`. Net LoC: -23 (six duplicate inline checks removed, plus four now-unused lambda declarations collapsed).
- **Tests**: six new unit tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`, placed immediately above the `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_*` cluster so the helper contract and its primary consumer sit in one chapter:
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenNeitherProviderNorRouteBlocked_returnsTrue` — baseline empty-maps pin.
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenProviderKeyMissing_returnsFalse` — post-M58 `key_missing` with `until: POSITIVE_INFINITY` pin, confirms the helper correctly delegates to `isProviderHealthy` for the permanent-plumbing case.
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenProviderHealthExpired_returnsTrue` — stale-entry pin, a `providerHealth.until < now` is treated as expired (guards against the pre-M31 `providerHealthMap.has(id)` shape that would incorrectly flag expired entries as unhealthy).
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenRouteLevelPenaltyActive_returnsFalse` — M29 regression pin: provider-level check passes but the composite route-health entry blocks the specific route, ensures the helper walks BOTH maps not just the provider one.
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenRouteLevelPenaltyExpired_returnsTrue` — expired-route-entry pin, symmetric with the provider-expired pin.
  - `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenRouteKeyComposedFromPlainModelID_matchesComposedForm` — **M31 regression pin**: longcat's unprefixed `LongCat-Flash-Chat` model id is penalized under its canonical `longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat` composite key; the helper must find the penalty regardless of whether the incoming `route.model` was prefixed. Guards against the pre-M31 bug where writers and readers built the key differently and penalties leaked into zombie map entries.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the helper body with a broken implementation that checks ONLY provider health (`return isProviderHealthy(providerHealthMap, providerRoute.provider, now)`, ignoring the `modelRouteHealthMap` parameter entirely — identical in shape to the pre-M29 bug). Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`: **12 expected failures** fired across the new helper unit tests AND every downstream call site that exercises route-level penalties. The helper-level pins `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenRouteLevelPenaltyActive_returnsFalse` and `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy_whenRouteKeyComposedFromPlainModelID_matchesComposedForm` caught the contract break directly, and the integration-level pins in the `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_*`, `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_*`, `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_*`, and `recommendTaskModelRoute_*` clusters caught the downstream misbehavior (e.g. `recommendTaskModelRoute_whenComplexityTierFullyDownButSiblingTierHealthy_degradesToSiblingTier` returned the wrong sibling because the route-level penalty on the complexity-tier route was invisible). 12 failures across 6 call sites confirms every dedupe target has at least one pin that proves it's using the helper and not a leftover inline copy — the whole point of a consolidation refactor is pinning the call sites to the helper, and verify-on-HEAD shows they're all pinned. Restored the helper, **201/201 pass** (195 pre-M64 + 6 new). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` helper with full docstring covering the M29/M31/M61 drift history and the deliberate `findCuratedFallbackRoute` divergence; six call sites updated to delegate — `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth`, `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry`, `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes`, `findPreferredHealthyRoute`, `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute`, `recommendTaskModelRoute`), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (6 new unit tests pinning the helper contract + added `isRouteCurrentlyHealthy` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the consolidated predicate. No production behavior change in the current tree — the six inline copies all agreed on the predicate, so the helper extraction is observationally identical. The value is structural: the next drift event (new health state, changed expiration policy, new sentinel value) now has one place to land instead of six, and the helper docstring serves as the canonical reference for "is this route routable right now" so reviewers of future patches can point at a named boundary instead of chasing the predicate shape across six inline copies.

### M63: `get_quota_backoff_status` tool handler iterated `providerHealthMap.entries()` without filtering `key_missing`, so post-M58 every call on a freshly-booted plugin dumped the entire 15–25-entry boot-time key_missing roster into the tool output labeled as "currently penalized" providers, making the tool useless for answering the one question its name advertises ("what's broken right now that I should avoid?") — agents calling the tool got handed a permanent-plumbing dump indistinguishable from a genuine outage `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `get_quota_backoff_status` at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:2975-3000` (pre-M63) iterated `providerHealthMap.entries()` and `modelRouteHealthMap.entries()` inline, emitting every entry with `health.until > now` into the status payload. Pre-M58 this was correct — the only way an entry landed in either map was via a live transient failure event (`quota`/`key_dead`/`no_credit`/`model_not_found`/`timeout`), so "live entry" and "agent-actionable backoff" were the same set. M58 (commit `9b125b5`) changed the invariant: `initializeProviderHealthState` now installs a `key_missing` entry with `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` for every uncredentialed curated provider at boot — typically 15–25 entries on a default install. `until > now` is permanently true for every `key_missing` entry, so every post-M58 call to `get_quota_backoff_status` on a freshly-booted plugin returned something like `{"iflowcn": {state: "key_missing", until: "never", type: "provider", retryCount: 0}, "opencode": {state: "key_missing", until: "never", ...}, ...}` for the entire roster, labeled as "currently penalized" providers. The tool's description explicitly says "Return all LLM providers currently penalized (quota backoff, dead key, no credit) and when they expire" — the contract is "transient backoffs the agent might plausibly retry through". `key_missing` is permanent plumbing state that requires operator action (run oauth, set env var); the agent has no routing alternative to "retry through" it. Same bug class as M59 (`buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`) and M60 (`buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` + `experimental.chat.system.transform`) at the tool-output layer: a narrow predicate (`until > now`) silently misbehaves under the post-M58 map invariant because the layer doesn't distinguish "live transient penalty" from "permanent plumbing presence".
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every agent call to the tool post-M58 on a freshly-booted plugin with any uncredentialed curated providers. The tool is exposed via `tool()` in the plugin handler set and is part of the agent-visible tool catalog advertised to every session that can read the tool. Agents invoke it to answer concrete questions like "is there a quota backoff active right now I should route around" or "why did the last inference fail with a 401" — and instead of getting the one actionable transient penalty they were looking for, they got a 15–25-entry dump with `until: "never"` on every entry, which is uninterpretable as a backoff list (nothing expires, so there's nothing to retry past). Worse than M59/M60's noise because this is a tool the agent *explicitly queries* when it wants authoritative health information: the agent's mental model of "call get_quota_backoff_status when confused" is directly contradicted by the tool returning permanent plumbing dressed up as transient backoffs. Same audit shape as M48–M62: post-M58 fills `providerHealthMap` with a new class of entries, and every old narrow-predicate reader silently starts emitting them into its output.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that returns a `Record<string, {state, until, type, retryCount}>` with one entry per agent-visible live penalty. The helper filters on BOTH `health.until > now` AND `isAgentVisibleHealthState(health.state)` (the M59 filter that returns `false` for `key_missing` and `true` for the transient set). Composes with `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` / `isAgentVisibleHealthState` so the "agent-visible vs permanent plumbing" distinction lives in a single named place across the codebase — every agent-facing output channel now goes through the same filter. Expired entries are skipped but NOT deleted from the maps; the helper is pure with no side effects, and map cleanup is the job of the dedicated `expireHealthMaps` helper, which the tool handler now calls separately before building the status payload. This is a small correctness improvement on top of the headline fix: pre-M63 the handler did inline `.delete()` calls while iterating the map, which is safe under JS Map mutation-during-iteration semantics but mixed rendering and bookkeeping in one pass, and the mixed pass was the exact shape where the key_missing filter was missing. Rewrote the tool handler as a thin wrapper: `expireHealthMaps(...)` for cleanup, then `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus(...)` for the filtered payload, then `JSON.stringify`.
- **Tests**: six new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`, placed near the existing `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_*` cluster so the M59/M60/M63 filters sit in one chapter:
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenBothMapsEmpty_returnsEmpty` — baseline empty pin.
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenOnlyKeyMissingEntries_returnsEmpty` — **headline integration pin**: post-M58 fresh-boot shape with three key_missing providers (iflowcn, opencode, kimi-for-coding — exact shipping shape), expects an empty object.
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenLiveQuotaPenalty_includesProviderEntry` — happy-path transient penalty pin, asserts the full `{state, until, type: "provider", retryCount}` shape and a non-"never" `until` string.
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenMixedKeyMissingAndLiveQuota_filtersKeyMissingOnly` — **sibling mixed pin**: the exact M59/M60 regression guard, prevents the M63 filter from collapsing into "suppress everything when key_missing is present". With one live quota and two key_missing entries, only the quota entry is emitted.
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenRouteLevelPenaltyLive_includesRouteEntry` — route-level penalty pin with `type: "model_route"`, ensures the M63 refactor preserved the pre-M27 route-health coverage the original handler added.
  - `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenEntriesExpired_excludesExpired` — defensive expired-entry pin, guards against callers who forget to run `expireHealthMaps` first; the tool description says "currently penalized" and expired is not current.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the `isAgentVisibleHealthState` filter in `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` (leaving the helper structure, the export, the expired-entry check, and the tool handler's caller wiring intact) and re-running `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Exactly **2 expected failures** fired: `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenOnlyKeyMissingEntries_returnsEmpty` (headline integration pin) and `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus_whenMixedKeyMissingAndLiveQuota_filtersKeyMissingOnly` (sibling mixed pin). Both are tests that assert on `key_missing` being filtered out; under the reverted helper, `key_missing` entries leak into the output and the assertion `Object.keys(result).length === 1` catches the extra entries. The other four new tests still passed against the reverted helper: the empty-map baseline is unrelated to filtering, the live-quota pin has no key_missing entries (so the filter is a no-op), the route-level pin uses only a route penalty, and the expired-entry pin exercises the `until <= now` check which is orthogonal to the filter. All pre-M63 tests continued to pass. Restored the fix, 195/195 pass (189 pre-M63 + 6 new). `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` helper with full docstring covering the post-M58 invariant change and the M59/M60/M63 lineage; `get_quota_backoff_status` tool handler rewritten to call `expireHealthMaps` then the new helper, with a block comment pointing at the helper's docstring), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (6 new tests + added `buildAgentVisibleBackoffStatus` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the tool-output fix. Production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: every agent calling `get_quota_backoff_status` between boot and the first successful oauth handshake on each curated provider stops seeing the full key_missing roster in the tool output and starts seeing an empty object (or just the transient entries that are genuinely live). Agents that used the tool's output to decide whether to fall back or retry stop acting on phantom backoffs. No behavior change when real transient penalties are active — those continue to surface identically. No behavior change for the rest of the plugin's routing logic, which consults `providerHealthMap` via `isProviderHealthy` and already skips key_missing providers at decision time; this fix only affects the agent-visible rendering layer, matching the M59/M60 pattern.

### M62: `recommend_model_for_role` tool handler hardcoded `filterVisibleProviderRoutes(best.provider_order)[0]` as `primaryRoute`, so post-M58 on the shipping `config/models.jsonc` shape where `opencode/*-free` is the primary and `iflowcn/*` the secondary, the tool returned a permanently `key_missing` route in the single slot it is supposed to populate with a working recommendation, and agents calling the tool had to parse `alternativeRoutes` to find something usable — defeating the tool's entire "hand me ONE concrete route" contract and introducing exactly the class of agent-confusion bugs M59/M60 fixed at the system-prompt-builder layer `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `recommend_model_for_role` tool handler at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:2848-2874` (pre-M62) computed `const visibleRoutes = filterVisibleProviderRoutes(best.provider_order); const primaryRoute = visibleRoutes[0] ?? null;` and then reported that slot as `primaryRoute` with `primaryProviderHealthy: isRouteHealthy(primaryRoute)` — hardcoded to array index 0 regardless of whether that position was actually routable. `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` (line 2496, post-M29) already walks `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` and confirms at least one healthy visible route exists before returning an entry, so `best` always had a routable sibling somewhere; the tool handler just ignored the walk and exposed `visibleRoutes[0]` directly. Post-M58 (commit `9b125b5`) `initializeProviderHealthState` started installing `key_missing` entries at boot for every uncredentialed curated provider, and for any entry whose `provider_order[0]` lives on an uncredentialed provider — exactly the shipping shape in `config/models.jsonc` where `glm-5.1` is `opencode/glm-5.1-free` (priority 1) + `iflowcn/glm-5.1` (priority 2), and `opencode` is `key_missing` on any freshly-booted plugin that hasn't run oauth — the tool returned `{recommendation: {primaryRoute: "opencode/glm-5.1-free", primaryProviderHealthy: false, ...}, alternativeRoutes: [{route: "iflowcn/glm-5.1", healthy: true}]}`. This is a SINGLE-recommendation tool; its entire purpose (per its own description: "Return the single best currently-available model for a role and/or task" and "Use this instead of select_models_for_role when you need one concrete recommendation") is to hand the agent ONE working route. Instead it was handing back a dead route and forcing the agent to do its own route-selection walk through `alternativeRoutes`, which is precisely the logic the tool was supposed to encapsulate. Same class as M61 at a different tool-output site: the inner decision (`selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`) walks the visible routes correctly, but the outer presentation layer falls back to `[0]` and undoes the walk.
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every agent turn that calls the tool between boot and the first successful opencode oauth handshake on the shipping `config/models.jsonc`. The tool is exposed via `tool()` in the plugin handler set and is directly callable by any agent that explicitly asks for a single-model recommendation — which in the aicoder-opencode + dr-repo deployment includes the `recommendation_consultant` agent, several of the autopilot scaffolding prompts, and any workflow that uses the tool for manual model pinning. On a freshly-booted plugin with no opencode oauth, EVERY call that lands on an entry with an `opencode/*-free` primary returns a dead route in the primary slot. The failure is silent: the agent receives a tool response that parses correctly, `primaryRoute` is non-null so the agent has no "no route" signal to trigger fallback, and `primaryProviderHealthy: false` is a subtle cue the agent may or may not act on depending on its prompt. Many calls result in the agent attempting inference against the dead route and getting an immediate provider error, which then triggers a separate failure path entirely. The behavioral impact is the same shape as M61: agents silently downgrade quality by acting on stale/broken recommendations, except here the failure mode is more overt because inference actually gets attempted against the dead route.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes(entry, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` that returns `{primaryRoute: ProviderRoute | null, primaryHealthy: boolean, alternativeRoutes: Array<{route: ProviderRoute, healthy: boolean}>}`. The helper calls M61's `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` to pick the first visible route whose provider is healthy AND whose composite-route-key entry is not penalized, promotes that route to `primaryRoute` with `primaryHealthy: true`, and puts every other visible route into `alternativeRoutes` with each route's individual `healthy` flag.
