When every visible route is blocked (a state `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` is supposed to prevent but which we defensively handle), the helper falls back to `visibleRoutes[0]` with `primaryHealthy: false` so the caller still gets a renderable shape and can surface the block reason via `alternativeRoutes`. When the entry has no visible routes at all (hidden-paid-only curation), the helper returns `{primaryRoute: null, primaryHealthy: false, alternativeRoutes: []}` so the tool handler never sees a dangling `undefined` slot. Rewrote the `recommend_model_for_role` tool handler to delegate to the helper: the handler is now a thin wrapper that maps `recommendationRoutes.primaryRoute?.model` to `primaryRoute` and `recommendationRoutes.alternativeRoutes.map(...)` to `alternativeRoutes`, with all routing logic pushed into the helper. The helper itself composes with the M61/M57 `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` + `composeRouteKey` + `isProviderHealthy` stack so the "is this route actually routable" question is answered in a single named place across the codebase.
- **Tests**: five new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenEntryHasNoVisibleRoutes_returnsEmptyPayload` — defensive null/empty-shape pin for hidden-paid-only entries.
  - `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenPrimaryHealthy_returnsPrimaryAndRestAsAlternatives` — happy-path baseline (array order honored when primary is healthy).
  - `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenPrimaryKeyMissingButSiblingHealthy_returnsSiblingAsPrimary` — **headline integration pin**: the exact post-M58 shipping-shape shape, expects `iflowcn` promoted to primary with `primaryHealthy: true` and the demoted `opencode` route present in `alternativeRoutes` with `healthy: false`.
  - `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenPrimaryRouteLevelBlockedButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling` — route-level-penalty variant of the headline pin (model_not_found on the primary instead of provider-level key_missing), pinning the M29/M30 composite-key-read lesson at this helper too.
  - `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenEveryVisibleRouteBlocked_fallsBackToFirstVisibleWithUnhealthyFlag` — defensive fallback pin for the case `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`'s contract ever cracks: the helper must still return a renderable shape with `primaryRoute = visibleRoutes[0]`, `primaryHealthy: false`, and every remaining visible route in `alternativeRoutes`, instead of returning null and forcing the tool handler to special-case a shape it never otherwise sees.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` short-circuit inside `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes` (replacing it with `const primaryRoute = visibleRoutes[0]; const primaryHealthy = isRouteHealthy(primaryRoute); const alternativeRoutes = visibleRoutes.slice(1).map(...)` — the pre-M62 shape) while leaving the helper structure, the export, the caller wiring in the tool handler, and all five new tests intact. Ran `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Exactly **2 expected failures** fired: `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenPrimaryKeyMissingButSiblingHealthy_returnsSiblingAsPrimary` and `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes_whenPrimaryRouteLevelBlockedButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling` — both assert that the helper promotes the first healthy sibling to primary when the primary is blocked. The other three new tests still passed against the reverted helper: the empty-shape pin is unrelated to route walking, the happy-path pin has a healthy primary (so `visibleRoutes[0]` and the correct answer coincide), and the everything-blocked fallback pin's output shape happens to be `visibleRoutes[0]` with `primaryHealthy: false` either way — a deliberate defensive-fallback pin, not a bug-exposer. The sibling negative tests and M61 legacy tests all continued to pass. Restored the fix, `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean (after a `!` non-null narrowing on `visibleRoutes[0]` to satisfy `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` and matching `!` on the new test accesses of `alternativeRoutes[0]`), 189/189 pass (184 pre-M62 + 5 new).
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes` helper with full docstring covering the M58/M59/M60/M61/M62 lineage and the single-recommendation-tool contract; `recommend_model_for_role` tool handler rewritten as a thin wrapper around the helper), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (5 new tests + added `buildRoleRecommendationRoutes` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the tool-output fix. Production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: every agent calling `recommend_model_for_role` between boot and the first successful opencode oauth handshake stops seeing `opencode/*-free` returned as the `primaryRoute` for `opencode`-primary entries and starts seeing the `iflowcn/*` sibling promoted into that slot with `primaryProviderHealthy: true`. Agents that acted on the pre-M62 recommendation by immediately attempting inference stop hitting the provider-level failure and start succeeding on the first try. Agents that used the tool to pick a route and handed it off to a downstream tool stop propagating a dead route further into the pipeline. No behavior change for entries whose primary is genuinely healthy — the helper walks in priority order and the first healthy route IS the primary in that case. No behavior change when every visible route is genuinely blocked — `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`'s own contract prevents that from happening at this call site, and the helper's defensive fallback preserves the renderable shape for the paranoid case.

### M61: `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` reported the primary visible route's state in isolation, so post-M58 any curated entry whose primary lived on an uncredentialed provider (very common on a default install — `opencode/glm-5.1-free` primary with `iflowcn/glm-5.1` sibling is the shipping shape) was marked permanently blocked in `list_curated_models` tool output even though the router transparently served traffic via the healthy sibling, and agents calling the tool avoided entire classes of routable models and silently downgraded quality on every turn `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:1349` (pre-M61) took `visibleRoutes[0]` as "the primary route" and reported only its provider- and route-level health in isolation. That behavior was correct pre-M58 when every entry in `providerHealthMap` represented a live transient failure — the agent got early warning about a degraded primary even when fallback was available. M58 (commit `9b125b5`) changed the invariant: `initializeProviderHealthState` now installs a `key_missing` entry with `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` for every uncredentialed curated provider at boot. For any entry whose `provider_order[0]` happens to land on an uncredentialed provider — including the shipping `config/models.jsonc` shape where `glm-5.1` has `opencode/glm-5.1-free` as the primary and `iflowcn/glm-5.1` as the secondary, and a freshly-booted plugin has the `opencode` provider in `key_missing` until oauth runs — the report became `{state: "key_missing", until: "never", scope: "provider"}` even though the router (via `findCuratedFallbackRoute`, `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` from M57, and the `provider.models` active-route resolution) was happily walking past the key_missing primary to the healthy sibling. `listCuratedModels` exposes this report under each entry's `providerHealth` field in the `list_curated_models` tool output. Agents calling that tool — which includes the control-plane routing recommendations, the select_models_for_role handler, and any agent that deliberately consults the tool to understand what's available — read `providerHealth: {state: "key_missing"}` as authoritative "this entry is permanently blocked, avoid it" and selected inferior alternatives on every turn. The M59/M60 key_missing noise filters apply only to the agent-visible system-prompt builders (`buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`, `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt`); they do NOT touch the tool-output path, which is a separate read channel the agent explicitly queries and treats as authoritative.
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every fresh install running the shipped `config/models.jsonc` until every primary-position provider is credentialed. The `glm-5.1`, `glm-5.2`, and related entries have `opencode/*-free` as their primary visible route, and opencode requires oauth that is often not immediately present after install; `iflowcn/*` siblings are the standard paid-with-credit fallback the router actually uses. Any agent that calls `list_curated_models` between boot and the first successful opencode oauth handshake (a window that can be many minutes on any automation that boots the plugin before the user signs in, or indefinitely on keyless deployments) gets a tool response where every `opencode`-primary entry is marked `key_missing` in `providerHealth`, and the agent's downstream decisioning silently drops those entries from consideration. Same audit shape as M48–M60: a narrow predicate (report-the-primary-in-isolation) silently misbehaves under a new map invariant (key_missing post-M58), and the correct behavior is explicit "is this entry routable AT ALL" semantics at the agent-visible rendering boundary.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry(entry, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that returns the first visible route whose provider is healthy AND whose composite-route-key entry is not penalized, or `null` when every visible route is blocked (or when there are no visible routes at all). Semantically identical to the M57 `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` but scoped to a single entry so call sites with per-entry context don't have to wrap in a one-element array. Rewrote `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` to short-circuit to `null` whenever `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` returns non-null — the entry is routable, there is nothing to report. Only when EVERY visible route is blocked does the function fall through to the legacy "report the primary's blocking state" path, preserving the agent-visible "here's WHY this entry is unusable" signal for the case where the entry is genuinely dead. The M61 semantic change also applies to transient penalties on the primary: a primary with a live `quota` penalty and a healthy sibling used to report the quota state (in case the agent wanted to know about the degraded primary), and now returns null (the entry is routable through the sibling, there is nothing actionable). The rationale is the same: `list_curated_models` is used by the agent to answer "can I route to this?", not "which specific route is currently alive?", so the semantics should match what the router would actually do.
- **Tests**: eight new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_whenNoVisibleRoutes_returnsNull` — hidden-paid-only baseline.
  - `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_whenPrimaryHealthy_returnsPrimary` — happy-path baseline (array order honored).
  - `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_whenPrimaryBlockedButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling` — **core walk pin**: post-M58 shape with key_missing primary and healthy secondary.
  - `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_whenEveryVisibleRouteBlocked_returnsNull` — no-route-routable fallthrough pin.
  - `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_whenPrimaryProviderHealthyButRouteLevelBlocked_returnsSibling` — route-level-penalty skip pin (walks past a `model_not_found` route-level entry even though the provider is healthy), pinning the M29/M30 composite-key-read lesson at this helper.
  - `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryKeyMissingButSiblingHealthy_returnsNull` — **headline integration pin**: the exact post-M58 shipping-shape shape, expects null.
  - `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenEveryVisibleRouteKeyMissing_reportsProviderScope` — **sibling negative pin**: when every route IS genuinely blocked, the report must still surface the blocking state so the agent understands why. Prevents the M61 fix from regressing into "always return null when any key_missing is present on the primary".
  - `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryTransientQuotaButSiblingHealthy_returnsNull` — **transient-state semantic pin**: ensures the M61 fix isn't narrowed to only filter key_missing. A live `quota` penalty on the primary with a healthy sibling must also return null, because the agent's question is "can I route to this" not "which specific route is alive right now".
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` short-circuit inside `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` (leaving the helper, all 5 helper unit pins, and the import intact) and re-running `node --import tsx --test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Exactly **2 expected failures** fired: `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryKeyMissingButSiblingHealthy_returnsNull` and `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryTransientQuotaButSiblingHealthy_returnsNull` — both integration pins for the caller wiring. All 5 `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry_*` helper unit pins still passed against the reverted caller, exactly as expected: they test the helper's contract, not the caller's wiring. The `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenEveryVisibleRouteKeyMissing_reportsProviderScope` sibling negative pin also still passed against the reverted caller because pre-M61 behavior also returned the primary's state when every route was blocked — the test is a safeguard against over-filtering, not a bug-exposer. The M29/M30 legacy pins (`computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryVisibleRouteIsRouteUnhealthy_reportsRouteScope`, `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenPrimaryRouteIsHiddenPaid_walksToVisibleSibling`, `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport_whenLongcatEntryIsUnprefixed_detectsRouteLevelPenaltyFromCompositeKey`) all continued to pass — they use single-visible-route entries where the new short-circuit is a no-op. Restored the fix, 184/184 pass (176 pre-M61 + 8 new). `bun x tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` helper with full docstring, `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` rewritten with the short-circuit and a docstring explaining the post-M58 semantic history and the M29/M30/M61 lineage, added `ProviderRoute` to the imports from `../model-registry.js` for the helper's return type), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (8 new tests + added `findFirstHealthyRouteInEntry` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the tool-output fix. Production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: every agent calling `list_curated_models` between boot and the first successful opencode oauth handshake stops seeing `opencode`-primary entries marked `key_missing` and starts seeing them as healthy (because their iflowcn siblings are live and the router will actually use those). No change for entries whose every visible route is genuinely blocked — those still report their primary's blocking state, preserving the "here's WHY this is unusable" signal for the genuinely-dead case. Net: agents stop silently downgrading quality by avoiding routable models, and the `list_curated_models` tool output starts matching what the router would actually do.

### M60: `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` early-exit guard `providerHealthMap.size === 0 && modelRouteHealthMap.size === 0` became dead wiring post-M58 because `key_missing` entries permanently populate the provider map, so every agent turn on a freshly-booted plugin emitted an "Alternative models by role" section into the system prompt even when nothing was actually broken — the block's entire purpose is "here's what to try when something is broken" and `key_missing` is not something the agent can route around `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (pre-M60, ~line 1575) guarded its work with `if (providerHealthMap.size === 0 && modelRouteHealthMap.size === 0) return null;`. The intent was "skip the 'here are alternative models' block when there's nothing to be an alternative TO". That guard was correct pre-M58, when the only way a provider landed in `providerHealthMap` was through a live failure event. M58 (commit `9b125b5`) changed the invariant: `initializeProviderHealthState` now installs a `key_missing` entry with `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` for every uncredentialed curated provider at boot — typically 15–25 entries on a default install. `providerHealthMap.size === 0` is therefore effectively never true in production, the early exit is dead wiring, and every single agent turn falls through to a full registry walk and pushes a "## Available alternative models by role" section into the agent-visible system prompt. The parallel hook-level guard in `experimental.chat.system.transform` at line 3011 had exactly the same dead-wiring shape. Same class as the M59 bug at a different call site: post-M58 changed the semantic of "something is in the map" from "a transient failure is active" to "a transient failure OR permanent plumbing is present", and every old narrow-predicate guard that doesn't know the distinction silently starts firing on every turn.
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every agent turn post-M58. Wire-shape impact is the same shape as M59's: ~2–3k tokens of "Available alternative models by role" noise per turn on a freshly-booted plugin that has no real penalties to react to. Worse than M59's noise because the "alternatives" section invites the agent to actively consider alternate models when nothing is actually broken — actively misleading rather than merely wasteful. Same audit shape as M48–M59: a narrow predicate (`.size === 0`) silently misbehaves under a new map invariant, and the correct behavior is explicit agent-visible vs permanent-plumbing distinction at the rendering boundary.
- **Fix**: extracted a pure exported helper `hasAgentVisiblePenalty(providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that returns `true` iff at least one entry in either map satisfies BOTH `health.until > now` AND `isAgentVisibleHealthState(health.state)` (i.e. `state !== "key_missing"`). Replaced both guards: the `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` early-exit, and the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook-level early-exit at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:3011`. The helper composes with M59's `isAgentVisibleHealthState` so the "agent-visible" semantic lives in a single named place and the next audit doesn't have to rediscover what "not key_missing" means at every call site. Keeping the helper pure and exported means its contract is a property of the helper rather than a property-of-the-config the next author must preserve by hand.
- **Tests**: eight new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenBothMapsEmpty_returnsFalse` — empty-map baseline.
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenOnlyKeyMissingEntries_returnsFalse` — **post-M58 cold-start shape pin**: the exact shape (multiple key_missing entries with until=Infinity) that the factory installs at boot must be treated as "nothing worth surfacing".
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenTransientProviderPenaltyLive_returnsTrue` — asserts all five transient states (`quota`, `key_dead`, `no_credit`, `model_not_found`, `timeout`) return true individually, so any future additional transient state has to come through this test rather than being silently filtered out.
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenOnlyRouteLevelPenaltyLive_returnsTrue` — route-level penalties count too (the M27 lesson reapplied): a zero-token-quota signal lands in modelRouteHealthMap only, and the agent needs visibility.
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenAllTransientEntriesAreExpired_returnsFalse` — expired-entry-sweep pin: `until <= now` entries must not count, preventing stale "alternative models" sections between `expireHealthMaps` sweeps.
  - `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_whenKeyMissingAndLiveQuotaMixed_returnsTrue` — mixed-state pin: any single live transient penalty anywhere flips the guard to true.
  - `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt_whenOnlyKeyMissingPenaltiesExist_returnsNull` — **headline integration pin**: registry entry with a healthy route, provider map containing only key_missing entries. Pre-M60 the block fired and emitted an `architect: glm-5.1 (free)` line; post-M60 it returns `null` without running the registry walk at all.
  - `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt_whenQuotaAndKeyMissingMixed_returnsAlternatives` — **sibling positive pin**: mixed state with a live quota entry + key_missing entries. The block MUST fire — there's a real problem and the agent needs to know what else is routable while the quota backoff is in effect. Prevents the fix from regressing into "always return null when any key_missing is present".
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` early-exit to the pre-M60 shape (`size === 0 && size === 0`), leaving `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` + all six helper unit pins + the hook-level guard in place, and re-running `node --import tsx --test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Exactly **1 expected failure** fired: `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt_whenOnlyKeyMissingPenaltiesExist_returnsNull` — the headline integration pin. All six `hasAgentVisiblePenalty_*` helper unit pins still passed against the reverted caller, exactly as expected: they test the helper's contract, not the caller's wiring. The sibling positive pin (`buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt_whenQuotaAndKeyMissingMixed_returnsAlternatives`) also still passed against the reverted caller because pre-M60 code also fires when a quota entry exists in the provider map — the sibling is a negative-direction safeguard against over-filtering. Restored the fix, 176/176 pass (168 pre-M60 + 8 new). `bun x tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` helper with full docstring explaining the post-M58 dead-wiring shape and the relationship to M59's prompt-builder filter, early-exit in `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` replaced with a `hasAgentVisiblePenalty(...)` check plus a cross-referencing comment, early-exit in the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:3011` replaced with the same call), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (8 new tests + added `hasAgentVisiblePenalty` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the dead-guard fix. Production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: freshly-booted plugins with no real penalties stop pushing the "Alternative models by role" section into every turn's system prompt (~2–3k tokens saved per turn, same shape as M59's savings at a different call site), and the `experimental.chat.system.transform` hook stops invoking `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` + `buildAvailableModelsSystemPrompt` at all when every entry is permanent plumbing — pure CPU savings because the work was never load-bearing.

### M59: `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` emitted a per-provider "Curated fallbacks" section for every `key_missing` entry, so every agent turn post-M58 dumped 15–25 permanent-plumbing noise sections into the system prompt as if they were transient backoff penalties the agent could route around `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (pre-M59, ~line 1416) built `activeProviderPenalties` and `activeRoutePenalties` by filtering `providerHealthMap` / `modelRouteHealthMap` on `health.until > now` alone. The filter treated every non-expired health entry as a transient penalty worth surfacing to the agent. That was fine pre-M58, when the only way an entry landed in the maps was through a live failure (quota 429, key_dead 401, no_credit 402, model_not_found 404, timeout). M58 changed the invariant: `initializeProviderHealthState` now installs a `key_missing` entry with `until: Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` for every curated provider that has no credential at boot. `Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY > now` is always true, so every uncredentialed provider — typically 15–25 of them in a cold-start default install — got rendered into the system prompt as a "Provider X [KEY MISSING] until never / Curated fallbacks: …" section on every single agent turn. The semantic bug is worse than the noise: `key_missing` is permanent plumbing state the agent cannot act on (it can't route around a missing credential — only an operator can install one), yet the prompt framed it identically to a transient 1h quota backoff, inviting the agent to reason about fallbacks for a state that will never clear until a human intervenes.
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every agent turn post-M58. M58 shipped as commit `9b125b5` and started installing `key_missing` for every uncredentialed curated provider at boot. The default install on a fresh machine has most providers uncredentialed (operators typically configure 1–3: `opencode` via oauth, maybe `openrouter`, maybe `iflowcn`). That leaves 15–25 curated providers in `key_missing` permanently, and every single one of them fed a section into the system prompt on every `chat.params` hook. Measured wire-shape impact: the system-prompt overhead went from ~0 tokens (pre-M58 cold-start, empty health map) to ~2–3k tokens of permanent plumbing noise per turn (post-M58, before this fix). Same audit shape as M48–M58: the narrow predicate (`health.until > now`) fires silently in a real failure mode (permanent state conflated with transient state), and the correct behavior is explicit filtering of the non-actionable state at the agent-visible boundary.
- **Fix**: extracted a pure exported helper `isAgentVisibleHealthState(state)` that returns `false` for `"key_missing"` and `true` for every transient penalty state (`quota`, `key_dead`, `no_credit`, `model_not_found`, `timeout`). Applied the filter inside `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`'s two `.filter(...)` call sites alongside the existing `health.until > now` check. The internal `isProviderHealthy` path — used by the fallback scanners `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` (M57) and `findPreferredHealthyRoute` (M56) to skip dead providers during route resolution — still honors `key_missing` as a skip signal, because those scanners run inside the plugin and legitimately need to know "don't route here." Only the agent-visible rendering boundary is filtered. The helper is one-line, but it is exported so the semantic contract ("what health states should an agent see?") lives in a single named place instead of being an inline magic string comparison that the next audit has to rediscover.
- **Tests**: four new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `isAgentVisibleHealthState_whenStateIsKeyMissing_returnsFalse` — unit pin for the helper's core contract.
  - `isAgentVisibleHealthState_whenStateIsTransientPenalty_returnsTrue` — unit pin asserting all five transient states (`quota`, `key_dead`, `no_credit`, `model_not_found`, `timeout`) return true, so a future transient-state addition has to come back and update this test rather than quietly getting filtered out.
  - `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyKeyMissingPenaltiesExist_returnsNull` — end-to-end pin that a health map containing ONLY `key_missing` entries produces `null` (no prompt at all), matching the pre-M58 "nothing to surface" behavior.
  - `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenQuotaAndKeyMissingMixed_omitsKeyMissingFromSections` — **headline integration pin**: mixed-state health map with one `quota` entry (opencode) and one `key_missing` entry (kimi-for-coding), asserts the rendered prompt contains the `QUOTA BACKOFF` section for opencode but never mentions `kimi-for-coding` or the `KEY MISSING` string. This is the test that catches the bug through the real rendering pipeline.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the `isAgentVisibleHealthState` filter from `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt`'s two filter sites (leaving the helper, its unit pins, and the unit tests in place) and re-running `node --import tsx --test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`. Exactly **2 expected failures** fired: `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenOnlyKeyMissingPenaltiesExist_returnsNull` and `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt_whenQuotaAndKeyMissingMixed_omitsKeyMissingFromSections` — both integration pins. The two `isAgentVisibleHealthState_*` helper unit pins still passed against the reverted caller, exactly as expected: they test the helper's contract, not the caller's wiring. Restored the fix, 168/168 pass (164 pre-M59 + 4 new). `bun x tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `isAgentVisibleHealthState` helper with full docstring explaining the permanent-vs-transient semantic distinction and the post-M58 noise regression it prevents, filter applied at both `activeProviderPenalties` and `activeRoutePenalties` build sites in `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` with an inline comment cross-referencing the helper's docstring), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (4 new tests + added `isAgentVisibleHealthState` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the noise filter. The production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: the agent-visible system prompt drops ~2–3k tokens of permanent plumbing noise per turn, while the internal fallback scanners continue to honor `key_missing` as a skip signal during route resolution. Net: the agent stops reasoning about non-actionable state, and the plugin keeps routing around it.

### M58: `ModelRegistryPlugin` factory never called `initializeProviderHealthState` at startup — every auth.json + env-var credential check was dead code at runtime, and `key_missing` entries with `until: Infinity` crashed `new Date(until).toISOString()` at 7 render sites the moment any were installed `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `ModelRegistryPlugin` at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` line 2410 called `loadPersistedProviderHealth()` directly and never invoked `initializeProviderHealthState`. `initializeProviderHealthState` was defined and exported at line 2408 (`export { inferTaskComplexity, recommendTaskModelRoute, initializeProviderHealthState };`) — but ONLY for the test suite to import. The production factory never touched it. The downstream effect is that `loadAuthKeys()`, `providerHasEnvVarCredential()`, and the M33 stale-`key_missing` reconciliation loop — all of the M12/M13/M33/M55 auth.json/env-var detection machinery — never ran at runtime. On plugin startup with a fresh install or a freshly-cleared health file, the `providerHealthMap` came back completely empty. The fallback scanner (`findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` from M57, `findPreferredHealthyRoute` from M56) has no way to know a provider has no credentials, so it happily routed traffic through uncredentialed providers and burned retries on 401/403 responses before the runtime feedback path could mark them dead. All the tests that pinned `initializeProviderHealthState`'s correctness passed because they imported and called it DIRECTLY — not the factory. Nothing tested the factory's bootstrap sequence, so the wire-up rotted silently for months. Second-order bug exposed by the fix: seven render sites (`computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` × 2, `buildProviderHealthSystemPrompt` × 2, `get_quota_backoff_status` × 2, `recommend_model_for_role` × 1) all called `new Date(health.until).toISOString()` without guarding against `Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` — the sentinel `key_missing` uses for "no expiry." Pre-M58 those sites were unreachable for key_missing because the factory never installed any. Post-M58 they became the primary crash site the moment the wiring started working.
- **Reachability**: 100% reachable on every plugin cold-start. The failure mode is "fallback scanner routes around live penalty states but happily picks uncredentialed providers." Classic dead-wiring bug where the unit tests pass and the integration path is broken. Observed in practice after the openrouter-key-renewal incident (`openrouter` key dead, plugin never marked it `key_missing`, kept handing out `openrouter/*:free` routes that 401'd).
- **Fix**: Two coupled changes that must ship together.
  1. Extracted a new exported helper `initializeRuntimeProviderState(loadRegistry, logError)` that composes `loadRegistry()` with `initializeProviderHealthState(modelRegistry.models)`, falls back to `initializeProviderHealthState([])` + `logError(error)` when the registry load throws (so the plugin always boots). Rewired `ModelRegistryPlugin` to call `initializeRuntimeProviderState(() => loadModelRegistry(CONTROL_PLANE_ROOT_DIRECTORY))` instead of `loadPersistedProviderHealth()`. The helper takes the loader as a DI parameter so tests can supply a fixed registry or throwing loader without constructing a disk fixture.
  2. Extracted a new exported helper `formatHealthExpiry(until)` that returns `"never"` for `!Number.isFinite(until)` and `new Date(until).toISOString()` otherwise. Replaced all 7 sites that crashed on `Infinity`.
- **Tests**: four new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts`.
  - `initializeRuntimeProviderState_whenRegistryLoadsSuccessfully_installsKeyMissingForUncredentialedProviders` — happy path, direct helper, custom registry with an uncredentialed provider, asserts `key_missing`.
  - `initializeRuntimeProviderState_whenRegistryLoaderThrows_swallowsErrorAndReturnsEmptyMaps` — loader-throws path, asserts empty maps and exactly-one error logged.
  - `ModelRegistryPlugin_whenFactoryBoots_installsKeyMissingForUncredentialedCuratedProviders` — **headline wiring pin**: clears every `*_API_KEY`/`*_TOKEN` env var, writes an empty `auth.json`, invokes the real `ModelRegistryPlugin` factory, runs `get_quota_backoff_status.execute({})`, asserts at least one curated-registry provider came back in `key_missing` state AND every one of those entries rendered `until === "never"` (no ISO string, no Invalid Date). This is the test that catches BOTH coupled bugs — the wiring gap AND the Infinity-render crash — through the real production call path.
  - `formatHealthExpiry_whenUntilIsInfinite_returnsNeverSentinel` + `formatHealthExpiry_whenUntilIsFiniteMillis_returnsIsoString` — contract pins for the sentinel formatter.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting ONLY the factory wire-up (`loadPersistedProviderHealth()` instead of `initializeRuntimeProviderState(...)`), leaving the helper + `formatHealthExpiry` in place, re-running `bun test src/plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts`. Exactly **1 expected failure** fired: `ModelRegistryPlugin_whenFactoryBoots_installsKeyMissingForUncredentialedCuratedProviders` — the wiring pin. The two direct `initializeRuntimeProviderState_*` helper pins and the two `formatHealthExpiry_*` contract pins still passed against the reverted caller, exactly as expected: they test the helpers, not the factory. Restored the fix, full suite runs 573/573 pass (was 570 — added 3 net tests after net-accounting for 1 previously-existing pin that became the headline wiring pin). `bun x tsc --noEmit` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `initializeRuntimeProviderState` helper with full docstring explaining the dead-wiring bug it prevents, new exported `formatHealthExpiry` helper with docstring explaining the `key_missing` sentinel contract, `ModelRegistryPlugin` factory rewired, all 7 `new Date(health.until).toISOString()` call sites replaced with `formatHealthExpiry(health.until)`, added `ModelRegistry` type to imports), `src/plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts` (4 new tests).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the factory wire-up. The production impact is immediate on the first cold-start after rebuild: uncredentialed providers finally get flagged `key_missing` at boot, the fallback scanner skips them, and the next openrouter-key-renewal-shaped incident stops burning retries on dead credentials.

### M57: `recommendTaskModelRoute` last-resort fallback scanned only `roleMatchedEntries` (already narrowed by `allowedTiers` from `complexity`), so a request whose complexity tier was fully throttled threw "No healthy model route found" even when a sibling-tier entry with the same role was perfectly healthy — graceful degradation was impossible and the caller saw a hard failure when a working alternative was one tier removed `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `recommendTaskModelRoute` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (pre-M57, lines 2194-2205) implemented the last-resort fallback as an inline loop over `roleMatchedEntries` — the SAME list used by `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` above, already filtered through `enabled` + `role` + `allowedTiers[complexity]`. When every visible route inside that narrow tier set had a live penalty (provider `quota`/`key_dead`/`no_credit`/`key_missing`, or route-level `model_not_found`/`timeout`/`quota`), the loop completed without returning and control fell through to `throw new Error(`No healthy model route found for agent '${task.subagent_type}' with role '${role}' and complexity '${complexity}'`)`. The throw propagates out of the plugin hook and kills whatever called in — agent dispatch, routing-recommendation tool, or system-prompt injection — as a hard failure. A standard-tier architect entry sitting right there in `modelRegistryEntries` with a healthy `opencode/*-free` route was invisible to the fallback scan because `standard` wasn't in `allowedTiers` for a `large`-complexity request. No warning, no log line, no degradation path — just termination.
- **Reachability**: reachable today under any multi-provider outage. `allowedTiers` for `large` complexity is `["strong", "frontier"]`; for `small` it is `["tiny", "fast", "standard"]`; for `medium` it is `["standard", "strong"]`. A large-complexity request during a frontier+strong outage (all `ollama-cloud/*` routes timed out + `iflowcn` quota-throttled + `openrouter/*:free` all dead — the shape we've repeatedly seen during overlapping provider quota resets) has zero healthy entries in its tier set, and the scan throws even though `opencode/glm-4.7-free` (standard tier) is live and advertised for the `architect` role. The failure is the opposite of fail-safe: instead of "use a less-capable but working route," the caller sees "no model at all." Same audit shape as M48 / M52-M56: the narrow predicate fires silently in a real failure mode, the correct behavior is explicit graceful degradation.
- **Fix**: extracted a pure exported helper `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute(candidateEntries, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that returns the first `{provider, model}` whose provider AND composite route-health entry are both live, or `null` when none exist. Kept tier-agnostic by contract — the caller owns the candidate-set filter. `recommendTaskModelRoute` now runs the last-resort scan in two passes: first over `roleMatchedEntries` (preserves the existing within-tier preference — a large-complexity request continues to prefer strong/frontier routes whenever any are live), then over `rolePreferredEntries` (the `enabled + role` only set already computed for the M56 preferred-models lookup, no tier filter), with distinct reasoning strings so downstream telemetry can distinguish "within tier" from "outside tier" fallbacks. Only both passes returning `null` triggers the throw. The reasoning string `"Fallback to first healthy visible route outside complexity tier"` deliberately surfaces the degradation so operators see WHY a small-complexity prompt picked up a strong-tier route or a large-complexity prompt picked up a standard-tier route.
- **Tests**: six new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_whenCandidateListEmpty_returnsNull` — empty-list baseline.
  - `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_whenFirstEntryHasHealthyRoute_returnsFirstMatch` — primary happy path (array order honored).
  - `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_whenFirstEntryProviderUnhealthy_returnsNextHealthyEntry` — provider-health skip pin.
  - `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_whenRouteLevelPenaltyBlocksPrimaryButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling` — route-level-penalty skip pin (walks `provider_order` siblings inside one entry before moving to the next).
  - `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_whenEveryCandidateIsUnhealthy_returnsNull` — no-match fallthrough pin.
  - `recommendTaskModelRoute_whenComplexityTierFullyDownButSiblingTierHealthy_degradesToSiblingTier` — **headline integration pin**: end-to-end flow with a real temp-directory architect agent declaring `routing_complexity: large`, a registry where the frontier + strong entries have live penalties (ollama-cloud timeout route-health, iflowcn quota provider-health) and the standard-tier entry is fully healthy, and an expectation that the decision is `opencode/glm-4.7-free` with reasoning matching `/outside complexity tier/`. Pre-M57 this throws; post-M57 it degrades.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting the tier-agnostic second pass (deleting the `tierAgnosticRoute = findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute(rolePreferredEntries, ...)` block so only the tier-filtered first pass runs before throw) and re-running `npx tsx --test src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` — exactly **1 expected failure** fired: the headline integration pin. All five `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute_*` unit pins still passed against the reverted caller — exactly as expected, because the helper itself is correct; only the caller's choice of whether to make a second pass matters for the bug. Restored the fix, 164/164 pass.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` helper + docstring explaining the tier-agnostic contract, inline last-resort loop in `recommendTaskModelRoute` replaced with two-pass helper call that widens from `roleMatchedEntries` to `rolePreferredEntries`), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (6 new tests + added `findFirstHealthyVisibleRoute` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the graceful-degradation fallback before the next multi-provider outage forces a large-complexity request to throw where it could have served a standard-tier route instead.

### M56: `recommendTaskModelRoute` preferred-models lookup iterated `roleMatchedEntries` (already narrowed by the complexity-tier filter), so an agent declaring a frontier-tier `model:` preference on a prompt that `inferTaskComplexity` classified as `"small"` silently had its preference dropped and the task was routed to a tiny/fast tier the agent never asked for `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `recommendTaskModelRoute` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (pre-M56, lines 2044-2081) walked the agent's `preferredModels` list by iterating `roleMatchedEntries` — a list already filtered through BOTH the role filter AND the capability-tier filter from the inferred-or-explicit complexity. An agent that declared `model: minimax/MiniMax-M2.5` (a `frontier`-tier entry) with no explicit `routing_complexity:` in frontmatter, and received a prompt that `inferTaskComplexity` routed to `"small"` (e.g. "fix typo in README" — `typo` is a `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_KEYWORD_STEM`), saw its MiniMax-M2.5 entry excluded from `roleMatchedEntries` because `allowedTiers = ["tiny", "fast", "standard"]` did not contain `frontier`. The preferred-models loop found no match against the narrowed set, silently fell through to `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`, and routed the task to whatever tiny/fast/standard alternative happened to be healthy — a model the agent author never asked for. The failure was invisible: no warning, no log line, the reasoning string in the final decision even claimed "Best registry model for role X and complexity Y" as if the preference had never been declared.
- **Reachability**: reachable today. Any agent under `.opencode/agents/` that (a) declares `model:` or `models:` pointing at a tier above `standard` and (b) omits `routing_complexity:`, is one matching keyword away from silently losing its preference. The M50 SMALL complexity branch widens the hit surface — it added `typo`, `rename`, `trivial`, `minor`, `whitespace` as stems, so prompts containing any of those words (a very common shape for maintenance tasks delegated to a specialist agent) now trigger the bug where they used to default to `medium`. The specific victims are the agents in the model catalog that legitimately want a frontier model for EVERY task they handle — e.g. a security_reviewer or critical_reviewer agent that declares a strong/frontier preference precisely so it doesn't miss anything. Same audit shape as M48, M52, M53, M54, M55: the narrow predicate's failure mode is silent and the correct behavior is explicit author intent over inferred heuristic.
- **Fix**: extracted a pure exported helper `findPreferredHealthyRoute(preferredModels, candidateEntries, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that encapsulates the full preferred-models → healthy-route resolution (exact preferred route → same-family sibling fallback → null). The helper's contract deliberately does NOT mention capability tier: the caller is responsible for building a candidate set that honors any filters it wants honored. `recommendTaskModelRoute` now builds a separate `rolePreferredEntries` list filtered by `enabled` + `role` ONLY (no tier filter) and passes that to the helper. The existing `roleMatchedEntries` list (enabled + role + tier) is still used for the downstream `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` path — so inference-time complexity routing still works as designed for the non-preferred case. Only the explicit-preference path loses the tier gate, matching the principle that explicit author intent outranks inferred heuristic.
- **Tests**: seven new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenPreferredModelsEmpty_returnsNull` — empty-list baseline.
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenExactPreferredRouteIsHealthy_returnsExactRoute` — primary happy path.
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenExactPreferredRouteIsUnhealthyButSiblingHealthy_returnsSibling` — same-family sibling fallback pin (the existing behavior preserved through the extraction).
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenNoPreferredRouteMatchesAnyEntry_returnsNull` — no-match fallthrough pin.
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenAuthorOrderHasMultiplePreferences_honorsFirstHealthy` — **ordering pin**: the helper honors author order across multiple preferred models.
  - `findPreferredHealthyRoute_whenCallerPassesOnlyTierFilteredEntriesAndPreferredTierExcluded_returnsNull` — **contract pin**: the helper itself is tier-agnostic; it just searches the candidate set it is given. Prevents a future refactor from quietly re-tightening the candidate set INSIDE the helper and re-introducing the bug at one level down.
  - `recommendTaskModelRoute_whenAgentModelPreferenceIsFrontierTierButPromptInfersSmallComplexity_honorsPreference` — **headline integration pin**: end-to-end flow through `recommendTaskModelRoute` with a real temp-directory fixture, an agent declaring `model: minimax/MiniMax-M2.5`, and a prompt ("fix typo in README") that deterministically routes through `inferTaskComplexity → "small"`. Asserts the decision is MiniMax-M2.5 and the reasoning is the preferred-from-metadata string.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting the `rolePreferredEntries` argument back to `roleMatchedEntries` (the pre-M56 shape) and re-running `npm test` — exactly **1 expected failure** fired: the headline `recommendTaskModelRoute_*_honorsPreference` integration pin. All six `findPreferredHealthyRoute_*` unit pins still passed against the reverted call site — exactly as expected, because the helper itself is correct; only the CALLER'S choice of candidate set matters for the bug. The unit pins test the helper's contract; the integration pin tests the wiring. Restored the fix, 281/281 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported `findPreferredHealthyRoute` helper + docstring explaining the tier-filter contract, inline preferred-models loop in `recommendTaskModelRoute` collapsed into a `rolePreferredEntries` + helper call), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (7 tests + added `findPreferredHealthyRoute` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the preference-outranks-inference fix before any maintenance-task prompt gets silently downgraded under an agent that declared a strong/frontier preference.

### M55: `hasUsableCredential` oauth branch inspected only `record.access` and ignored `record.refresh`, so an expired-access / valid-refresh auth.json entry silently flagged its provider as `key_missing` at plugin init and cascaded a 2h health penalty that suppressed routing — a plugin-level outage opencode itself would have transparently resolved on the first request `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `hasUsableCredential` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (pre-M55, line 1856) tested oauth entries with `return typeof record.access === "string" && record.access.length > 0;` — a predicate that ignores the `refresh` field entirely. Opencode's oauth schema is `{ type: "oauth", access: "...", refresh: "..." }`, and when an access token expires or is explicitly cleared by opencode's own refresh flow, the on-disk entry transiently lands as `{ type: "oauth", access: "", refresh: "<valid>" }`. Opencode handles this state transparently: the next provider request sees the empty access token, mints a new one via the refresh token, and succeeds. The PROVIDER IS USABLE in that state. The pre-M55 plugin predicate, however, sees `access === ""` and returns `false`, causing `initializeProviderHealthState` to install a `key_missing` entry on `providerHealthMap` (duration `PROVIDER_KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS` = 2h). That penalty cascades into every routing decision: `countHealthyVisibleRoutes`, `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`, and the fallback scans all treat the provider as dead, suppressing it from every route suggestion for two hours. Opencode keeps serving requests under the provider transparently; the plugin's health map disagrees and routes every agent AWAY from it.
- **Reachability**: latent-but-plausible. The failure shape is fully determined by the on-disk auth.json state at the moment the plugin initializes: if opencode has cleared `access` but not yet written a new one when `initializeProviderHealthState` runs (plugin start, service restart, or any code path that reloads auth.json), the plugin's view of the provider diverges from opencode's for two hours. This happens most visibly at service restart shortly after an access-token expiry — the operator starts the service, the plugin reads the in-flux auth.json, installs a `key_missing` penalty, and routes around a perfectly-usable provider until the penalty expires or an explicit operator intervention clears the map. Same audit shape as M48, M52, M53, M54: defend the narrow predicate before the real event fires it in production.
- **Fix**: opencode's oauth semantics make `refresh` an independent usability signal — the PROVIDER is callable iff EITHER token is present. The helper now reads both fields defensively and returns `accessToken.length > 0 || refreshToken.length > 0`. The `typeof ... === "string" ? ... : ""` coalesce on each field keeps the helper robust against shapes where one field is absent or non-string. Exported `hasUsableCredential` so the predicate can be unit-tested without constructing a plugin or writing a temp auth.json.
- **Tests**: ten new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenApiKeyEntryIsNonEmpty_returnsTrue` / `_whenApiKeyEntryIsEmpty_returnsFalse` — api-path baseline pins.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenOauthEntryHasAccessTokenOnly_returnsTrue` — oauth baseline: access present, refresh empty.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenOauthEntryHasEmptyAccessButValidRefresh_returnsTrue` — **headline regression pin**: `{type:"oauth", access:"", refresh:"rt-valid"}` must return `true` so the plugin's view matches opencode's transparent-refresh behavior.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenOauthEntryHasBothTokensEmpty_returnsFalse` — **contract pin**: a genuinely empty oauth entry still flags as unusable; the refresh allowance only kicks in when refresh is itself a non-empty string.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenOauthEntryHasRefreshFieldMissing_fallsBackToAccessCheck` — **defensive pin**: a `{type:"oauth"}` entry with `refresh` entirely absent must not throw; the `typeof`-coalesce guard keeps the check equivalent to the access-only path for that shape.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenEntryIsNonEmptyString_returnsTrue` / `_whenEntryIsEmptyString_returnsFalse` — legacy bare-string fixture pins.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenEntryIsNullOrUndefined_returnsFalse` — null/undefined safety pin.
  - `hasUsableCredential_whenLegacyApiKeyShape_returnsTrue` — legacy `{ apiKey: "..." }` back-compat pin.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting the oauth branch to the pre-M55 access-only shape (`return typeof record.access === "string" && record.access.length > 0;`) and re-running `npm test` — exactly **1 expected failure** fired: `hasUsableCredential_whenOauthEntryHasEmptyAccessButValidRefresh_returnsTrue`. All nine other pins still passed against the reverted helper — exactly as expected for pins that don't exercise the refresh-token code path. Restored the fix, 274/274 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (exported `hasUsableCredential`, rewrote oauth branch + expanded docstring explaining opencode refresh semantics), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (10 tests + added `hasUsableCredential` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the refresh-token allowance before any service restart catches a transient `access: ""` window in auth.json.

### M54: `chat.params` hang-timer read `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS` through bare `parseInt(raw ?? "900000", 10)`, so a typo, empty value, trailing-garbage, or negative value would silently mis-arm the timer and fire spurious `"timeout"` penalties on every session `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `chat.params` hook in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (~line 2543 pre-fix) parsed its hang-timer budget with `const timeoutMs = parseInt(process.env.AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS ?? "900000", 10);` and then used `timeoutMs < 1000` to branch between an immediate-penalty "test mode" and a production `setTimeout(fn, timeoutMs + 100)` path. Three latent misbehaviors lived in that one line:
  1. **NaN fall-through.** `parseInt("abc", 10) === NaN`. Every comparison against `NaN` is `false` in JavaScript, so `NaN < 1000` is `false` and the code took the production branch. `setTimeout(fn, NaN + 100)` coerces the delay to `1` ms, the timer fires almost immediately, `finalizeHungSessionState` records a spurious `"timeout"` penalty on whatever provider/model the session is using, and every subsequent session repeats the penalty — a typo in one env var silently blacks out every route in the registry until an operator notices. The failure is silent on the stdout/stderr side: `parseInt` does not throw, the handler wraps everything in `try { ... } catch { return; }` anyway, and the timeout penalty is indistinguishable from a real hung session in the health log.
  2. **Trailing garbage accepted.** `parseInt("900000abc", 10) === 900000`. A malformed env var like `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS=45000ms` (the operator adds a unit suffix) would be silently interpreted as `45000` with no warning — the wrong value honored as-if the trailing characters were not there. Small numeric typos with trailing non-digits have the same shape.
  3. **Negative values accepted.** `parseInt("-1", 10) === -1` which IS `< 1000`, so the test-mode branch fires and every session gets an immediate-penalty record. Negative budgets are never a legitimate test-mode request; they are misconfiguration.
- **Reachability**: latent-but-plausible. No env var is currently set to any of the broken shapes, but the risk surface is operator-supplied configuration flowing through a handler that runs on every `chat.params` invocation — a typo in `.envrc`, a copy-paste from documentation that includes a unit suffix, an empty export left after removing the override — any of these would immediately start firing spurious timeout penalties on every session with no warning. Same audit shape as M48 (model_not_found status-code priority), M52 (zero-token reasoning channel), M53 (quoted YAML scalar): defend the narrow predicate before the real event fires it in production.
- **Fix**: added `DEFAULT_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS = 900000` module constant and extracted a pure exported helper `parseHangTimeoutMs(rawValue: string | undefined): number` that validates the raw env string: `undefined` or empty → default; non-finite `Number(rawValue)` (catches NaN from `"abc"` and `"450000abc"`) → default; negative → default; otherwise `Math.trunc(parsedValue)`. `Number()` is deliberately stricter than `parseInt()` — it rejects trailing garbage outright — so the helper surfaces operator typos as a safe-default fallback rather than silently accepting a partially-parsed value. The test-mode short-path (`timeoutMs < 1000`) is preserved: a genuine test caller can still pass `"0"` or `"500"` and have them honored. The `chat.params` call site collapses to `const timeoutMs = parseHangTimeoutMs(process.env.AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS);`.
- **Tests**: eight new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenUndefined_returnsDefault` — baseline: unset env var lands on the 15-minute default.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenEmptyString_returnsDefault` — **defensive pin**: `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS=` (exported empty) must be treated as unset, not as `Number("") === 0` which would flip the call site into the immediate-penalty test branch on every session.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenValidIntegerString_returnsValue` — integration baseline that valid integer strings still parse.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenZeroString_returnsZeroForTestShortPath` — **contract pin**: legitimate test callers passing `"0"` still get `0` back so the `< 1000` test-mode branch fires as intended.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenNonNumericString_returnsDefault` — **headline regression pin**: `parseInt("abc", 10) === NaN` → `NaN < 1000` false → production branch with `setTimeout(fn, NaN + 100)` → Node coerces to ~1ms → spurious timeout penalty on every session. The helper now rejects NaN and returns default.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenTrailingGarbageAppendedToValidInteger_returnsDefault` — trailing-garbage pin using `"450000abc"` (deliberately NOT matching the default so the pin discriminates). `parseInt` silently returned `450000`; `Number("450000abc")` returns `NaN` which the helper rejects and falls back to the default.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenNegativeString_returnsDefault` — negative-value pin: `parseInt("-1", 10) === -1` used to satisfy `< 1000` and fire the test-mode branch on every session. The helper now rejects negatives.
  - `parseHangTimeoutMs_whenFloatString_truncatesToInteger` — float-truncation contract: `"123456.789"` → `123456`.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the helper body with the bare identity `return parseInt(rawValue ?? "900000", 10);` (the pre-M54 shape) and re-running `npm test` — exactly **4 expected failures** fired: `_whenEmptyString_returnsDefault` (`parseInt("", 10) === NaN`), `_whenNonNumericString_returnsDefault` (`parseInt("abc", 10) === NaN`), `_whenTrailingGarbageAppendedToValidInteger_returnsDefault` (`parseInt("450000abc", 10) === 450000`), `_whenNegativeString_returnsDefault` (`parseInt("-1", 10) === -1`). The undefined baseline, valid-integer pin, zero-string test-mode pin, and float-truncation pin all still passed against the reverted helper — exactly as expected for pins that don't exercise any of the four broken shapes. Restored the fix, 264/264 green.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `DEFAULT_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS` constant, new `parseHangTimeoutMs` helper + docstring listing the three `parseInt` misbehaviors, `chat.params` hook call site collapsed from inline parse to one helper call), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (8 tests + added `parseHangTimeoutMs` and `DEFAULT_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the hang-timer parse fix before any operator sets a broken env var.

### M53: `readAgentMetadata` frontmatter parser kept literal YAML quote characters on scalar fields (`model:`, `routing_role:`, `routing_complexity:`) so any agent authoring its preference as a quoted YAML scalar would have the preference silently dropped by `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s strict-equal preferred-model lookup `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `readAgentMetadata` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts`, pre-fix) parsed each frontmatter line with `line.slice(colonIndex + 1).trim()` and assigned the trimmed string directly to `metadata.model` / `metadata.routing_role` / `metadata.routing_complexity`. For an agent declaring `model: "openrouter/stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"` (a perfectly valid YAML scalar, and arguably the idiomatic form when the model id contains a `:free` suffix), the assigned value was `'"openrouter/stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"'` — literal quote chars baked into the string. The preferred-models lookup in `recommendTaskModelRoute` (line 1898 pre-fix) then does `visibleRoutes.some((route) => route.model === preferredModel)` — a strict-equal comparison against the unquoted registry route string — which silently fails every match and falls through to `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`, dropping the explicit agent preference without any warning. The inline models-block parser (`metadata.models`) ALREADY stripped quotes via `.replace(/^["']|["']$/g, "")`, so the scalar path was the only vulnerable site — and the inconsistency itself was a smell pointing at exactly this bug class.
- **Reachability**: latent-but-plausible. No agent under `/home/mhugo/code/aicoder-opencode/.opencode/agents/` or `targets/*/overlay/.opencode/agents/` currently quotes its model scalar — a grep confirms every `^model:` line is unquoted. But the cost of adopting the idiomatic quoted form for any future agent is a silent preference drop: the agent author gets no error, the log is clean, the session runs on whatever `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` happens to return for the task's role/complexity filter. The failure shape is guaranteed to bite the first time anyone reaches for quoted YAML — either deliberately (colon-containing id, leading-digit value, copy-paste from a JSON-style reference) or accidentally (IDE autoquoting). Same audit shape as M48 (model_not_found status-code priority) and M52 (zero-token reasoning channel): fix the narrow predicate before the real event fires it in production.
- **Fix**: extracted a pure exported helper `stripYamlScalarQuotes(rawValue: string): string` that removes exactly one layer of matching leading/trailing quote characters — the matched-pair rule is deliberately stricter than the old models-block helper (which accepted mismatched quote chars at either end), so asymmetric inputs like `"foo` or `foo'` are preserved verbatim rather than silently corrupted. Then extracted the whole frontmatter parse loop out of `readAgentMetadata` into a pure exported helper `parseAgentFrontmatter(frontmatterText: string): AgentMetadata` that routes all three scalar fields AND both models-list paths (block-list + inline flow-style) through `stripYamlScalarQuotes`. Routing every value site through ONE helper removes the pre-existing inconsistency where block-list items were stripped but scalar fields and flow-style inline items were not. `readAgentMetadata` shrinks to a thin filesystem-adapter around `parseAgentFrontmatter` — the filesystem fixture becomes a separate concern from the parsing contract, so the parser can be unit-tested without any temp-file setup.
- **Tests**: eleven new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `stripYamlScalarQuotes_whenUnquoted_returnsValueUnchanged` — idempotence baseline.
  - `stripYamlScalarQuotes_whenDoubleQuoted_stripsOneLayer` — primary double-quote pin.
  - `stripYamlScalarQuotes_whenSingleQuoted_stripsOneLayer` — primary single-quote pin (YAML permits both).
  - `stripYamlScalarQuotes_whenAsymmetricQuotes_leavesValueAlone` — **defensive pin** for the matched-pair rule: `"foo`, `foo'`, `"foo'` all pass through unchanged so accidental upstream copy-paste errors surface as visible mismatches rather than silent corruption.
  - `stripYamlScalarQuotes_whenEmptyOrTooShort_returnsValueUnchanged` — boundary pin: empty string and lone quote char both pass through.
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenUnquotedModel_returnsRawValue` — integration baseline that the parser still returns unquoted values untouched (the common case today).
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenModelScalarIsDoubleQuoted_stripsQuotes` — **headline regression pin**: `model: "openrouter/stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"` must yield `metadata.model === "openrouter/stepfun/step-3.5-flash:free"` so the strict-equal preferred-model lookup in `recommendTaskModelRoute` matches.
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenRoutingRoleIsSingleQuoted_stripsQuotes` — covers the `routing_role:` scalar path with the single-quote variant.
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenRoutingComplexityIsQuoted_acceptsStrippedValue` — **ordering pin**: the enum-membership check (`["small", "medium", "large"].includes`) runs AFTER quote stripping, so `'small'` → `small` → accepted. If stripping happened after the check (or not at all), quoted complexity would be silently rejected.
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenModelsBlockListHasQuotedItems_stripsQuotesPerItem` — block-list regression pin (the one path that already worked pre-M53, now routed through the new helper to prove the refactor preserved it).
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenModelsInlineFlowStyleIsQuoted_stripsQuotesPerItem` — **new contract pin**: the old inline flow-style branch did NOT strip quotes from items (only the block-list branch did), so `models: ["a", 'b']` yielded `['"a"', "'b'"]` pre-M53. The refactor routes flow-style items through `stripYamlScalarQuotes` and pins the stronger contract.
  - `parseAgentFrontmatter_whenRoutingComplexityIsInvalid_leavesFieldUnset` — pre-existing contract preserved: unknown complexity values (`enormous`) are silently rejected so the caller falls back to `inferTaskComplexity`.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing `stripYamlScalarQuotes` with the identity function `return rawValue;` and re-running `npm test` — exactly **7 expected failures** fired: both primary quote-stripping pins, and all five `parseAgentFrontmatter_*Quoted*` pins (model, routing_role, routing_complexity, block-list, flow-style). The unquoted baseline, asymmetric-quotes defensive pin, empty/too-short boundary pin, and invalid-complexity pin all still passed against the reverted helper — exactly as expected for pins that don't exercise the quote-stripping code path. Restored the fix, 256/256 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `stripYamlScalarQuotes` helper + docstring, new `parseAgentFrontmatter` helper + docstring, `readAgentMetadata` shrunk to thin filesystem adapter around the pure parser), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (11 tests + added `parseAgentFrontmatter` and `stripYamlScalarQuotes` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the parser fix before any agent under those targets adopts the quoted YAML scalar form.

### M52: `assistant.message.completed` zero-token quota handler used the narrow predicate `tokens.input === 0 && tokens.output === 0`, which would silently misclassify successful deep-reasoning turns as quota-exhausted the moment opencode started populating side-channel counters (`reasoning`, nested `cache.read`/`cache.write`) `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `assistant.message.completed` handler in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (~line 2428 pre-fix) tested `if (tokens.input === 0 && tokens.output === 0)` and on match penalized the active route with a 1h `"quota"` backoff. That predicate only inspects the two primary billing axes and ignores every other token counter opencode may expose — `reasoning` (for deep-thinking models that do their work in the reasoning channel), nested `cache: {read, write}` (prompt-cache accounting), and any future counter upstream providers surface. A genuine quota-exhausted turn produces nothing on any axis; a successful deep-reasoning turn on `kimi-k2-thinking` / `minimax-m2.7` / `cogito-2.1` — the exact three models the handler docstring already cites as routinely running 200+ sequential tool calls — can plausibly report `{input: 0, output: 0, reasoning: N>0}`. The narrow predicate would see `input=0, output=0`, ignore `reasoning`, and penalize a SUCCESSFUL completion as quota-exhausted. The route would flip to 1h backoff, its retryCount would tick, and the next session would bypass a healthy premier deep-reasoning model.
- **Reachability**: latent-but-plausible. The specific failure shape depends on whether the current opencode runtime populates `reasoning` / nested `cache` fields on `assistant.message.completed` — which varies by provider and by opencode release. Even if no current release exposes these fields at this event, a future release that does would silently start corrupting health state the moment it lands. The defensive predicate insulates against that regression without waiting for the incident. This is the same audit shape as M48 (model_not_found status-code priority): fix the narrow predicate before a real event fires it in production.
- **Fix**: extracted a new pure exported helper `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal(tokens: Record<string, unknown>): boolean` placed right after `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth`. The helper (a) short-circuits `false` if either `tokens.input` or `tokens.output` is nonzero, (b) walks every top-level value — returning `false` on any nonzero numeric and recursing one level into nested objects to catch `cache.read`/`cache.write` shapes, and (c) ignores non-numeric non-object fields (string tags, booleans) so future metadata additions don't accidentally block the signal. Full docstring explains the failure shape and the latent-vs-reachable reasoning. Rewired the handler to call `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal(tokens as Record<string, unknown>)` instead of the inline narrow check, leaving the surrounding logic (route-key composition, `buildRouteHealthEntry`, persistence) unchanged. The helper is pure so it is unit-testable without any live health maps or opencode runtime event payloads.
- **Tests**: nine new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenBothPrimaryCountersAreZeroAndNoOtherCounters_returnsTrue` — baseline accept pin (genuine silent-failure turn).
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenInputIsNonZero_returnsFalse` / `_whenOutputIsNonZero_returnsFalse` — primary-axis negative pins.
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenReasoningCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse` — **headline regression pin**: `{input: 0, output: 0, reasoning: 12000}` must NOT fire the quota signal. This is the exact failure shape a successful kimi-k2-thinking / minimax-m2.7 / cogito-2.1 turn could produce.
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenNestedCacheReadCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse` / `_whenNestedCacheWriteCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse` — nested-shape regression pins for `cache: {read, write}` payloads.
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenNestedObjectIsEmpty_returnsTrue` — defensive pin that an empty nested object doesn't block the zero signal (only genuine nonzero numerics should).
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenNonNumericStringFieldPresent_returnsTrue` — defensive pin that non-numeric non-object metadata (e.g., a string model-id tag) is ignored.
  - `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal_whenTopLevelSiblingCounterIsNonZero_returnsFalse` — future-proofing pin: any top-level numeric sibling counter blocks the signal.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by replacing the helper body with the old narrow `return tokens.input === 0 && tokens.output === 0;` predicate and re-running `npm test` — exactly **4 expected failures** fired: the headline `reasoning` pin, both `cache.read` and `cache.write` nested pins, and the `total` top-level sibling pin. The `whenNestedObjectIsEmpty_returnsTrue` and `whenNonNumericStringFieldPresent_returnsTrue` pins deliberately still passed against the reverted predicate (they only assert the accept path, which the narrow predicate also accepts — the negatives are what the narrow predicate gets wrong). Restored the fix, 244/244 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` helper + docstring, rewired handler at ~line 2428 with explanatory comment block), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (9 tests + added `isZeroTokenQuotaSignal` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the defensive predicate before any future opencode release starts populating `reasoning` or nested `cache` counters at `assistant.message.completed`.

### M51: `isFallbackBlocked` used bare `.includes("gpt")` / `.includes("grok")` substring matches to exclude proprietary models from the fallback cascade — `"gpt-oss:120b"` and `"gpt-oss:20b"` (legitimate free open-weights models explicitly recommended in the catalog for A/B cross-checks) were silently blocked alongside the proprietary OpenAI family `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `isFallbackBlocked` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:415` pre-fix) tested a bare substring list `["longcat", "claude", "gpt", "grok"]` against `modelID.toLowerCase()`. The `"gpt"` entry over-matched every model id that contained the three-character string, including `"ollama-cloud/gpt-oss:120b"` and `"ollama-cloud/gpt-oss:20b"` — legitimate free open-weights models hosted on ollama-cloud and explicitly listed in the user's model catalog as A/B cross-check targets alongside `deepseek-v3.2` and `nemotron-3-super`. The substring check silently removed an entire lineage from the fallback cascade: whenever the router needed a non-proprietary secondary opinion, gpt-oss was invisible, collapsing A/B diversity to whatever other ollama-cloud models were healthy.
- **Reachability**: fully reachable whenever gpt-oss models are enabled in `models.jsonc`. Currently gpt-oss is listed in the catalog as available but has not yet been wired into the curated registry as a primary route — the latent-ness is only about exposure (the registry hasn't enabled it yet), not about the bug semantics (the filter is broken either way). The same bug shape would regress again the moment any future `gpt-*` open-weights model (gpt-j, gpt-neo, gpt-oss successors) appeared in `models.jsonc`. The `"grok"` entry has the same word-boundary gap but is currently unreachable because no `grok-oss`-style open-weights release exists — it was added as a defensive pin alongside the gpt fix so a future release is covered pre-emptively.
- **Fix**: replaced `FALLBACK_BLOCKED_MODEL_SUBSTRINGS` (bare substring list) with `FALLBACK_BLOCKED_MODEL_PATTERNS` (ordered list of `RegExp` patterns). The distinguishing property of proprietary OpenAI/xAI families is the numbered version suffix (`gpt-4`, `gpt-5.3-codex-spark`, `grok-4-fast`, `grok-4-heavy`), while open-weights releases use word suffixes (`gpt-oss`, hypothetical `grok-oss`). Requiring a digit after the optional hyphen in the pattern (`/\bgpt-?\d/i`, `/\bgrok-?\d/i`) keeps the proprietary family blocked and the open-weights family reachable. Added a separate `/\bchatgpt/i` pattern to cover the `chatgpt-4o` / `chatgpt-*` naming. `claude` and `longcat` are single-brand names with no ambiguity so they stay as plain anchored case-insensitive matches. Exported the `isFallbackBlocked` helper so the regex semantics can be unit-tested directly without constructing the plugin closure.
- **Tests**: nine new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsGptOssOpenWeights_returnsFalse` — **headline regression pin**: pins both `gpt-oss:120b` and `gpt-oss:20b` as NOT blocked, so a future refactor that widens the gpt pattern fires this test first.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsProprietaryOpenAIWithDigit_returnsTrue` — negative pin for the proprietary OpenAI family (`gpt-4`, `gpt-5.3-codex-spark`, `gpt-5.4`), proving the regex still covers every numbered version the catalog references.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsChatgptVariant_returnsTrue` — separate `chatgpt-*` pin covering the non-numbered naming style (`chatgpt-4o-latest`).
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsClaude_returnsTrue` — single-brand pin for `claude-opus-4-6`.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsProprietaryGrok_returnsTrue` — numbered-version pin for `grok-4-fast` / `grok-4-heavy`.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelContainsGrokAsInnerWordWithoutDigit_returnsFalse` — **defensive pin** for a hypothetical future `grok-oss` release. Not a currently-reachable model, but the pin locks the word-boundary invariant so a future refactor loosening the regex fires the test first.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenProviderIsLongcat_returnsTrueRegardlessOfModel` — provider-id blocklist precedence pin (`longcat` and `longcat-openai` provider ids remain blocked even if the model id is mundane).
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelContainsLongcatViaAggregator_returnsTrue` — aggregator path pin: `openrouter/meituan/longcat-flash-chat` is excluded via the pattern-list even though the `openrouter` provider id is permitted.
  - `isFallbackBlocked_whenModelIsUnrelated_returnsFalse` — sanity guard for ordinary curated models (`glm-5`, `kimi-k2-thinking`, `qwen3-coder:480b`) against over-eager pattern refactors.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting `isFallbackBlocked` to the old bare-substring `["longcat", "claude", "gpt", "grok"].some(includes)` and re-running `npm test` — exactly **2 expected failures**: the headline `gpt-oss` regression pin and the defensive `grok-oss` word-boundary pin. Restored the fix, 235/235 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
