- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (replaced `FALLBACK_BLOCKED_MODEL_SUBSTRINGS` with `FALLBACK_BLOCKED_MODEL_PATTERNS` regex list + explanatory comment block, exported `isFallbackBlocked`, added helper docstring), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (9 tests + added `isFallbackBlocked` to imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims start exposing gpt-oss to the fallback cascade when it lands in `models.jsonc`.

### M50: `inferTaskComplexity` never returned `"small"` — the `TaskComplexity` type and the `tierMap` both declared a `"small"` row (mapping to `["tiny", "fast", "standard"]`) but the inference path could not reach it, so every trivial inferred prompt got routed to medium (standard+strong) and the tiny+fast tier rows in `models.jsonc` were dead capacity `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `inferTaskComplexity` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:1390` pre-fix) tested `LARGE_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` then `MEDIUM_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` and defaulted to `"medium"` — there was no `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` path. The `TaskComplexity` type (`"small" | "medium" | "large"`), the `routing_complexity` frontmatter parser (line 1474 accepts all three), and the downstream `tierMap` (line 1696, `small: ["tiny", "fast", "standard"]`) all declared the `small` row, but the inference-path callers of `recommendTaskModelRoute` — which is the path used whenever neither `task.complexity` nor `agent.routing_complexity` is set — could not produce `"small"` from any prompt. The `small` row was therefore dead code reachable ONLY via explicit overrides, and every inferred trivial prompt ("fix typo in README", "rename foo to bar", "strip trailing whitespace") silently landed in the medium tier's `standard+strong` candidate set.
- **Reachability**: always reachable. Every session that goes through `recommendTaskModelRoute` without a complexity override runs `inferTaskComplexity`, and the autopilot + non-tagged interactive sessions routinely invoke it on prompts that should legitimately be tiny/fast work. The capacity waste compounds: tiny/fast tier models sit idle (they have no inferred-complexity way to be selected) while the standard/strong pool absorbs trivial prompts that did not need its capability budget. The dead-row shape has been latent since `small` was added to `TaskComplexity` — the inference function was grown against MEDIUM/LARGE first and the SMALL branch was never written.
- **Fix**: added `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_KEYWORD_STEMS` (deliberately narrow: `"typo"`, `"rename"`, `"trivial"`, `"minor"`, `"whitespace"` — concrete mechanical operations, not vague adjectives like `simple`/`quick`/`easy` which routinely appear in medium-work prompts like `"simple implementation of the payments flow"`). Built a `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_REGEX` using the existing `buildLeadingBoundaryRegex` helper so the leading-word-boundary invariant is shared with the other tiers (inflections like `"renames"` / `"renaming"` still match; inner-substring false positives like `"fully"` matching `"full"` are still excluded). Inserted the SMALL check between LARGE and MEDIUM in the cascade — LARGE wins first (scope dominance: `"refactor and rename across modules"` stays large), then SMALL wins over MEDIUM on ambiguous matches (`"fix typo"` matches both `fix` and `typo`, small is the right call because the mechanical op dominates).
- **Tests**: nine new / updated tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsTypo_classifiesAsSmall` — headline dead-row regression pin.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsRename_classifiesAsSmall` — mechanical rename signal.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsRenamesInflection_stillClassifiesAsSmall` — leading-boundary inflection pin (`renames` / `renaming` / `renamed`), mirrors the existing `refactoring` inflection pin.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsTrivial_classifiesAsSmall` — explicit operator signal.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsWhitespace_classifiesAsSmall` — formatting-only edits. Deliberately avoids LARGE stems like `across` in the prompt so the SMALL path is the only match.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsMinor_classifiesAsSmall` — `"minor version bump"` author signal.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsBothTypoAndFix_prefersSmallOverMedium` — **tie-break pin**: `"fix typo"` matches BOTH medium (`fix`) and small (`typo`); small must win so trivial mechanical ops don't keep burning standard+strong capacity. Fires if a future refactor reorders the cascade.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptMentionsRefactorAndRename_prefersLargeOverSmall` — **scope-dominance pin**: a prompt mentioning both a large-scope signal (`refactor`) and a small-scope mechanic (`rename`) classifies as large. Pins the LARGE-before-SMALL ordering.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptUnrelatedToAnyStem_defaultsToMedium` — **default regression pin**: ensures the unspecified-task default did not shift from medium to small (which would silently downgrade every neutral prompt).
- **Pre-existing test updated**: `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptContainsCarefullyUnrelatedToFull_doesNotClassifyAsLarge` previously asserted `"medium"` for the prompt `"Please carefully review this one-line typo fix in the README."`. That assertion was the state before the SMALL path existed; post-M50 the prompt mentions `"typo"` which is now the correct signal, so the assertion is updated to `"small"`. The test's original intent ("don't classify as large") is preserved — `"small"` still satisfies it, and `"small"` is semantically more correct because the tiny/fast tier was specifically sized for a typo-fix shape.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by commenting out the `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_REGEX.test(...)` branch in `inferTaskComplexity` and re-running `npm test` — exactly **8 expected failures** (7 new SMALL pins + the updated pre-existing typo test). Restored the fix, 226/226 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_KEYWORD_STEMS`, `SMALL_COMPLEXITY_REGEX`, SMALL branch in the cascade + explanatory comment block on ordering), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (9 tests added/updated).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims start routing inferred trivial prompts into the tiny/fast tier.

### M49: `model_not_found` route penalty reused `ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` (1h) despite being structurally longer-lived than a quota window — missing models were re-probed hourly, producing guaranteed 404s every cycle and polluting health telemetry `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` handler's `model_not_found` write path passed `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` (an alias for `ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` = 1h) to `buildRouteHealthEntry`. The two penalty classes have different decay semantics: `quota` expires on a refill clock (hourly windows are common upstream contracts), while `model_not_found` reflects a structural property of the provider — the upstream simply does not serve this model id. Reusing the quota duration meant the plugin re-probed the missing route every hour, got a guaranteed 404, wrote `retryCount++`, and reset `until` to `now + 1h` on the next failure. The retry telemetry accumulated meaningless 404-cycle noise and the downstream dead-route filters (`findHealthyRouteForFallback`, the `provider.models` active-route resolution) kept flipping this route from `healthy → penalized → healthy` on an hourly clock instead of quarantining it for a session-scale window.
- **Reachability**: fires immediately against any misspelled / deprecated / never-wired model id in `models.jsonc`, every openrouter router-synthesis failure (500 "Model not found"), and every direct-provider 404 — i.e. a commonly-reachable path, not a speculative edge case. The M43 preserve-longer invariant on `buildRouteHealthEntry` (route-level parity of M36) made it structurally safe to extend this one penalty class independently: a shorter quota penalty on the same route cannot shrink an active model_not_found window post-M43. Before M43 this change would have silently half-applied, so the window to land it opened only after M43 closed the merge invariant.
- **Fix**: introduced `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS = 6 * 60 * 60 * 1000` at module scope (6h — long enough to skip an interactive session's worth of retries without re-probing, short enough that a newly-deployed model the next morning gets picked up on the first attempt). Extracted a `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` thin wrapper over `buildRouteHealthEntry` that hardcodes the state + duration so future writers cannot drift the duration by copy-pasting a call site. Rewired the `session.error` handler to call the wrapper; removed the duration argument and the state literal from the call site. Exported both the constant and the wrapper so tests can pin the semantic invariant without constructing the full plugin.
- **Tests**: four new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS_isStrictlyLongerThan_ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` — **semantic invariant pin**. Fires if a future refactor collapses both constants to the same value, which would reopen the hourly-404-cycle bug even if the helper signature stays intact.
  - `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth_whenNoExistingEntry_returnsSixHourWindow` — **value pin** asserting `until - now === ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS`. Transitively covers the handler call site since it is a thin pass-through.
  - `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth_whenUnprefixedRegistryShape_composesIdempotentKey` — longcat-shape regression mirroring M30/M47, proving the wrapper inherits `composeRouteKey`'s idempotent behavior from `buildRouteHealthEntry` (so both raw and already-composite runtime ids land on the same canonical route key).
  - `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth_whenExistingPenaltyOutlivesNewWindow_preservesLongerPenalty` — **M43 preserve-longer parity regression pin**. Bumping this duration is only safe because the merge invariant holds; if a future refactor regresses preserve-longer, a shorter penalty on the same route would silently shrink an active model_not_found window and this test fires first.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS` back to `60 * 60 * 1000` and re-running `npm test` — exactly **1 expected failure** on the strict-greater semantic pin; the value pin still passes because it asserts against the constant itself (by design — the value pin guards "the wrapper uses this constant", the semantic pin guards "the constant is larger than quota", and the two failures compose). Restored the fix, 217/217 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `ROUTE_MODEL_NOT_FOUND_DURATION_MS` constant, exported `buildModelNotFoundRouteHealth` wrapper, updated handler call site + comment block), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (added 4 tests + extended the imports).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the longer backoff window.

### M48: `session.error` handler fired route-level `model_not_found` penalty on a bare `message.includes("model not found")` match, short-circuiting authoritative provider-level status codes (401/402/403/429) — dead keys and drained accounts were half-quarantined as per-route problems instead of provider-wide ones `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` handler in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (around the `isModelNotFound` check, line ~2076 pre-fix) read `const isModelNotFound = modelID !== undefined && message.includes("model not found");` and, on match, fired a **route-level** `model_not_found` penalty (`QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` = 1h on the composite `provider/model` key) and then `return`ed — completely bypassing `classifyProviderApiError(statusCode, message)`. Any API error whose body happened to contain the phrase short-circuited the authoritative status-code classification, regardless of what HTTP status the upstream returned. The priority-dominance rule that M35 established inside `classifyProviderApiError` (status codes win over keyword heuristics) was not applied at the event-handler path one level up.
- **Reachability**: fully reachable through any provider, proxy, or aggregator whose error bodies embed the requested model name in their auth/quota narratives. Concrete cases: (a) `401 "unauthorized: your key cannot access model not found in allowlist"` → should fire `key_dead` (provider-level, 2h) so every route through that dead key quarantines together; instead fired `model_not_found` (route-level, 1h), leaving sibling routes through the same dead provider burning retries and flipping the one penalized route back to "healthy" an hour later only to fail the same way. (b) `402 "insufficient credits: model not found in paid tier"` → should fire `no_credit` (2h provider); fired 1h route instead. (c) `403 "forbidden: ... model not found ..."` → same as 401 path. (d) `429 "rate limit exceeded: model not found in free quota window"` → **wrong scope entirely**: the provider is throttling, not the model, so all routes through that provider must back off; the route-level penalty left the sibling routes retrying and feeding the same rate-limit loop. The bug is the event-handler parallel of the M35 fix inside `classifyProviderApiError`, and once M35 raised the invariant explicitly it was structurally inevitable that this one-level-up path had the same shape.
- **Fix**: extracted a new pure helper `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound(statusCode, lowerMessage)` in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` that gates the keyword match on `MODEL_NOT_FOUND_HTTP_STATUS_CODES = Set([0, 404, 500])` — the only statuses that genuinely mean "this model does not exist at this provider" (0 = no authoritative signal available, 404 = HTTP-canonical not-found from direct providers, 500 = openrouter router synthesis). Authoritative status codes 401/402/403/429 are deliberately excluded so `classifyProviderApiError` downstream correctly routes them to `key_dead`/`no_credit`/`quota` at provider level. Rewired the `session.error` handler to call the new helper instead of the bare `message.includes`. The helper is pure, exported, and unit-testable without any live health maps or opencode runtime event payloads.
- **Tests**: nine new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` covering three accept cases, four priority-dominance regression pins, and two negative keyword-required pins:
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when404WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsTrue` — direct-provider HTTP-canonical path.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when500WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsTrue` — openrouter router-synthesis path.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_whenStatusIsZeroWithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsTrue` — proxy-stripped / network-error path.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when401WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsFalse` — **headline regression pin**: dead-key priority dominance.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when402WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsFalse` — drained-account priority dominance.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when403WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsFalse` — forbidden-key priority dominance.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when429WithModelNotFoundMessage_returnsFalse` — throttled-provider scope pin (wrong-scope bug).
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_whenStatusIs500WithUnrelatedMessage_returnsFalse` — keyword still required, bare 500 not penalized.
  - `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound_when404WithUnrelatedMessage_returnsFalse` — keyword still required, transient 404 not penalized.
- **Verification**: verify-on-HEAD by reverting `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound` to the old unconditional `return lowerMessage.includes(MODEL_NOT_FOUND_KEYWORD)` and re-running `npm test` — exactly **4 expected failures** on the four priority-dominance pins (401/402/403/429 cases), the three accept cases and two keyword-required cases all still pass. Restored the fix, 213/213 green, `tsc -p tsconfig.json` clean build.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (added `MODEL_NOT_FOUND_HTTP_STATUS_CODES`, `MODEL_NOT_FOUND_KEYWORD`, exported `shouldClassifyAsModelNotFound` helper, rewired `session.error` handler call site), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (added 9 tests + added import of the new helper).
- **Rebuild note**: `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` will need a rebuild on the next service start so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix.

### M47: `findRegistryEntryByModel` hand-rolled the runtime-vs-registry comparison in two fragile branches instead of sharing `composeRouteKey` — the four-way cartesian of {prefixed, unprefixed} × {runtime, registry} left one cell silently broken (already-composite runtime id matched against an unprefixed registry row) `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `findRegistryEntryByModel` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:333`) compared the runtime `{id, providerID}` against the registry `provider_order[].model` with two hand-rolled branches: `providerRoute.model === ${providerID}/${id}` (the "synthetic composite" path) OR `providerRoute.provider === providerID && providerRoute.model === id` (the defensive unprefixed-registry path). The four-way cartesian of input shapes — {runtime raw id, runtime already-composite} × {registry composite, registry unprefixed} — has ONE cell the helper did not cover: runtime already-composite (`id = "longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat"`) AND registry unprefixed (`model = "LongCat-Flash-Chat"`). The synthetic composite path double-prefixed to `"longcat/longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat"` (no match). The defensive branch compared `"LongCat-Flash-Chat" !== "longcat/LongCat-Flash-Chat"` (no match). Result: `undefined` returned for a valid entry, silently dropping both the capability-tier temperature override AND the `## Active model routing context` system-prompt injection for that session.
- **Reachability**: not currently triggered in the repo-default tree — opencode's runtime convention is that `Model.id` is the raw provider-relative id, not composite. But the failure shape is close to reachable: (a) any adjacent plugin's `provider.models` hook that rewrites the id to composite form puts the runtime side in the already-composite cell, and (b) longcat is the living example of an unprefixed registry row (three entries in `models.jsonc`: `LongCat-Flash-Chat`, `LongCat-Flash-Thinking`, `LongCat-Flash-Lite`). Same drift class as M30's health-map write/read asymmetry, which is exactly what `composeRouteKey` was extracted to absorb — but the M30 fix only landed on the health-map paths, not on `findRegistryEntryByModel`. The read-side gap is the M30 parallel.
- **Fix**: reuse `composeRouteKey` on BOTH sides of the comparison. Build the runtime composite key via `composeRouteKey({provider: model.providerID, model: model.id})` — the helper's `.startsWith(${provider}/)` guard makes it idempotent so an already-composite input passes through unchanged. Compare against `composeRouteKey(providerRoute)` for each registry route — same idempotent behavior for composite vs unprefixed registry rows. Both sides normalize to the same canonical key regardless of input shape, collapsing the four-way cartesian into a single uniform comparison. Removed the now-redundant defensive OR branch. Also exported the helper so the new tests can import it directly without going through `chat.params`.
- **Tests**: five new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`, one per cartesian cell plus a negative pin:
  - `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeIdIsRawAndRegistryIsComposite_returnsEntry` — common case (ollama-cloud/glm-5).
  - `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeIdIsRawAndRegistryIsUnprefixed_returnsEntry` — longcat-shape with raw runtime id.
  - `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeIdIsAlreadyCompositeAndRegistryIsUnprefixed_returnsEntry` — **headline regression**, the uniquely-broken cell.
  - `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeIdIsAlreadyCompositeAndRegistryIsComposite_returnsEntry` — already-composite runtime id against composite registry (previously covered by the defensive branch, must still match after removing it).
  - `findRegistryEntryByModel_whenRuntimeModelIsNotInRegistry_returnsUndefined` — negative pin that the reuse didn't accidentally become a catch-all.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by reverting the helper back to the two-branch hand-rolled comparison. Re-ran the suite: exactly **1 expected failure** (`_whenRuntimeIdIsAlreadyCompositeAndRegistryIsUnprefixed_returnsEntry`) — the uniquely-broken cell. The other three positive tests passed even under the old code (they land in one of the two covered branches), which is the correct contract: the headline test is the ONLY one pinning the drift closure, the other three defend against regressions in the now-shared helper. Restored the fix. Full test suite 204/204 pass. `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (share `composeRouteKey` + remove defensive branch + export; docstring updated), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (5 new tests + import).
- **Rebuild note**: lives in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` needs rebuilding for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the reuse on next service restart. Not critical today (the uniquely-broken cell is not reached by current runtime shapes), but closes the M30 drift gap before any future plugin rewrites model ids into composite form.

### M46: `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` task-filter substring direction was reversed, so the `best` branch of `recommendTaskModelRoute` filtered out every candidate on every realistic user prompt and silently fell through to the last-resort scan, bypassing tier + billing preference ranking `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:1713`) checked `entry.best_for.some((bf) => bf.toLowerCase().includes(lowerTask))` — asking "does the short best_for label contain the entire user prompt as a substring". `task` is passed by `recommendTaskModelRoute` as `task.description ?? task.prompt`, and `task.description` is usually undefined on opencode plugin invocations, so `lowerTask` is the full user prompt (tens to hundreds of words). `best_for` entries are short canonical tags ("coding", "refactor", "long_context"). The include direction was backwards: `"coding".includes("please investigate the streaming cancellation bug in our coding agent...")` is virtually always false. Same reversal on the `default_roles` OR branch.
- **Reachability**: live on every realistic `recommendTaskModelRoute` call. The `best` branch silently filtered out every candidate (`candidates.length === 0` → returns null) and control fell through to `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s last-resort scan (line ~1667) which picks the first healthy visible route from the first role-matched entry in insertion order — skipping `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`'s tier ordering AND its billing-mode preference AND its dead-sibling tie-break (M40/M41). The last-resort path still delivers a working route so the bug doesn't crash anything — it quietly downgrades routing quality on every real call. The existing happy-path tests only passed because one used a toy prompt (`"coding"`) that happened to be a substring of `"coding tasks"`, and the other unknowingly fell through to the last-resort scan (which returned the same single-entry route the test asserted). The comment in `_whenBestRegistryPathIsHit_returnsSinglePrefixedRoute` actually claims "the `best` branch truly runs" — but traced the code and the old direction means it did not. Two "regression tests" existed that could not distinguish a working filter from a non-filter.
- **Fix**: reversed the includes direction on both branches. `lowerTask.includes(bf.toLowerCase())` and `lowerTask.includes(r.toLowerCase())` — now asks "does the task prompt mention the label". Matches the normal direction for long-text-contains-short-token substring checks. Added a docstring block explaining the correct direction, the `task.description ?? task.prompt` caller contract, and why the old direction was effectively an always-false filter on real traffic.
- **Tests**: two new regression tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask_whenLongTaskPromptContainsBestForToken_keepsMatchingCandidate` — headline. A realistic multi-sentence prompt mentions `"coding"` once; the candidate's `best_for: ["coding", "refactor"]` must match and the candidate must be kept. Under the old direction `"coding"` cannot contain the full prompt and the candidate was dropped.
  - `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask_whenTaskPromptMentionsNoBestForTokenOrRole_returnsNull` — symmetric negative pin. A prompt that mentions neither any `best_for` token nor any `default_roles` token must return null so `recommendTaskModelRoute`'s last-resort scan gets to run cleanly. Prevents the reversed direction from quietly becoming a catch-all no-op filter.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by reverting the direction back to the old reversed version. Re-ran the suite: exactly **1 expected failure** (`_whenLongTaskPromptContainsBestForToken_keepsMatchingCandidate`) and the negative test still green (because under the old direction it was also null — via the filter-out-everything path instead of the specific-no-match path, but still null). Restored the fix. Full test suite 199/199 pass. `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (`selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` task filter + docstring), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (2 new tests).
- **Rebuild note**: lives in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` needs rebuilding for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the fix on next service restart. This is the widest-reach fix of the recent audit — every non-toy opencode session currently misses the `best` branch's tier/billing preference ranking.

### M45: `classifyProviderApiError` keyword fallback (statusCode=0 path) checked quota before no_credit/key_dead, so messages mixing "rate limit" with "insufficient credits" or "unauthorized" silently short-circuited to the 1h quota class — exact same failure mode the M35 HTTP-status priority fix addressed, latent at the keyword path `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `classifyProviderApiError` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:678`) had paid the M35 priority fix at the HTTP status branch — 402/401/403 now dominate over keyword heuristics — but the keyword fallback (statusCode=0 path) still ran quota → no_credit → key_dead. `"rate limit exceeded: insufficient credits on this account"` at statusCode=0 matched `"rate limit"` first and returned `"quota"` (1h penalty) instead of the correct `"no_credit"` (2h). The out-of-credit provider got retried an hour later, hit the same error, and the cycle repeated indefinitely — identical failure loop to the HTTP-402 case M35 fixed, just one code path over.
- **Reachability**: fully live. StatusCode is 0 whenever (a) the proxy strips the authoritative status and only forwards the body (cloudflare workers, some mitmproxy chains), (b) the provider returns a structured 500 body carrying the real failure in the message (observed on minimax-cn, occasionally on openrouter `:free` tiers), (c) the network error path surfaces with statusCode=0 and the provider's upstream error in the message. All three happen in dr-repo autopilot runs. Symmetric bug on the key_dead side: `"rate limit on unauthorized requests: token invalid"` at statusCode=0 returned quota instead of key_dead, so a dead key was retried every hour for the plugin's lifetime.
- **Fix**: reversed the keyword fallback order to longer-penalty-first: `no_credit → key_dead → quota`. Mirrors the intent of the HTTP-status branch (specific/severe signal wins over generic rate-limit narrative). Narrow by design — keyword sets aren't disjoint in practice because providers routinely wrap their real failure in a "rate limit exceeded" wrapper, so checking the specific buckets first is the only way to avoid the short-circuit. Docstring updated with the same rationale block as M35, explaining why the keyword path needs the symmetric priority treatment and enumerating the three statusCode=0 reachability scenarios.
- **Tests**: two new regression tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIsZeroAndMessageHasBothRateLimitAndInsufficientCredits_returnsNoCreditNotQuota` — headline regression. Message `"rate limit exceeded: insufficient credits on this account"`, statusCode 0, asserts `"no_credit"`.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIsZeroAndMessageHasBothRateLimitAndUnauthorized_returnsKeyDeadNotQuota` — symmetric key_dead case. Message `"rate limit on unauthorized requests: token invalid"`, asserts `"key_dead"`.
  - Existing `_whenStatusIsZeroAndQuotaKeyword_returnsQuotaFromFallback` test still passes unchanged (its message `"provider reported quota exhaustion"` doesn't match any no_credit/key_dead keyword, so it still lands in quota). Updated that test's comment to reflect the new priority order.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by reverting the order back to `quota → no_credit → key_dead`. Re-ran the plugin test file: exactly **2 expected failures** (both new regression tests) and every other test still green. Restored the fix. Full test suite 197/197 pass. `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (keyword fallback order + docstring), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (2 new tests + 1 comment update).
- **Rebuild note**: lives in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` needs rebuilding for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the fix on next service restart. Important for any deployment where a proxy is in the request path.

### M44: `chat.params` hang-timer callback recorded the timeout penalty without evicting the session's tuple from the three hang-detection maps, leaking ~150 bytes per silent-death session for the plugin process lifetime `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `setTimeout` callback in `chat.params` (armed for `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS + 100`, default ~15min) called `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` directly, wrote the result into `modelRouteHealthMap`, and `return`ed — never invoking `clearSessionHangState`. Both terminal cleanup paths (`session.error` and `assistant.message.completed`) DO call `clearSessionHangState`, so the happy and error paths are tidy. But for sessions that silently die (upstream network drop mid-stream, client Ctrl-C without a TERM handler, parent opencode crash that never fires `session.error`), NEITHER terminal handler runs — the hang-timer callback is the plugin's only cleanup signal, and it didn't clean. Per-session tuples (`sessionStartTimeMap` → number, `sessionActiveProviderMap` → string, `sessionActiveModelMap` → `{id, providerID}`) leak ~150 bytes per silent-death session for the plugin process lifetime.
- **Reachability**: live in the current tree. Dr-repo autopilot runs long-lived opencode processes across dozens of sequential sessions; every silently-killed upstream (iflowcn quota-cutoff mid-stream, minimax 5xx that closes the socket without a JSON error body, openrouter `:free` tier hang) leaves a permanent tuple. Not catastrophic per event, but fits the same "slow process-lifetime leak" pattern as M41's closure retention — both are invisible until a multi-hour autopilot run accumulates enough to show up as RSS drift.
- **Fix**: extracted `finalizeHungSessionState` pure wrapper at `src/plugins/model-registry.ts:836` that calls `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` and, on a non-null penalty result, ALSO calls `clearSessionHangState` before returning. On null (session already completed or still within budget) it leaves the maps untouched — preserves existing semantics for both no-op branches. Rewired the `chat.params` hang-timer callback to use the wrapper. No change to `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` itself — M41's closure-retention invariant (pure query helper, primitive inputs) is preserved. No change to `clearSessionHangState` — still a pure map-clearing helper usable from the terminal-event handlers.
- **Tests**: three new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `finalizeHungSessionState_whenSessionHung_clearsAllThreeSessionMapsAndReturnsPenalty` — headline regression. Full context (startTime past budget, active provider + model), calls finalize, asserts penalty returned AND all three session maps have `.has(sessionID) === false`.
  - `finalizeHungSessionState_whenSessionAlreadyCompleted_leavesMapsIntactAndReturnsNull` — startTime empty (terminal handler ran), asserts null return and provider/model maps with stale crumbs are NOT touched. Pins the no-op branch from accidentally clearing unrelated state.
  - `finalizeHungSessionState_whenDurationStillWithinBudget_leavesMapsIntactAndReturnsNull` — elapsed=10ms, budget=20ms, asserts null return and all three maps keep their entries. Pins the within-budget branch.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by temporarily replacing the `clearSessionHangState(...)` call in the wrapper with `void` statements. Re-ran the plugin test file: exactly **1 expected failure** (`_whenSessionHung_clearsAllThreeSessionMapsAndReturnsPenalty`) and the two no-op tests still green (correctly — they never hit the clear branch). Restored the fix. Full test suite 195/195 pass. `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (`finalizeHungSessionState` wrapper + `chat.params` callback rewire), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (3 new tests).
- **Rebuild note**: lives in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` needs rebuilding for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the leak fix on next service restart.

### M43: `buildRouteHealthEntry` unconditionally overwrote existing route-health `until`, missing the M36 "preserve longer penalty" invariant and leaving the same shrink-on-fresh-event bug latent at the route level `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `buildRouteHealthEntry` (`src/plugins/model-registry.ts:560`) built its returned health entry as `{ state, until: now + durationMs, retryCount: existing?.retryCount + 1 }` — unconditionally taking the NEW state and the NEW `until`, even when the existing entry's `until` was further in the future. Its provider-level twin `computeProviderHealthUpdate` (same file, line 486) has paid the M36 fix for this exact class of bug since 2026-03: if `existing.until > newUntil`, keep the existing state and until, only increment retryCount. The route-level helper had never been brought to parity.
- **Reachability**: latent in the current tree. All four route-health writers (`session.error` `model_not_found`, `assistant.message.completed` zero-token quota, `chat.params` immediate-timeout test branch, `chat.params` hang-timer via `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty`) currently pass the same `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS = 1h` duration, so no in-tree caller can construct a scenario where `existing.until > now + 1h`. But two paths were one config edit away from making it reachable: (a) another opencode process (dr-repo autopilot, letta-workspace shim) can write a longer-than-1h `until` to the shared `providerHealth.json` and our reader would load it — the next same-route event would silently shrink that longer penalty back to 1h, re-opening a known-bad route; (b) any future writer that differentiates duration by class (e.g. "real `model_not_found` gets 2h because the model genuinely doesn't exist") would immediately re-introduce the M36 bug — a later 1h `timeout` event on the same route would cut the 2h `model_not_found` penalty in half and revive the dead route an hour early. Same failure mode as the provider-level pre-M36 regression: fresh keyword-classified short penalty revives a longer authoritative one.
- **Fix**: ported the M36 preserve-the-longer branch into `buildRouteHealthEntry`. When `existing && existing.until > newUntil`, return `{ state: existing.state, until: existing.until, retryCount: existing.retryCount + 1 }` — same shape as the provider helper. `retryCount` still ticks so repeat failures remain visible in the health report regardless of which branch wins. Added a docstring block explaining the M36 parallel and why this fix matters before any future writer differentiates route durations.
- **Tests**: two new tests in `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenExistingUntilIsLongerThanNewUntil_preservesExistingStateAndUntil` — headline regression. Construct existing `{state:"model_not_found", until: now+2h, retryCount:3}`, fire a fresh 1h `timeout` event, assert the result keeps `"model_not_found"` + `until = existing.until` + `retryCount = 4`.
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenNewUntilIsLongerThanExisting_adoptsNewStateAndUntil` — complementary boundary: existing `{state:"timeout", until: now+10min}`, fresh 1h `quota` event → new `"quota"`/`now+1h`/`retryCount=2` wins. Pins the preserve branch from silently swallowing the common "later event extends the window" case.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by appending `&& false /* VERIFY-ON-HEAD */` to the preserve branch's `if`. Re-ran the plugin test file: exactly **1 expected failure** (the preserve-regression test) and the complementary boundary test still green (correctly so — that path takes the fall-through branch regardless). Restored the fix. Full relevant test suite 105/105 pass (22 `model-registry.test.ts` + 69 `plugins/model-registry.test.ts` + 14 `plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts`). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (preserve branch + docstring in `buildRouteHealthEntry`), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (2 new tests).
- **Rebuild note**: lives in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` — `dist/plugins/model-registry.js` needs rebuilding for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the invariant. Important **before** any future writer is added with a non-1h route duration, or a parallel opencode process pushes a longer `until` into the shared state file.

### M42: `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` preserved authored array order instead of sorting by `priority`, so every plugin `visibleRoutes[0]` "primary route" consumer silently trusted the config author to hand-sort `provider_order` correctly `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` in `src/model-registry.ts:352` returned the filtered slice in authored array order. Six call sites in `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` consume that result assuming ascending-priority order: `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport` treats `visibleRoutes[0]` as the entry's primary route (drives the `scope:"provider"` vs `scope:"route"` classification injected into the agent system prompt), the `provider.models` active-route resolution at line 1802 does the same, and the `findHealthyRouteForFallback` + `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` paths iterate with `.find` expecting the first healthy hit to be the highest-priority healthy hit. The `ProviderRoute` schema carries an explicit `priority: number` field precisely so authors can express ordering, but nothing in the pipeline enforced that the array order matched the priority field. `getPreferredVisibleProviderRoute` (in the same file, 65 lines down) was already paying a defensive `[...filter].sort((a,b)=>a.priority-b.priority)[0]` for exactly this reason — the helper just wasn't reused by the plugin's primary-route consumers.
- **Reachability**: latent in the current tree — every `models.jsonc` entry today happens to author `provider_order` in ascending-priority order, so the six consumers all Do The Right Thing by coincidence of config hygiene. But the invariant was entirely implicit: a single out-of-order edit to `config/models.jsonc` (e.g. appending a new route at the end of an existing array with a `priority` lower than its siblings) would silently poison the agent system prompt's "Active model routing context" section, flip `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`'s primary/secondary classification, and bias `findHealthyRouteForFallback` to a non-primary route for as long as the bad order lived. Classic foot-gun: the kind of bug that only manifests after a config refactor you'd never suspect could break the plugin.
- **Fix**: moved the priority sort into `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` itself. The helper now returns `[...visibleRoutes].sort((leftRoute, rightRoute) => leftRoute.priority - rightRoute.priority)`, making the invariant a property of the helper rather than a property-of-the-config that authors must preserve by hand. V8's `Array.prototype.sort` is stable since Node 12, so routes with identical priorities keep their authored order (no behavior change for tied priorities). Simplified `getPreferredVisibleProviderRoute` to `filterVisibleProviderRoutes(providerRoutes)[0]` since the defensive local sort is now redundant. Docstring on `filterVisibleProviderRoutes` updated to document the new contract and the six plugin call sites that depend on it.
- **Tests**: two new tests in `src/model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `filterVisibleProviderRoutes_whenInputArrayOrderDivergesFromPriority_returnsPrioritySorted` — pins the sort contract by feeding routes in reverse-priority order `[3, 1, 2]` and asserting the output is `[1, 2, 3]`.
  - `filterVisibleProviderRoutes_whenHiddenRoutesInterleavedWithOutOfOrderVisibleRoutes_sortsOnlyTheSurvivors` — stronger regression: interleaves hidden routes (togetherai, xai) with visible survivors whose authored order is REVERSED from priority, asserts the result contains only the survivors in ascending-priority order. Catches two related bugs in one pin: (a) naive implementations that preserve insertion order, and (b) alternate implementations that sort BEFORE filtering (which would leak hidden routes into the comparator).
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by temporarily reverting the `.sort(...)` call (returning `visibleRoutes` directly). Re-ran `npx tsx --test src/model-registry.test.ts`: exactly **2 expected failures** (both new tests), everything else green. Restored the fix. Full relevant test suite: 103/103 pass (22 `model-registry.test.ts` + 67 `plugins/model-registry.test.ts` + 14 `plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts`). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/model-registry.ts` (docstring + `.sort` step in `filterVisibleProviderRoutes`, simplified `getPreferredVisibleProviderRoute`), `src/model-registry.test.ts` (2 new tests).
- **Rebuild note**: the change lives in `src/model-registry.ts`, not the plugin file itself — `dist/model-registry.js` needs to be rebuilt for dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims to pick up the sort.

### M41: `chat.params` hang-timer `setTimeout` closure captured the full opencode `input` object, retaining per-request payloads (prompt body, tool list, message history) for up to 15 minutes per session `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the else-branch of `chat.params` (production path, `AICODER_ROUTE_HANG_TIMEOUT_MS ≥ 1000`) armed a `setTimeout` callback that referenced `input.sessionID` three times and otherwise closed over `input` transitively. `setTimeout` holds its callback until the timer fires or is cleared, and the callback's closure keeps alive every free variable — so the **entire opencode request payload** (prompt body, tool list, attached message history, injected system prompts, provider/model records) was pinned in closure state for `timeoutMs + 100` milliseconds, default `900_100 ms = 15 min`. `hangTimer.unref?.()` prevented the timer from blocking process exit but had **no effect on retention** — `unref()` only unblocks the event loop, it does not drop the closure reference. Under sustained load (e.g. dr-repo autopilot running 3+ concurrent sessions, each with 30 KB–2 MB of prompt+tool payload), this produced 45 KB–6 MB of per-session retention scaled by the 15-minute hang-timeout window. Long-running opencode plugin processes grew heap steadily until expirations caught up.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable in every normal `chat.params` invocation. The only escape hatches were (a) the `< 1000 ms` test-only branch (never taken in production), or (b) the session completing fast enough that `clearSessionHangState` ran while the closure was still in queue — but `clearSessionHangState` only clears the **session maps**, it does not clear the timer, so the timer still holds the closure until the 15-min deadline regardless of completion. Every session paid the full retention cost for 15 minutes after start.
- **Fix**: extracted pure exported `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty(sessionID, sessionStartTimeMap, sessionActiveProviderMap, sessionActiveModelMap, modelRouteHealthMap, timeoutMs, now)` at model-registry.ts:753 returning `{ routeKey, health } | null`. The helper takes only primitive `sessionID` (a string) plus references to the outer Maps — no `input` object anywhere in its signature. Rewired the `chat.params` hang-timer branch to capture two primitive locals (`capturedSessionID = input.sessionID`, `capturedTimeoutMs = timeoutMs`) and pass them to the helper; the closure no longer mentions `input` at all, so V8 can GC `input` (and its transitive references — prompts, tools, messages) as soon as `chat.params` returns. Hoisted the backoff durations from the plugin closure to module scope as `ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` / `PROVIDER_KEY_DEAD_DURATION_MS` / `PROVIDER_NO_CREDIT_DURATION_MS` so the pure helper can reference them; the closure now has aliases that re-export the module constants to keep the existing call sites unchanged.
- **Tests**: five new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_whenSessionAlreadyCompleted_returnsNull` — `clearSessionHangState` ran before the timer fired; late-firing timer must be a no-op.
  - `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_whenDurationWithinBudget_returnsNull` — duration **equal to** timeoutMs is within budget (boundary case, `>` not `>=`), preventing a photo-finish timer from poisoning a borderline-successful turn.
  - `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_whenProviderOrModelMissing_returnsNull` — session start-time present but provider/model maps were cleared; return null rather than guess.
  - `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_whenSessionHung_returnsTimeoutEntry` — headline happy path: hung session + full context → returns canonicalized composite route key, `state: "timeout"`, `retryCount` carried forward (incremented from 4 → 5), `until` in the future. Also doubles as a regression pin for M38 double-prefix avoidance (the helper delegates to `buildRouteHealthEntry` which routes through `composeRouteKey`).
  - `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty_closureDoesNotRetainFullInput_regressionPin` — compile-time shape assertion via `Parameters<typeof ...>`. If a future refactor re-introduces a rich `input` parameter the test stops compiling, forcing the author to re-review the retention story.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by temporarily inverting the duration check (`if (duration > timeoutMs) return null`) in the helper — a deliberate sign-flip. Ran the test file: exactly **2 expected failures** (`_whenDurationWithinBudget_returnsNull` and `_whenSessionHung_returnsTimeoutEntry`) and the other three green. Restored the fix. `timeout 180 npm test` full suite: **188/188 pass** (183 + 5 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new module-scope `ROUTE_QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS` et al + `evaluateSessionHangForTimeoutPenalty` helper + rewired `chat.params` hang-timer closure), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 5 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start — memory footprint of long-running opencode processes should drop noticeably after restart, especially on dr-repo autopilot where 3+ sessions × 15-min retention × 30 KB–2 MB payloads was the dominant steady-state contributor.

### M40: `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` comparator lost its route-health tiebreaker after the M29→M40 refactor, letting a dirty candidate beat an equivalently-healthy cleaner sibling `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: M40 refactored the ranking comparator from `aUnhealthyCount - bUnhealthyCount` (ascending, dead-count minimizing) to `bHealthyCount - aHealthyCount` (descending, live-count maximizing). That fixed one bug (a `1/1 dead` candidate beating a `2/5 dead` candidate because `1 < 2`) but silently lost a useful signal: when two candidates tie on healthy count, the old comparator still ranked the cleaner one higher via its unhealthy-count term, while the new comparator had no tiebreaker at all and fell through to billing preference / original insertion order. Concrete symptom: the pinned `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask skips routes to keyless providers` regression test failed because `unavailable-primary` (1 healthy `iflowcn` + 1 dead `missing-provider`) tied with `fallback-model` (1 healthy `iflowcn`) on healthy=1, then won on insertion order — the router picked the dirty entry even though the clean sibling was strictly better.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable any time two entries in the same capability tier have identical live-route counts — very common for small registries where most entries have 1–2 live `iflowcn`/`ollama-cloud` routes and some carry an extra openrouter fallback that is temporarily penalized. The dirty candidate would be selected and then immediately waste a retry on the dead sibling route before discovering the live one, doubling tail latency on every selection in the tied group.
- **Fix**: extracted `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth(entry, providerHealthMap, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` (model-registry.ts:692) which walks the visible routes once and returns `{ healthy, unhealthy }`. `countHealthyVisibleRoutes` now delegates to this helper (kept as a thin wrapper so existing callers/tests don't churn). Rewired the comparator in `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask` to call `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth` once per candidate, rank by `healthy` descending (primary), then `unhealthy` ascending (tiebreaker). Branchless, single-walk, unit-pure.
- **Tests**: three new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth_whenMixOfHealthyAndPenalized_returnsBothCounts` — pins the helper's pair-valued contract (provider-dead and route-dead both counted as unhealthy, both against separate routes).
  - `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth_whenAllRoutesHealthy_returnsZeroUnhealthy` — happy path.
  - `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask_whenHealthyCountsTie_prefersCandidateWithFewerDeadSiblings` — **headline tiebreaker regression**. Builds a dirty candidate (1 healthy + 1 provider-dead) and a clean candidate (1 healthy, no siblings), lists dirty first so stable-sort-only would leave it winning, and asserts the clean sibling wins. Plus the existing `src/plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts::selectBestModelForRoleAndTask skips routes to keyless providers` test now passes (was the canary).
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by temporarily reverting the tiebreaker line (`if (aHealth.unhealthy !== bHealth.unhealthy) return aHealth.unhealthy - bHealth.unhealthy;`) with a `// VERIFY-ON-HEAD` comment. Ran both test files: exactly **2 expected failures** — the new `_whenHealthyCountsTie_prefersCandidateWithFewerDeadSiblings` test AND the keyless-provider canary — and everything else green. Restored the fix. `timeout 180 npm test` full suite: **183/183 pass**. `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `summarizeVisibleRouteHealth` helper + `countHealthyVisibleRoutes` delegated to it + two-key comparator in `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 3 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M39: `session.error` classification cascade used `||` between status and keywords, letting an earlier-bucket keyword pre-empt a later-bucket authoritative status code `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `session.error` event handler classified provider errors with three parallel `(statusCode === X) || (KEYWORDS.some(...))` checks evaluated top-down in the order `quota → no_credit → key_dead`. Because `||` short-circuits on the first truthy branch, a **keyword match in an earlier bucket pre-empted an authoritative status code in a later bucket**. Two concrete regressions:
  - **HTTP 402 + `"rate limit exceeded: insufficient credits"`** → matched `"rate limit"` in the quota bucket, returned `quota` (1h), the provider was retried an hour early, the upstream returned the same 402, the loop repeated. Correct class: `no_credit` (2h).
  - **HTTP 401 + `"rate limit on unauthenticated requests"`** → same pattern. Returned `quota` (1h) instead of `key_dead` (2h). A dead API key was silently re-tried every hour forever because it never got the full key_dead quarantine. openrouter's 401 response format was a real victim here — several of its error paths pack status-plus-humanized-narrative together, and the narrative often mentions rate limiting.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable. Any provider that returns 401/402/403 with a body containing any of the four quota substrings (`"quota"`, `"rate limit"`, `"rate_limit"`, `"too many requests"`) — which are common in humanized error messages — was misclassified. The quota keywords are deliberately narrow, but the symmetric bug across all three status buckets makes it broad in practice.
- **Fix**: extracted pure exported `classifyProviderApiError(statusCode, lowerMessage)` (model-registry.ts:584) with explicit priority: (1) recognized HTTP status code wins authoritatively — `429 → quota`, `402 → no_credit`, `401/403 → key_dead`; (2) only fall back to keyword heuristics when no status is recognized; (3) return `"unclassified"` for truly ambiguous errors so the caller skips the penalty entirely. Hoisted `QUOTA_KEYWORDS`, `NO_CREDIT_KEYWORDS`, `KEY_DEAD_KEYWORDS`, `QUOTA_HTTP_STATUS_CODE`, `NO_CREDIT_HTTP_STATUS_CODE`, `KEY_DEAD_HTTP_STATUS_CODES` from the plugin closure to module scope so the pure helper can reference them. Rewired the `session.error` handler to call the classifier once and dispatch via a cheap `if/else if` instead of three redundant checks.
- **Tests**: eight new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `classifyProviderApiError_when402WithRateLimitKeyword_returnsNoCreditNotQuota` — headline regression.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_when401WithRateLimitKeyword_returnsKeyDeadNotQuota` — second regression.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_when403WithQuotaKeyword_returnsKeyDeadNotQuota` — symmetric 403 branch.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_when429WithNoCreditKeyword_returnsQuota` — pins that authoritative 429 dominates in the other direction too (billing-plan message shouldn't flip to no_credit).
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIsZeroAndQuotaKeyword_returnsQuotaFromFallback` — keyword fallback path works when status is absent (proxy stripped).
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIsZeroAndNoCreditKeyword_returnsNoCredit` — same for no_credit.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIsZeroAndUnrelatedMessage_returnsUnclassified` — critical invariant: random transient errors ("connection reset", bare 500s) must NOT quarantine a healthy provider.
  - `classifyProviderApiError_whenStatusIs500AndNoKeywords_returnsUnclassified` — explicit 500 non-recognition.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by stubbing the helper body to the old `||` cascade. Ran the test file: exactly **3 expected failures** (402, 401, and 403 with pre-empting keyword) and **5 passes** (429 case, fallback paths, unclassified paths — all uninvolved in the pre-emption bug). Restored the fix. 175/175 green (167 + 8 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (hoisted constants, new `classifyProviderApiError` helper, rewired session.error handler), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 8 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M38: the four `modelRouteHealthMap` write sites built naive `${providerID}/${modelID}` keys, producing unlookupable double-prefixed entries for already-composite model ids `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: writers of `modelRouteHealthMap` at four sites — `session.error` (`model_not_found` backoff), `assistant.message.completed` (zero-token quota), `chat.params` (immediate-timeout branch for test short timeouts), `chat.params` (setTimeout hang-timer branch) — all built the route key via the naive template literal `` `${providerID}/${model.id}` ``. Every **reader**, since M30, was already going through `composeRouteKey`, which short-circuits when `model` already starts with `${provider}/`. When opencode delivers a model id that is already composite (which is how non-openrouter providers like `ollama-cloud`, `openrouter`, and `iflowcn` routinely arrive — `model.id = "ollama-cloud/glm-5"`, `"openrouter/xiaomi/mimo-v2-pro"`), the naive write produced `"ollama-cloud/ollama-cloud/glm-5"` — a dead key no reader could ever find. The penalty persisted forever in the in-memory map AND in `providerHealth.json` as an un-findable zombie. The actual live route kept being advertised as healthy, the router re-selected it, the error re-fired, and the plugin wrote ANOTHER ghost entry. `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth` (M34), `findCuratedFallbackRoute`, `recommendTaskModelRoute`, `computeRegistryEntryHealthReport`, `selectBestModelForRoleAndTask`, and the system-prompt builders all silently lost visibility into these penalties.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable for any provider whose opencode `model.id` is composite. That's a very common shape: all `ollama-cloud/*` models (33 in the catalog), every `openrouter/<vendor>/<model>` route, `iflowcn/<model>` routes. The plain-id case (`longcat`'s `LongCat-Flash-Chat`) happened to work correctly by accident — the naive template matched `composeRouteKey`'s output for unprefixed ids — which is precisely why the bug never surfaced as a loud symptom: the routes that failed got the penalty silently dropped, the routes that happened to be plain-id persisted correctly, so the health tool looked partially populated and nothing screamed.
- **Fix**: extracted pure exported `buildRouteHealthEntry(providerID, modelID, state, durationMs, existing, now)` (model-registry.ts:505). It routes the key through `composeRouteKey`, which is idempotent on composite ids and additive on plain ones, and builds a `ModelRouteHealth` record with incremented retryCount. Returns `{ routeKey, health }` so the caller still performs the mutation — keeps the helper pure and unit-testable. Rewired all four write sites to call the helper, build the key once, and pass that key to both the `map.set` and the `map.get` used to look up `existing`. Now the **read-for-existing** and the **write-of-new** both canonicalize through `composeRouteKey`, eliminating the possibility of drift in either direction.
- **Tests**: five new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenModelIDIsAlreadyComposite_doesNotDoublePrefix` — headline regression for `"ollama-cloud/glm-5"`.
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenModelIDIsUnprefixedPlainId_addsProviderPrefix` — plain-id branch (longcat) still works.
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenOpenrouterDeliversAlreadyComposite_preservesSingleSlash` — pins `"openrouter/xiaomi/mimo-v2-pro"` (multi-segment vendor-qualified id).
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenReadBackViaComposeRouteKey_hitsSameKey` — explicit symmetry invariant: for both composite and plain ids, the write-side key equals the read-side key. This is the invariant the four call sites broke.
  - `buildRouteHealthEntry_whenExistingEntryHasRetryCount_incrementsIt` — repeat-failure observability preserved.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by stubbing the helper body back to the naive template literal (`` const routeKey = `${providerID}/${modelID}` ``). Ran the test file: exactly **3 expected failures** (the `doesNotDoublePrefix`, `preservesSingleSlash`, and the symmetry read-back tests) and **2 passes** (the plain-id case, which the naive template happens to handle correctly by coincidence, and the retryCount increment test which is key-agnostic). Restored the fix. 167/167 green (162 + 5 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Scope note**: intentionally did NOT also adopt the M36 "preserve longer-lived penalty" policy for route-level writes in this iteration. All four route-level writers currently use the same `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS = 1h`, so the downgrade bug is not reachable at route level today. Deferred to a future iteration for defensive symmetry if durations ever diverge.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `buildRouteHealthEntry` helper at ~505, rewired four write sites in the event handler and chat.params hooks), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 5 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M37: `loadPersistedProviderHealth` lost every live penalty when one persisted entry was corrupt, and accepted zombie entries with non-numeric `until` `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: two reachable bugs in one call site. (1) The per-entry loop body ran `health.until === "never" ? Infinity : (health.until as number)` and then `{ ...health, until }` — any `null` or non-object entry threw on `.until` access, the outer `try/catch` swallowed the exception, and **every** valid sibling entry was silently lost. A single corrupt row = full state wipe on plugin restart, meaning live `no_credit` / `key_missing` / `quota` backoffs vanished. (2) The `as number` cast was a static lie: if `until` was a corrupt string like `"forever"` or `NaN`, the `until <= now` comparison coerced or produced `false` (NaN comparisons always false), and the row loaded as an un-expirable **zombie** that never dropped out of either health map. A `NaN` provider-level `until` would permanently bench the provider until someone manually edited `providerHealth.json`. There was also no validation of `state` — an older plugin version writing an unknown union member would load it into the runtime map and break readers that rely on the union (`healthStateLabel` switch, fallback decision logic).
- **Reachability**: very reachable. The `providerHealth.json` file is shared across three opencode services (aicoder-opencode, dr-repo, letta-workspace) that each load the plugin independently, and the atomic-rename-writer only prevents partial writes — it does not prevent schema drift between plugin versions running concurrently. Manual edits are also common during debugging. A single stray `null` from any path (cancelled write, user editing, version skew) previously dumped the entire health map on the next restart, causing the plugin to immediately re-route to providers it had already learned were broken — the exact loop the health maps exist to prevent.
- **Fix**: extracted pure exported `parsePersistedHealthEntry(rawEntry, now)` (model-registry.ts:100). Validates shape (`typeof === "object"`, not `null`), `state` (runtime set `PROVIDER_HEALTH_STATES`), `until` (`"never"` → `Infinity`; finite number → keep; everything else → reject), expiry (`until <= now` → reject as already-expired), and `retryCount` (finite non-negative number). Returns `null` on any failure. `loadPersistedProviderHealth` rewired to iterate `Object.entries(parsed as Record<string, unknown>)` and `continue` on nulls instead of throwing. Parsed-root is itself typed as `unknown` and guarded — JSON files containing `null` or a top-level array no longer propagate further than the outer guard.
- **Tests**: eight new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenEntryIsWellFormed_returnsNormalizedRecord` — happy path.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenUntilIsNeverLiteral_normalizesToInfinity` — pins the `"never"` → `Infinity` contract the `key_missing` persistence path relies on.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenEntryIsNull_returnsNullWithoutThrowing` — the headline isolation regression.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenStateIsUnknown_returnsNull` — schema-drift rejection.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenUntilIsCorruptString_returnsNullInsteadOfZombie` — zombie prevention, string branch.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenUntilIsNaN_returnsNullInsteadOfZombie` — zombie prevention, NaN branch.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenUntilIsAlreadyInThePast_returnsNullAsExpired` — existing expiry semantics preserved.
  - `parsePersistedHealthEntry_whenRetryCountIsMissing_returnsNull` — no silent defaults for missing fields.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by stubbing the helper body with an unchecked cast matching the old inline loop logic (`const health = rawEntry as ProviderHealth & { until: number | "never" }; const until = health.until === "never" ? Infinity : (health.until as number); if (until <= now) return null; return { ...health, until };`). Ran the test file: exactly **5 failures** (null, unknown state, corrupt-string until, NaN until, missing retryCount) and **3 passes** (well-formed, "never" literal, already-expired — all cases the old code did handle correctly). Restored the fix. 162/162 green (154 + 8 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new `PROVIDER_HEALTH_STATES` runtime set, new `parsePersistedHealthEntry` helper, rewired `loadPersistedProviderHealth`), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 8 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M36: `recordProviderHealth` unconditionally overwrote existing provider penalty, downgrading longer lockouts `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `recordProviderHealth` (closure inside `ModelRegistryPlugin`) computed `newUntil = Date.now() + durationMs` and then `providerHealthMap.set(providerID, { state, until: newUntil, retryCount: prev+1 })` unconditionally. A 1h `quota` error against a provider already in a 2h `no_credit` penalty SHORTENED the lockout to 1h, causing premature retries on a provider the plugin already knew was broken for longer. Worse: `key_missing` state uses `until = Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY`; a subsequent finite `quota`/`timeout` penalty would silently downgrade the provider from "never retry — no key" to a 1h retry window, re-exposing the router to a guaranteed-fail credential.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable on any provider that receives a sequence of different error classes in one session — very common for multi-route providers like openrouter, iflowcn, ollama-cloud where opencode rotates between routes with varying error modes within the same minute. Especially dangerous for the `key_missing` → `quota` downgrade because `key_missing` is an explicit "do not try" signal set by `initializeProviderHealthState`.
- **Fix**: extracted pure exported `computeProviderHealthUpdate(existing, newState, newUntil)` helper (model-registry.ts:410). Returns the existing record (with bumped retryCount) when `existing.until > newUntil`, i.e. longer-lived penalty wins. Otherwise returns a fresh record. `recordProviderHealth` closure rewired to delegate. `Infinity > any finite` in JS handles the `key_missing` case without special-casing. Scope intentionally limited to provider-level; the three `modelRouteHealthMap` write sites all currently use the identical `QUOTA_BACKOFF_DURATION_MS = 1h`, so the same bug class isn't reachable at route level today (deferred as future defensive work).
- **Tests**: four new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `computeProviderHealthUpdate_whenExistingLongerPenalty_preservesExistingStateAndUntil` — 2h no_credit existing, 1h quota incoming, asserts no_credit + longer until preserved, retryCount bumped to 2. The headline regression.
  - `computeProviderHealthUpdate_whenKeyMissingInfinityExists_doesNotDowngradeToQuotaFinite` — `until=Infinity` existing, finite quota incoming, asserts state stays `key_missing`.
  - `computeProviderHealthUpdate_whenIncomingIsLonger_acceptsIncoming` — 1h quota existing, 2h no_credit incoming, asserts incoming is accepted (prevents over-correction).
  - `computeProviderHealthUpdate_whenNoExistingEntry_createsFreshRecord` — undefined existing, asserts fresh record with retryCount=1.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by stubbing the helper body to unconditional overwrite (`void existing; return { state: newState, until: newUntil, retryCount: (existing?.retryCount ?? 0) + 1 }`); exactly 2 tests failed (`whenExistingLongerPenalty`, `whenKeyMissingInfinityExists`), the incoming-is-longer and no-existing-entry tests still passed as expected, restored fix. 154/154 green (150 + 4 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new helper + recordProviderHealth rewire), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (import + 4 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M35: `inferTaskComplexity` used substring matching, flipping trivial tasks to large tier on false positives like `"carefully"` containing `"full"` `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `inferTaskComplexity` classified task complexity by `largeKeywords.some((kw) => lowerPrompt.includes(kw))` and the analogous medium check. `includes` is a raw substring match, so any prompt containing `"carefully"` matched `"full"` and was classified `large` → routed to the `strong`/`frontier` tier. Same false-positive pattern for other `-fully` adverbs (`beautifully`, `thoughtfully`, `prayerfully`, `respectfully`) and other inner substrings. A one-line typo fix phrased "please carefully review..." would burn frontier-tier compute. Reverse false positives in the medium list (`add` in `address`, `fix` in `prefix`, `test` in `latest`) flipped default-medium tasks to medium deterministically — less costly since medium is the default fallback anyway, but still wrong.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable. The function is called from `recommendTaskModelRoute` when `task.complexity` and `agent_metadata.routing_complexity` are both absent, which is the common case for ad-hoc tool calls and tests. Any prompt containing an `-fully` adverb (a very common English construction in polite requests) was misclassified as `large`.
- **Fix**: extracted `LARGE_COMPLEXITY_KEYWORD_STEMS`, `LARGE_COMPLEXITY_LITERAL_PHRASES` (for `end-to-end`, which has a non-word-char hyphen), and `MEDIUM_COMPLEXITY_KEYWORD_STEMS` to module-level constants. Built two precompiled `RegExp` instances with leading word boundaries only (`\b(?:stem1|stem2|...)`, escaping regex metacharacters). Leading-only (not trailing) deliberately, so inflections like `refactoring`, `systems`, `completed`, `updates` still match — a trailing boundary would silently miss common variants. `end-to-end` stays on a literal substring check because `-` is not a word char in JS regex. Default-medium fallback preserved.
- **Tests**: four new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptContainsCarefullyUnrelatedToFull_doesNotClassifyAsLarge` — the headline regression.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptContainsBeautifullyUnrelatedToFull_doesNotClassifyAsLarge` — word-boundary coverage for another `-fully` adverb. (Note: initial draft used `wonderful`/`successful`, but those words only contain `ful` with one L, not the literal 4-char `full`, so they are NOT substrings and do not actually exercise the bug. Replaced with `beautifully`, which does contain `full`.)
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptUsesRefactoringInflection_stillClassifiesAsLarge` — asserts the leading-only boundary still catches inflected forms.
  - `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptUsesEndToEndLiteralPhrase_classifiesAsLarge` — pins the hyphenated-phrase escape hatch.
  - Existing test `inferTaskComplexity_whenPromptSystemWorkIsNamed_returnsLarge` still passes: `"Rework the prompt system across..."` matches `\brework`, `\bsystem`, `\bacross` as whole-word starts.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by reverting the check to the `.includes()` substring form with the new constants; exactly 2 new tests failed (carefully, beautifully), the inflection and end-to-end tests still passed as expected, restored fix. 150/150 green (146 + 4 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (constants + regexes + inferTaskComplexity rewire), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (4 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M34: openrouter `provider.models` hook advertised route-level-dead models to opencode's router `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: the `provider.models` hook for openrouter (lines ~1357-1383) only consulted `providerHealthMap.get("openrouter")` — if the whole provider was blocked it returned `{}`, otherwise it returned every registry-enabled openrouter model id verbatim. It never consulted `modelRouteHealthMap`, so a SPECIFIC openrouter route carrying a route-level penalty (`model_not_found`, zero-token quota, hang `timeout`) was still advertised to opencode's router as available. The router would pick it, fail, the error handler would re-record the same penalty, and the loop would repeat on the next turn. Every other reader in the plugin (system prompts, agent tools, fallback selectors — M29/M30/M31/M32) already honored route-level health; the `provider.models` hook was the one remaining layer where the penalty was invisible, and it happens to be the layer where opencode actually routes traffic.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable. Path to hit: (1) openrouter provider is healthy (key live, no quota). (2) User has a registry entry whose `provider_order` points at `openrouter/<some-model>` and that model returns a 404 "model not found" (openrouter synthesized when a model was pulled upstream, or the model id shifted) OR returns zero tokens on both input/output (quota exhausted for that specific model). (3) `session.error` / `assistant.message.completed` writes `modelRouteHealthMap.set("openrouter/<some-model>", {state: "model_not_found", until: now + 1h, ...})`. (4) Next `provider.models` hook fire — the model id is still in the filter's allow set (because the hook never consults route health) and opencode advertises it as available again. (5) Agent asks opencode to route, opencode picks the dead route, fails, penalty re-recorded, loop.
- **Fix**: extracted a new exported pure helper `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth(providerModels, enabledRawModelIDs, providerID, modelRouteHealthMap, now)` that applies both the enabled-in-registry filter AND the route-health check in one pass, composing the route key via `composeRouteKey` for symmetry with the read-side convention. The `provider.models` hook now delegates to it instead of the inline `Object.fromEntries(Object.entries(...).filter(...))`. Provider-level penalty short-circuit (return `{}` when whole provider is blocked) is preserved upstream, so no behavioral change for that path.
- **Tests**: two new tests in `model-registry.test.ts`:
  - `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth_whenRawModelHasRouteLevelPenalty_isExcludedFromOpencodeModelMap` — seeds a map with one route-penalized model, one healthy free model, one never-enabled model; asserts only the healthy free model survives.
  - `filterProviderModelsByRouteHealth_whenRouteLevelPenaltyHasExpired_keepsModelAvailable` — seeds an already-expired entry (`until = now - 1`) and asserts the model is NOT filtered out, so the plugin doesn't race `expireHealthMaps` between sweeps.
- **Verification**: verified-on-HEAD by stubbing the helper body to the old enabled-only filter (with `void` placeholders for the unused params to silence warnings); exactly 1 test failed (the penalty-active case), the expired-penalty test correctly still passed since the stub is strictly more permissive. Restored fix. 146/146 green (144 + 2 new). `npm run build` clean.
- **Files**: `src/plugins/model-registry.ts` (new exported helper + hook rewire), `src/plugins/model-registry.test.ts` (2 new tests).
- **Rebuilt `dist/plugins/model-registry.js`** so dr-repo and letta-workspace overlay shims pick up the fix on next service start.

### M33: `initializeProviderHealthState` never reconciled stale `key_missing` entries when credentials reappeared `✅ COMPLETED`

Completion Notes (2026-04-11):
- **Bug observed**: `initializeProviderHealthState` iterated `knownProviders` with the guard `if (!providerHealthMap.has(providerID))` before running the `hasKey` check. Combined with `loadPersistedProviderHealth` restoring `key_missing` entries from disk with `until=Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` (the `"never"` serialization), the guard short-circuited whenever an entry was already restored — meaning a provider flagged `key_missing` in a prior session remained permanently blocked even after the user added a valid credential in `auth.json` or an env var. The only escape hatch was manually editing `providerHealth.json`. Likely the underlying cause of the user's completed task #9 (openrouter-key-renewal), where a renewed key did not take effect without a provider-health reset.
- **Reachability**: production-reachable. Path to hit: (1) user runs the plugin without credentials for provider X → `initializeProviderHealthState` flags it `key_missing` with `until=Infinity` → `persistProviderHealth` serializes it as `"until": "never"`. (2) User later adds a credential for X (auth.json edit, oauth token renewal, env var). (3) Plugin restart → `loadPersistedProviderHealth` restores the `key_missing` entry → `initializeProviderHealthState`'s early-exit skips the `hasKey` re-check → X stays `key_missing` forever. The first branch of the loop (`loadAuthKeys`) detected the new credential correctly, but the loop body never consulted it for already-present entries.
- **Fix**: split the loop into two branches. If `existing?.state === "key_missing"` and `hasKey` is now true, `providerHealthMap.delete(providerID)` + `hasChanges = true` + `continue` — reconciling the stale entry. Otherwise if no existing entry AND no key, mark `key_missing` as before. Other penalty states (`quota`, `timeout`, `model_not_found`) are left untouched — only `key_missing` is reconciled, because it is the only state that represents "absence of credential" rather than "provider-side failure under a live credential".
- **Test**: `initializeProviderHealthState_whenPersistedKeyMissingButCredentialNowPresent_reconcilesAwayStaleEntry` in `src/plugins/model-registry.keyless.test.ts`.
